بالقلوب؛ بل ذلك منهم دليل الإيمان وعبارة عنه. فيقبل قولهم في الأحكام الظاهرة بحق العبارة بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم به. وعلى ذلك عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم من المعارف وإن كانت لها حقائق غيرها. مع ما كان في الذي بيّنا دلالة ذلك. وكذلك الأمر المتوارث في التفصيل بين الكفار وبين المؤمنين بالأعلام وأنواع الزي، أو المخالطة مع الأهل، وإن لم يكن تلك بكفر ولا إسلام، فمثله أمر العبارة باللسان. وعلى هذا ما بينا من الآيات في العلم بالإيمان وأمر القلوب فيما جاء به النصوص، فمثله الذي نحن فيه. والله أعلم. وعلى ذلك أمر المكره على الكفر، وقول نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إنما يعبر عما في قلبه لسانه»؛ وعلى ما ذكرتُ أمر الإملاك والشهادات وأنواع المذاهب في الأديان بما علم ذلك بالأمور الظاهرة، فمثله حكم القبول. وقد تجد: الله أمر بأن يقاتل ليعطوا الجزية، وأن يجاروا إلى أن يسمعوا كلام الله. وفي ذلك التّرك بين المسلمين يتعيشون لينظروا في أمورهم ويتدبروا في أحكامهم فيعلموا بذلك حقائقها - وإن كان لا يُحتمل تأسيسها على ما فيها من تأليف القلوب ودفع التظالم وأنواع الفساد إلا بالله - ليطمئن قلوبهم بالإيمان وتحتمل أنفسهم الإجابة إلى الإسلام، فمثله في الذين أظهروا الإيمان بالله وأجابوا المؤمنين إلى ما عندهم من الأحكام. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
With hearts; rather that from them is a sign of faith and an expression of it. So their statement is accepted in apparent rulings by right of expression, since we have no way to true knowledge of it. And upon that, general matters among creation are carried according to what their capacity of knowledge can bear, even if they have other realities. Along with that which we have clarified of its indication. Similarly, the inherited practice of distinguishing between the disbeliever and the believer by signs and types of attire or mixing with family, even if that is not disbelief nor Islam, so similarly is the matter of verbal expression. And upon this, what we have clarified from the verses concerning knowledge of faith and the matter of hearts according to what the texts have brought, so similarly is that which we are in. And God knows best. And upon that is the matter of the one coerced into disbelief, and the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Indeed the tongue expresses what is in his heart'; and upon what I have mentioned concerning the matter of marriages and testimonies and various schools in religions by which it is known from apparent matters, so similarly is the ruling of acceptance. And you find that God commanded to fight so that they give the jizya, and to give asylum until they hear the word of God. And in that is leaving among Muslims to live together to look into their affairs and ponder their rulings so that they may know their realities thereby - even if their foundation is not possible except through God's bringing together of hearts and repelling oppression and types of corruption - so that their hearts may be reassured with faith and their souls may bear the response to Islam, so similarly is the case of those who have shown faith in God and responded to the believers with what they have of rulings. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument about the relationship between outward verbal confession and inner faith. Maturidi states that we judge people by their apparent statements because we have no direct access to their inner hearts. He supports this with examples from inherited practice (distinguishing believers by dress), the hadith that the tongue expresses the heart, and the rulings on marriage, testimony, and jizya. The key point is that in worldly matters, we accept outward declarations, even though true faith resides in the heart. This does not negate inner faith; rather, the outward is a sign of it.

Why Hypocrites Are Denied Forgiveness Despite Confession
Objection and answer: if verbal confession is accepted, why punish hypocrites?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reasoning behind why hypocrites, despite verbal confession, are not considered true believers and are denied eternal rewards.

Core Idea
Outward confession does not guarantee true faith or afterlife reward.

This passage presents an objection: if we accept verbal confession as sufficient for worldly rulings, why are hypocrites denied forgiveness? Imam Maturidi responds by distinguishing between outward acceptance and inner reality, showing that hypocrites do not truly worship, proving they lack genuine faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice how the objection is posed and the answer is given.
Focus on the logical structure: if... then... why not...?
2
Identify the objection
The opponent argues: if verbal confession alone is sufficient for faith in worldly rulings, then hypocrites who confess should also receive the promised rewards of the afterlife. Identify this conditional argument.
3
Understand Maturidi's answer
Imam Maturidi responds by pointing out that hypocrites do not truly worship in reality, nor do they attain virtue with God. Their outward confession does not earn them the afterlife rewards. This proves they are not true believers.
The key distinction is between apparent rulings (worldly) and true faith (which requires inner sincerity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: فإن كان ما يُقبل منهم من الإيمان في ظواهر الأحكام باللسان دليلاً على أنه هو خاصة. فلم حُرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم والثواب الجزيل؟ ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then it is said to them: If what is accepted from them of faith in the apparent rulings by the tongue is a proof that it is solely [verbal], then why are they denied by it forgiveness and what is promised for faith of eternal bliss and great reward? Then, because they are not entitled to worship in reality nor do they attain virtue with God, that is proof that they are not believers. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer unit. The opponent argues: if we accept verbal confession as sufficient for worldly rulings, then hypocrites who confess should also receive the rewards of faith. Maturidi answers that hypocrites do not actually worship in reality nor attain virtue, proving they are not true believers. Thus, verbal confession alone does not earn them the afterlife reward; it only affects worldly judgments.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That outward verbal confession of faith guarantees salvation and entrance into Paradise in the afterlife.
Correction: Hypocrites may confess verbally but are denied forgiveness and reward because their confession lacks inner sincerity and true worship, showing that genuine faith requires both inward conviction and outward action accepted by God.

Checkpoint

Outward Actions Determine Worldly Rulings
Maturidi cites verses to prove outward actions determine worldly rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses about fighting to argue that outward profession, not inner belief, is the basis for worldly rulings.

Core Idea
Outward actions, not hidden beliefs, determine how we are treated in this world.

Maturidi, in his Kitab al-Tawhid, provides a scriptural proof to counter those who argue that inner faith alone matters. He cites three clear Quranic commands to fight disbelievers and polytheists, but notes that the fighting is based on what they manifest, not what they conceal. This passage establishes a key principle: in worldly affairs, we judge by the apparent, while the heart's true state is known only to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the repeated Quranic citations.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses
Find the three verses from Surah Tawbah that Maturidi quotes. They all command fighting against disbelievers or polytheists.
The verses are: 9:123, 9:36, and 9:5.
3
Understand the key observation
Maturidi points out that the fighting is based on what people manifest outwardly (shirk and kufr), not on what they conceal in their hearts.
This is the central point: outward action triggers the ruling.
4
Follow the logical inference
If outward shirk triggers fighting, then outward faith (verbal confession) should end it. Maturidi argues that this is exactly what the Quran shows.
The heart's true state remains hidden, but we act on the apparent.
5
Reflect on the implication
This passage supports the view that verbal confession is sufficient for legal purposes in this world, even though true faith resides in the heart.
Connect this to broader discussions of faith and works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: قال الله عز وجل: ﴿قَاتِلُوا الَّذِينَ يَلُونَكُمْ مِنَ الْكُفَّارِ﴾ [التوبة: ١٢٣]، وقال: ﴿وَقَاتِلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ كَافَّةً﴾ [التوبة: ٣٦]، وقال: ﴿فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ﴾ [التوبة: ٥]؛ ويقاتل على ما يظهرون من الشرك والكفر دون ما يضمرون، ولم يجب بهذا أن لا يكون الشرك والكفر بالقلوب. فما يبعد أن يُؤمر بالقتال حتى يؤمنوا، ثم يُمنَع القتال إذا أظهروا الإيمان باللسان وإن كان حقيقة موضع الإيمان القلب، إذ لا يمنع هذا كونه فيه. والله الموفق.
Then it is said to them: God Almighty said: 'Fight those who are adjacent to you of the disbelievers' [9:123], and He said: 'And fight the polytheists all together' [9:36], and He said: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' [9:5]; and they are fought based on what they manifest of polytheism and disbelief, not what they conceal, and it does not follow from this that polytheism and disbelief are not in the hearts. So how far-fetched is it that he is commanded to fight until they believe, then fighting is prevented when they manifest faith by the tongue, even if the true locus of faith is the heart, since this does not prevent it from being in it. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof. Maturidi cites three Quranic verses that command fighting disbelievers and polytheists. He notes that the fighting is based on what they manifest outwardly, not on what they conceal. If fighting were based on inner disbelief, it would never stop because we cannot know hearts. But the Quran shows that when people outwardly profess faith, fighting ceases. Thus, outward profession is the basis for rulings, while inner faith remains in the heart. This supports the idea that verbal confession is a valid indicator.

Correction: Maturidi explicitly says fighting is based on outward manifestation, not inner concealment.

B) To show that fighting is based on outward manifestations

D) To argue against jihad

Key Takeaway
In this world, rulings are based on outward actions; the heart's true state is known only to Allah.

The Shahada: Legal Protection, Not Faith's Essence
Maturidi interprets the hadith on fighting until shahada to distinguish legal cause from faith reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi interprets the hadith on fighting until shahada to distinguish the legal function of testimony from the inner reality of faith.

Core Idea
The shahada spares life, but does not define the essence of faith.

Maturidi turns to a well-known prophetic hadith to reinforce his argument. This hadith is often cited to show that uttering the shahada is sufficient for worldly protection. But Maturidi draws a careful distinction: the shahada is a cause (sabab) for legal protection, not the inner reality (haqiqa) of faith. Understanding this distinction is key to his position on faith and actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice that the hadith mentions 'fighting until they say La ilaha illa Allah' and Maturidi's comment follows.
The Arabic is concise—reflect on its structure.
2
Identify the key claim
Maturidi says the two testimonies are a 'cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith.' What does this mean for the relationship between external utterance and inner belief?
3
Reflect on the distinction
Consider why this distinction matters for the broader debate about faith and works. If verbal confession only grants worldly security, what does it imply about the nature of faith?
This connects to Maturidi's view that faith is inner conviction (tasdiq), not mere utterance.
4
Connect to previous lessons
Recall earlier arguments about the definition of faith. This hadith supports the idea that the shahada suffices for legal rulings but does not define faith's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم في الخبر: أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله، وقيل: حتى يشهدوا، فيكون الشهادتان سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان. والله الموفق.
Then it is said to them concerning the report: 'I was commanded to fight people until they say: There is no god but God', and it was said: 'until they testify', so the two testimonies are a cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This is another proof from a prophetic hadith. The hadith commands fighting until people utter the shahada. When they do, their lives are spared. Maturidi emphasizes that the shahada is a legal cause (sabab) for protection from killing, not the reality (haqiqa) of faith itself. This supports the argument that verbal confession is sufficient for worldly rulings (like protection of life) but does not define true faith.

Rational Proof: Faith Is Assent of the Heart
Maturidi argues rationally that faith is inner assent, not verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational argument that faith (iman) is fundamentally an inner assent of the heart, not merely verbal expression.

Core Idea
Faith is inner assent, not just words — because it can't be coerced and must exist where speech is forbidden.

Maturidi presents a rational proof that iman (faith) is not merely a verbal confession but an inner state of the heart. He begins with the linguistic meaning of iman as tasdiq (assent) and argues that the reality of faith is located in the heart because it cannot be coerced by external forces. He then strengthens his argument with a practical example: during prayer, one is forbidden to speak, yet faith is required, proving that faith is an inner reality independent of speech. This lesson unpacks his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall argument.
2
Understand the linguistic foundation
Notice that Maturidi starts with the linguistic definition of iman as tasdiq (assent) and its implication.
3
Follow the argument against coercion
Maturidi argues that faith cannot be coerced, so its locus is the heart, where no creature has authority.
4
Analyze the prayer example
Maturidi gives a concrete case: in prayer, one cannot verbally profess faith, yet faith is essential. If faith were verbal, prayer would invalidate faith.
5
Draw the conclusion
Conclude that faith must be an inner state of the heart, not merely outward speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما العقل فلأنه دين، والأديان تعقد، وما به اعتقادات الأديان القلوب، وكذلك. مع ما كان الإيمان في اللغة التصديق، وحقيقته الذي لا يُحتمل القهر والجبر هو الذي في القلب، إذ لا يجري فيه سلطان أحد من الخلق. وجملة ذلك أنه يجوز أن لا يكون لسان، ولا يُحتمل رفع الدين الحق ولا الإيمان بالله والرسل من أحد؛ ثبت أن حق ذلك القلب. مع ما كان ذلك من المحال ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحن في حال الخطاب بحال وباللسان؛ فعامة الأوقات على الخلق تمر بدونه؛ بل من الأحوال أحوال يُنهى المرء فيه أن يقول: آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك، نحو الكون في الصلاة، فيصير الإيمان على هذا القول بحيث ينهى، ودين الإسلام بحيث يُفسد عبادته؛ والله جعله شرطا للجواز.
As for the intellect, because [faith] is a religion, and religions are contracted, and that by which the beliefs of religions are [held] is the hearts. And likewise, since faith in language is tasdiq (assent), and its reality, which cannot be coerced, is that which is in the heart, for no one has authority over it. In sum, it is possible that there be no tongue, and it is not conceivable that true religion or faith in God and the messengers be removed from anyone; therefore it is established that the true locus of that is the heart. Moreover, it is absurd for the act of faith to be absent from the one tested in the situation of address by the tongue; for most times pass without it; rather, there are states in which one is forbidden to say 'I believe in the books and prophets and the resurrection' and the like, such as being in prayer. Then, according to this view, faith would become something that is prohibited, and the religion of Islam would become something that invalidates one's worship; yet God made it a condition for validity.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof. Maturidi argues from the linguistic meaning of iman as tasdiq (assent) that its reality is in the heart because it cannot be coerced by any creature. He then argues that if faith were merely verbal, it would be impossible to have faith in situations where speech is prohibited, such as during prayer. But prayer requires faith, so faith must be an inner state. Therefore, the true locus of faith is the heart, not the tongue.

Key Terms
عقل
دين
تصديق
قلب
لسان
صلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That verbal expression is always possible and therefore sufficient for faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows that verbal expression is not always possible (e.g., in prayer) and that faith is an inner assent that cannot be coerced, so it must be in the heart.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say that faith cannot be merely verbal expression?
A) Because verbal expression is forbidden in prayer
B) Because the Quran says so
C) Because the Prophet said so
D) Because faith is a feeling

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates through reason that faith is an inner assent of the heart, not merely verbal confession, because it cannot be coerced and must remain valid even when speech is prohibited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you verbally declared something about your faith while your heart felt indifferent or doubtful? How does Maturidi's argument that faith is inner assent expose the gap between your words and your heart? What will you do to bring them into alignment starting today?
?
If you were placed in a situation where you could never speak about your faith again, would you be confident that your iman remains intact? What specific steps can you take now to strengthen the inner conviction of your heart so that it stands firm even when your tongue is silent?
?
This lesson teaches that faith cannot be coerced—no one can force genuine belief in your heart. Are there any areas in your life where you have been relying on external factors (e.g., routine, family pressure, social habit) to sustain your faith rather than a deep personal conviction? What would it cost you to replace that reliance with true inner tasdiq?

The Objection from Fighting Disbelievers and Maturidi's Reply
Maturidi answers the Karrami objection that outward fighting proves iman is verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that outward fighting against disbelievers targets their manifest shirk and kufr, not the inner reality of faith, and that verbal testimony is only a cause for protection, not the essence of iman.

Core Idea
Outward shirk is fought, not inner disbelief; confession protects life but does not equal faith.

The Karramiyya argued that because Muslims fight disbelievers until they confess, this shows iman is verbal. Maturidi responds by distinguishing between outward manifestation and inner reality, using Quranic verses and a key hadith to show that fighting is based on what is apparent, while faith resides in the heart. This lesson unpacks that critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Maturidi's Quranic response
Read the Arabic passage carefully, focusing on how Maturidi cites three Quranic verses commanding fighting against disbelievers and polytheists. Notice that he emphasizes fighting is based on what they manifest.
The verses are from Surah at-Tawba.
2
Identify the distinction between outward and inward
Maturidi argues that fighting does not prove that shirk and kufr are not in the hearts. Instead, it proves that the command to fight is tied to outward actions. Reflect on how this answers the Karrami objection.
3
Analyze the hadith argument
Maturidi cites the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah' to show that the shahada is a cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith. Compare this to the Quranic argument.
This reinforces that verbal confession does not define iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه [هو] خاصة . فلم حُرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم والثواب / الجزيل ؟ ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على [١٩٥] أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يقال لهم : قال الله عز وجل: قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار ﴾ [ التوبة ، ۱۲۳/۹] . وقال وقاتلوا المشركين كافة ﴾ [التوبة، ٣٦/٩] وقال: ﴿فاقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم [ التوبة ، ٥/٩] ؛ ويقاتل على ما يظهرون من الشرك والكفر دون ما يضمرون، ولم ﴾ يجب بهذا أن لا يكون الشرك والكفر بالقلوب. فما يبعد أن يُؤمر بالقتال حتى يؤمنوا، ثم يُمنَع القتال إذا أظهروا الإيمان باللسان وإن كان حقيقة موضع الإيمان" القلب، إذ لا يمنع هذا کونه فيه . والله الموفق. ثم يقال لهم في الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله»، وقيل: «حتى يشهدوا ، فيكون الشهادتان سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان. والله الموفق.
That [it] is specifically ... so why are they deprived through it of forgiveness and the promised eternal bliss and great reward for faith? Then because it is not permissible for them to worship in reality and they do not attain any virtue from Allah by it, this is proof that they are not believers. There is no power except with Allah. Then it is said to them: Allah Almighty said: 'Fight those who are adjacent to you of the disbelievers' [at-Tawba 123]. And He said: 'And fight the polytheists all together' [at-Tawba 36]. And He said: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' [at-Tawba 5]. And they are fought on account of what they manifest of shirk and kufr, not what they conceal, and this does not necessitate that shirk and kufr are not in the hearts. So what prevents that they are commanded to fight until they believe, then fighting is prevented when they manifest faith by the tongue even though the true place of faith is the heart? For this does not prevent that it [faith] is in it. And Allah is the Grantor of success. Then it is said to them concerning the hadith: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say "There is no god but Allah,"' and it is said: 'until they bear witness,' so the two testimonies are a cause of preventing killing, not the reality of faith. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The Karramiyya argue that if iman is only in the heart, why are disbelievers deprived of forgiveness and fought? Maturidi replies that they are punished for outward shirk and kufr, not for hidden disbelief. He cites Quranic verses commanding fighting against disbelievers and polytheists, explaining that the fighting is based on what they manifest, not what they conceal. The command to fight continues until they show faith by the tongue, but this does not negate that true faith resides in the heart. He also cites the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah,' showing that the verbal testimony is a cause for protection from killing, not the reality of iman. Thus, outward confession does not define the essence of faith.

كفر
شرك

شهادتان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Karramiyya believe that because Muslims fight disbelievers until they confess verbally, this proves that iman is purely verbal confession.
Correction: Maturidi shows that fighting is for outward shirk and kufr, and verbal confession is only a cause for protection, not the reality of faith.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of fighting disbelievers according to Maturidi's response?
A) To force them to have faith in the heart
B) To stop their outward shirk and kufr
C) To punish them for their inner disbelief
D) To make them utter the shahada only

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that fighting is based on manifest shirk, not inner disbelief, and that the shahada is a cause for protection, not the reality of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada, do you ever stop to examine whether your heart truly affirms it, or do you rely on the words alone to feel secure? What would you do if you found your heart was not fully attuned?
?
How often do you judge others' faith based on their outward actions—like prayers or attendance—while ignoring the state of your own inner conviction? In light of Maturidi's argument, what accountability does that place on you?
?
If your life were threatened for your faith, would your tongue confess while your heart trembled? Are you willing to ask Allah to purify your heart so that your words and inner reality are one?

Maturidi's Rational Proof that Faith is in the Heart
Maturidi argues rationally that iman is inner affirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational arguments for why true faith (iman) must be inner affirmation (tasdiq) in the heart, not merely verbal confession.

Core Idea
Faith is inner affirmation; the tongue can be coerced but the heart cannot.

Maturidi offers several rational proofs to show that iman is fundamentally a matter of the heart. He begins with the linguistic meaning of iman as tasdiq, then argues that what can be coerced cannot be true faith, and that there are situations where verbal confession is prohibited. This lesson unpacks his arguments and shows why the Karramiyya view is mistaken.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the flow of Maturidi's argument sink in before dissecting it.
Notice how Maturidi uses multiple rational proofs in sequence.
2
Identify the linguistic and rational basis
Maturidi starts by stating that iman is a religion and religions are held in hearts. Then he notes that linguistically iman means tasdiq, and its essence is what cannot be coerced. Find these points in the text.
The linguistic definition is key to his argument.
3
Examine the arguments from coercion and possibility
Maturidi argues that what can be coerced cannot be true faith, and that a person can exist without a tongue but not without faith in the heart. Reflect on why these points are rational proofs.
Coercion is impossible on the heart.
4
Consider the prayer argument
Maturidi points out that during prayer, one is prohibited from saying certain words of faith. If faith were verbal, prayer would prohibit faith, which is absurd. This refutes the Karramiyya.
This is a powerful reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما العقل فلأنه دين، والأديان تعقد ، وما به اعتقادات الأديان القلوب، وكذلك . مع ما كان الإيمان في اللغة التصديق، وحقيقته الذي لا يُحتمل القهر والجبر هو الذي في القلب، إذ لا يجري [فيه] سلطان أحد من الخلق. وجملة ذلك أنه يجوز أن لا يكون لسان، ولا يُحتمل رفع الدين الحق ولا الإيمان بالله والرسل من أحد؛ ثبت أن حق ذلك القلب. مع ما كان ذلك من المحال ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحن في حال الخطاب بحال وباللسان؛ [ف] عامة الأوقات على الخلق تمر بدونه ؛ بل من الأحوال أحوال يُنهى المرء فيه أن يقول : آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك، نحو الكون في الصلاة"، فيصير الإيمان على هذا القول بحيث ينهى، ودين الإسلام بحيث يُفسد عبادته ؛ والله جعله شرطا للجواز "، وجعله دائما لا يتغير ولا يتبدل ولا يجوز فيه النسخ . ثبت أنه على غير ما ظنت الكرامية . على [۱۹۰] أن الله تعالى أعلى درجة / الإيمان في القلوب حتى صيّرها أعلى الدرجات، وصيّر الإيمان مما يقوم به الخيرات، وعند وجوده يصلح العبادات ؛ وما يحتمل ما وصفت إنما هو القلوب لا الألسن، لذلك كانت أحق .
And as for the intellect, because it is a religion, and religions are held, and that by which the beliefs of religions are [held] is the hearts, and likewise. Since faith linguistically is tasdiq, and its reality which cannot be coerced or compelled is that which is in the heart, for no created being has authority over it. The sum of that is that it is possible that there be no tongue, and it is not permissible to remove the true religion nor faith in Allah and His messengers from anyone; so it is established that the reality of that is the heart. Moreover, it is impossible that the act of faith be absent from the tested person at the time of address by state and by tongue; [for] most times pass over creation without it [the tongue]; rather, among the states are states in which a person is prohibited from saying, 'I believe in the books, prophets, resurrection,' and the like, such as being in prayer. So according to this view, faith would be something that is prohibited, and the religion of Islam would be something that corrupts one's worship. And Allah made it a condition for validity, and made it perpetual, not changing, not altering, and not subject to abrogation. It is established that it is contrary to what the Karramiyya thought. Indeed, Allah Almighty made the degree of faith higher in the hearts, making them the highest degrees, and made faith something by which good deeds are performed, and upon its existence acts of worship are valid. And that which can bear what I have described is only the hearts, not the tongues. Therefore they are more deserving.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a rational argument. Maturidi begins by stating that iman is a religion, and religions are held in the hearts. Linguistically, iman means tasdiq (affirmation), and its reality is that which cannot be subjected to coercion or compulsion; this is what is in the heart, because no created being has authority over it. He argues that a person can exist without a tongue, but cannot be divested of the true religion or faith in Allah and His messengers from one's heart. Moreover, it is impossible for the act of faith to be absent from the tested person at the time of divine address, since most times people go through life without verbal expression. In fact, there are situations where a person is prohibited from saying 'I believe in the books, prophets, resurrection,' such as during prayer. If iman were verbal, then performing prayer would involve a prohibition of iman, which would corrupt worship. But Allah has made iman a condition for the validity of worship and made it perpetual and unchangeable. This is contrary to the Karramiyya view. Finally, Allah has placed iman in the hearts, making it the highest degree, and only hearts can bear the qualities described, not tongues.

قلب
لسان
كرامية
إكراه
صلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That iman is merely verbal confession.
Correction: Maturidi shows that iman is essentially inner affirmation (tasdiq) because it cannot be coerced and there are situations where verbal confession is prohibited, such as during prayer.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that iman cannot be merely verbal?
A) Because the tongue can be coerced
B) Because it is impossible to always speak
C) Because there are situations where speaking faith is prohibited
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
True faith (iman) is the heart's affirmation, not just verbal confession, as it alone is immune to coercion and consistent with Islamic practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe' with your tongue, do you ever feel a disconnect from what your heart truly holds? What is one area where your heart's affirmation does not match your words, and what will you do about it today?
?
This lesson teaches that true faith is secure in the heart and cannot be removed by any external force. Is your heart's faith strong enough that if you were forced to deny it verbally, you would remain firm? What can you do to strengthen that inner conviction starting this week?
?
The example of prayer shows that even worship can be corrupted if we prioritize speech over heart. In your own prayer, do you focus more on the words or on the inner presence of faith? What specific change will you make from your next prayer to ensure your heart is fully present?

Quranic Evidence that Iman is in the Heart
Maturidi uses Quranic verses to prove iman is in the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses to prove that the reality of faith resides in the heart, not the tongue.

Core Idea
Faith is in the heart because the tongue can be forced, but Allah forbids compulsion.

Maturidi presents a series of Quranic arguments to establish that iman is fundamentally an inner reality of the heart, not merely a verbal declaration. The passage begins by noting that faith is known through thought and reflection, which are heart-acts, then cites the verse 'No compulsion in religion' to exclude the tongue, and finally uses the Quran's own address to believers as evidence. Let's unpack these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi moves from one Quranic evidence to the next.
The passage is dense; multiple proofs are packed together.
2
Understand the first argument: faith known by thought and reflection
Maturidi states that the reality of faith is known through 'thought and reflection' (fikr and nazar), which are works of the heart. This sets the stage that faith is an inner act.
This is a foundational premise: iman is linked to intellectual acts of the heart.
3
Analyze the 'no compulsion' argument
The verse 'No compulsion in religion' is used to argue that faith cannot be in the tongue because the tongue can be coerced. If faith were merely verbal, it could be forced, contradicting the Quranic principle.
This is a key point: the tongue is like other instruments that can be compelled.
4
Examine the evidence from Quranic address
Maturidi notes that the Quran addresses believers as 'O you who believe' even when they are not uttering faith verbally. This shows that the reality of faith exists in them at that moment, which can only be in the heart.
The address includes all who have iman, regardless of current speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإن الخطاب بالإيمان يلزم بالعقول، ويُعرف حقيقة ما به الإيمان بالفكر والنظر وذلك عمل القلوب، فمثله الإيمان. مع ما كان الألسن قد تستعمل وتجبر كغيرها من الآلات ، والله تعالى يقول : لا إكراه في الدين ﴾ [البقرة، ٢٥٦/٢] ، فلم يجز أن يجعل حقيقته فيما فيه الإكراه. وقال الله تعالى: فمن يكفر بالطاغوت ويؤمن بالله ﴾ [البقرة، ٢٥٦/٢] وليس الكفر بالطاغوت باللسان خاصة، فمثله الإيمان ألا يُرى إلى قوله : ألم تر إلى الذين يزعمون إلى قوله : وقد أمروا أن يكفروا به ، فيصير الميل والتحاكم ترك للإيمان وإن أخبر عن لسانه أنه يزعم أنه مؤمن بالذي عليه الإيمان به والله الموفق. و في كتاب الله الخطاب بقوله : يا أيها الذين آمنوا في غير موضع " ، ثم لم يرتب أحد ممن ينسب إلى الإسلام والإيمان في ذلك أنه من تضمنه، وإن لم يكن هو وقت فرع الخطاب معه يستعمل لسانه في فعل الإيمان ثبت أن حقيقته التي بها سمّاهم بهذا قائمة فيهم وقت الخطاب، وهي لا تحتمل إلا أن تكون في القلب ولا قوة إلا بالله
Moreover, the address of faith is binding upon the intellects, and the reality of that by which faith [is] is known through thought and reflection, and that is the work of the hearts. So faith is similar. And since tongues may be used and coerced like other instruments, and Allah Almighty says: 'There is no compulsion in religion' [al-Baqara 256], it is not permissible to make its reality in that which involves compulsion. And Allah Almighty said: 'So whoever disbelieves in the taghut and believes in Allah' [al-Baqara 256], and disbelief in the taghut is not specifically by the tongue, so faith is similar. Do you not see His saying: 'Have you not seen those who claim' until His saying: 'and they have been commanded to disbelieve in it' [an-Nisa 60]? Thus inclination and arbitration become abandonment of faith even if he reports from his tongue that he claims to be a believer in that which he should have faith in. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And in the Book of Allah, the address 'O you who believe' occurs in numerous places, and no one who attributes himself to Islam and faith has doubted that it includes them, even if at the time of the address he is not using his tongue for the act of faith. So it is established that the reality by which He named them with this is existing in them at the time of the address, and it cannot be except in the heart. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage presents Quranic evidence. Maturidi first states that the address to faith is binding on the intellect, and the reality of faith is known through thought and reflection, which are works of the heart. Therefore, faith is akin to that. He then points out that tongues can be forced, but Allah says 'There is no compulsion in religion' (Quran 2:256), so it is not permissible to place the reality of faith in something that involves compulsion. He also cites the verse 'So whoever disbelieves in the taghut and believes in Allah' (Quran 2:256) and notes that disbelief in the taghut is not specifically by the tongue. Then he refers to the verse about those who claim faith but seek judgment from taghut (Quran 4:60), showing that inclining to taghut is abandonment of faith, even if the tongue claims otherwise. Finally, he notes that the Quran addresses believers as 'O you who believe' many times, and no one doubts that it includes them, even if at that moment they are not uttering the words of faith. This proves that the reality by which they are called believers is existing in them at the time of address, and it can only be in the heart.

يا أيها الذين آمنوا
طاغوت

نظر

Correction: Maturidi shows the address includes them even when not speaking, proving the reality of faith is in the heart.

Key Takeaway
The reality of faith is in the heart; the tongue is only an instrument that can be coerced, but true faith is a matter of inner conviction.

Faith is Not Forced: Refutation of Coercion
Maturidi uses Quranic verses to prove that faith cannot be coerced, thus it is in the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that faith is an internal conviction of the heart, not merely verbal confession, because it cannot be coerced.

Core Idea
Faith cannot be forced; it is a voluntary act of the heart.

Imam Maturidi grounds his argument on the Quranic prohibition of compulsion in religion. He argues that since faith is addressed to the intellect and requires thought and reflection—acts of the heart—it cannot be reduced to tongue speech, which can be coerced.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the argument. Then read the literal translation to understand each part.
The passage uses two Quranic verses as evidence.
2
Identify the logical premises
Maturidi builds his case in steps: faith is known by intellect -> intellect uses thought/reflection -> those are heart actions -> tongue can be coerced -> Quran forbids coercion -> therefore faith is not in the tongue.
Track how each premise leads to the conclusion.
3
Analyze the Quranic verses
Look at how each verse is used: 'No compulsion in religion' negates coercion, so faith cannot be in something subject to force. 'Whoever disbelieves in Taghut...' shows that disbelief is not merely verbal, so faith is similarly not verbal.
Both verses point to the internal nature of belief.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this matters: faith must be voluntary and personal. Coercion produces hypocrisy, not genuine belief.
This connects to broader themes of free will and accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإن الخطاب بالإيمان يلزم بالعقول، ويُعرف حقيقة ما به الإيمان بالفكر والنظر وذلك عمل القلوب، فمثله الإيمان. مع ما كان الألسن قد تستعمل وتجبر كغيرها من الآلات، والله تعالى يقول: لا إكراه في الدين، فلم يجز أن يجعل حقيقته فيما فيه الإكراه. وقال الله تعالى: فمن يكفر بالطاغوت ويؤمن بالله وليس الكفر بالطاغوت باللسان خاصة، فمثله الإيمان.
Furthermore, the address concerning faith is binding by intellects, and the reality of what faith is is known through thought and reflection, and that is the work of hearts, so similarly faith [is the work of hearts]. Especially since tongues may be used and coerced like other instruments, and Allah Almighty says: 'There is no compulsion in religion' (2:256), so it is not permissible that its reality be placed in that which involves coercion. And Allah Almighty says: 'Whoever disbelieves in Taghut and believes in Allah' (2:256) and disbelief in Taghut is not specifically by the tongue, so similarly is faith.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a proof that faith is in the heart, based on the impossibility of coercion. The author argues that the address of faith is understood by the intellect through thought and reflection, which are acts of the heart. Therefore, faith itself is an act of the heart. He supports this by noting that tongues can be coerced like other limbs, but Allah says 'There is no compulsion in religion,' so faith cannot be placed in something subject to coercion. He then cites the verse about disbelieving in Taghut and believing in Allah, arguing that disbelief in Taghut is not merely verbal, so similarly faith is not merely verbal.

العقل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is simply saying words with the tongue, regardless of inner belief.
Correction: The Quran's prohibition of compulsion shows that faith cannot be mere tongue speech because tongues can be forced; faith must be a voluntary internal conviction.

Checkpoint
How does the verse 'There is no compulsion in religion' support Maturidi's argument about faith?
A) It shows that faith can be forced by the tongue
B) It shows that faith cannot be coerced, so it must be in the heart
C) It shows that religion is not important
D) It shows that everyone must believe

Key Takeaway
Faith is an internal conviction of the heart, proven by the impossibility of coercion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The lesson teaches that faith cannot be forced; even your own habits can coerce you into empty ritual. What will you do today to ensure your prayer is a genuine act of your heart, not just a routine?
?
Have you ever verbally agreed with something Islamic (like affirming belief in the Oneness of Allah) in a social setting, while your heart felt doubt or indifference? The author says the tongue can be coerced, but faith is of the heart. What does that inconsistency reveal about the state of your faith? Will you confront it or ignore it?
?
The verse 'There is no compulsion in religion' is often cited as a proof of tolerance. But in your own life, are you subtly coercing yourself into religious practices out of guilt, fear, or peer pressure—rather than genuine conviction? If your faith is to be true, it must be chosen freely. What is one step you can take today to reclaim the voluntary love for Allah in your heart?

The Address 'O You Who Believe' Shows Faith in the Heart
Maturidi argues that Quranic address to believers implies faith is already in their hearts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Quranic address 'O you who believe' to prove that faith is a stable inner state in the heart, not merely a verbal act.

Core Idea
The Quranic address proves faith is in the heart, not just on the tongue.

In this brief but powerful passage, Imam Maturidi draws a simple logical inference from a recurring Quranic phrase. By examining how Allah addresses believers, he demonstrates that faith must already reside in their hearts even when they are not actively speaking. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how Maturidi uses the Quranic address as his starting point.
2
Follow the logical flow
Maturidi states: 1) Allah addresses believers in the Quran. 2) No Muslim doubts this includes them. 3) Even when they are not speaking the words of faith. 4) Therefore, the reality of faith is in the heart. Trace this reasoning.
The conclusion relies on the fact that the address applies even without tongue.
3
Understand the implication
This argument shows that faith is a stable inner state, not dependent on constant verbal affirmation. It refutes the idea that one must always be speaking faith to be a believer.
This connects to later discussions on the relationship between faith and action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و في كتاب الله الخطاب بقوله: يا أيها الذين آمنوا في غير موضع، ثم لم يرتب أحد ممن ينسب إلى الإسلام والإيمان في ذلك أنه من تضمنه، وإن لم يكن هو وقت فرع الخطاب معه يستعمل لسانه في فعل الإيمان ثبت أن حقيقته التي بها سمّاهم بهذا قائمة فيهم وقت الخطاب، وهي لا تحتمل إلا أن تكون في القلب ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And in the Book of Allah, the address by His saying: 'O you who believe' occurs in many places. Then no one who ascribes to Islam and faith ever doubts that they are included in it, even if at the time the address was directed to him he was not using his tongue in the act of faith. So it is established that the reality by which He named them with this name is present in them at the time of address, and it cannot be except in the heart. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quranic mode of address. Maturidi points out that Allah repeatedly says 'O you who believe' to people. No Muslim doubts that this address includes those who truly have faith. Yet at the moment the verse is recited, the listener may not be actively uttering words of faith with their tongue. Since the name 'believers' applies to them even when their tongue is silent, the reality of faith must be something in the heart, not dependent on constant verbal expression.

Key Terms
الخطاب
الإيمان
القلب
اللسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think one must constantly verbalize faith to be called a believer.
Correction: The Quranic address shows that faith is a stable inner state, not dependent on constant speech.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the Quranic address 'O you who believe'?
A) That the tongue is essential for faith
B) That faith can only be present when the tongue speaks
C) That faith is present in the heart even when the tongue is not speaking
D) That the address is only for the angels

Key Takeaway
The Quranic address 'O you who believe' establishes that faith is a reality in the heart, present even when the tongue is silent.

?
Today, commit to a specific practice that strengthens your inner faith, such as silent reflection on Allah's names or sincere repentance. What will you do to make your heart's faith more alive than your tongue's speech?

Faith is a Specific Act, Not All Acts of Obedience
Maturidi proves that faith is a specific act, not the aggregate of all good deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that faith is a specific act (heart's conviction) and not the sum of all acts of obedience, and how he uses Quranic rebukes to prove this.

Core Idea
Faith is a well-defined act, not the entire collection of good deeds.

Maturidi presents a nuanced argument distinguishing faith from general acts of obedience. He examines how the Quran addresses believers who fall short in obligations, showing that calling them 'believers' while they omit duties would be contradictory if faith meant all acts. This lesson unpacks his logical proof that faith is a specific, limited act — the conviction of the heart.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Let the structure of Maturidi's argument sink in before analyzing it.
Pay attention to the Quranic reference style: the author uses logic and Quranic address patterns.
2
Identify the key argument
Find Maturidi's central claim: faith is a name for a specific act, not all acts. Notice how he uses the Quran addressing believers despite their shortcomings to refute the alternative view.
The argument hinges on the idea that if faith meant all acts, then omitting an act would break the name 'believer'.
3
Reflect on implications
Think about why this matters for defining faith. This distinction shapes how we understand the relationship between faith and actions in Islamic theology.
Maturidi's conclusion reinforces that faith is primarily inner conviction, not a synonym for all good deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك إذ لا أحد التبس عليه تضمنه تلك الآيات ممن يصدق بالله وبرسوله؛ ثبت أن الإيمان اسم لمعروف الحد، وأن كلاً من ذلك لسانه قد يغفل عنه؛ فيبطل به قول من يقول: الإيمان اسم لجميع الطاعات مع ما وقع ذلك الخطاب على المتروك من الفرائض؛ فلو كان اسما للكل لكانوا يُخاطبون: «يا أيها الذين آمنوا ببعض الإيمان»، أو «آمنوا مع الثنيا فيه»؛ كما لا يصلح في مثل ذلك المعاتبة باسم الأبرار والمتقين، ثبت أن الإيمان اسم للخاص من العبادات لا للكل. ثم لا أحد منهم في وقت نزول الآية يُعرف منه استعمال اللسان بذلك، ثبت أن التسمية كانت لا به. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And likewise, since no one who believes in Allah and His Messenger is confused about the inclusion of those verses [the ones addressed to believers], it is established that faith is a name for a well-known limit, and that each of them, his tongue may be heedless of it. Thus nullified is the saying of those who say: faith is the name for all acts of obedience, especially since that address occurred concerning the abandoned obligations. For if it were the name for all, they would have been addressed: 'O you who believe with part of faith,' or 'believe with an exception in it.' Just as it is not appropriate in such a case to rebuke with the name of the pious and the righteous. So it is established that faith is a name for the specific act of worship, not for all. Then, not one of them at the time of the revelation of the verse is known to have used his tongue [to utter faith], so it is established that the naming was not by it. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a proof that faith is not equivalent to all acts of obedience, but is a specific, well-defined act (which is the conviction of the heart). Maturidi argues that the Quranic verses rebuking believers for failing to perform certain obligations (like jihad) would be contradictory if faith meant all acts, because then the believers would be lacking faith by their omission. But since they are still called 'believers', faith must be something less than the totality of good deeds. If faith were the sum of all acts, then those who omitted some would have to be called 'believers with part of faith' or 'believers with an exception', which is not how the Quran addresses them. Also, the rebuke is not directed at them as 'the pious' or 'the righteous', but as 'believers'. Therefore, faith is a specific act (i.e., inner conviction), not the whole set of acts. Furthermore, at the time of revelation, the companions were not constantly uttering faith with their tongues, so the naming of them as believers was not based on verbal utterance.

Key Terms
الحد
الطاعات
الفرائض
الأبرار
المتقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is equivalent to all acts of obedience, so performing good deeds increases faith and omission decreases it.
Correction: Maturidi shows that faith is a specific well-defined act (heart's conviction) distinct from external acts; believers can fail in obligations yet still be called believers.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi refute the idea that faith is the name for all acts of obedience?
A) By showing that believers are rebuked for neglecting some acts yet still called believers
B) By arguing that faith is only verbal
C) By saying that all acts are impossible to perform
D) By claiming that the Quran never addresses believers

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that faith is a specific act of the heart, not the entirety of obedience, by showing that Quranic rebukes would be inconsistent otherwise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you miss a prayer or fall short in a duty, do you feel that your faith has diminished? How does Maturidi's distinction between faith and deeds challenge your self-assessment? Will you today separate your conviction of heart from your list of achievements in worship?
?
The Quran calls you a believer despite your shortcomings. Does this comfort you or make you more fearful? What obligation have you been neglecting that you now realize you must attend to, not to prove your faith, but because the One who calls you 'believer' commands it?
?
If faith is a specific act of the heart, then its absence cannot be compensated by outward deeds. Have you ever relied on your good works to feel secure about your iman? What would it take for you to examine your heart's reliance on Allah rather than your own performance?

The Meaning of Irja' and the Hashwiyya's Suspension of Judgment
Maturidi explains the second interpretation and defines irja'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second interpretation of the hadith as suspending judgment on one's own faith, and the meaning of irja' as suspension and respite.

Core Idea
Irja' means suspending judgment, not only in politics but also in personal faith.

Maturidi examines a second interpretation of the hadith that condemns the Murji'ah. Here, the focus shifts from postponing judgment on others to suspending judgment on one's own status as a believer. The Hashwiyya, by using exceptions like 'if Allah wills,' exemplify this type of irja'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi defines irja' before giving the example.
The passage uses technical terms like الإرجاء and الاستثناء.
2
Identify the definition of irja'
Find the sentence that defines irja' as suspension in answering and granting respite. Also note the rational clarification that it is suspension in a matter that is their action.
3
Reflect on the Hashwiyya's practice
Consider how the Hashwiyya suspend judgment by not definitively calling themselves believers but using exceptions. Ask yourself why this is considered irja'.
Maturidi mentions that some reports about worldly life being irja' are not sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني أن يكون ذلك فيها عليه حال الفاعل في فعله من الوقف في ذلك، نحو ما قالت الحشوية في اسم المؤمن والدُّنْيا فيه. ومعلوم أن الإرجاء هو الوقف في الجواب والإمهال للنظر. ثم لا يقطعون في أنفسهم القول بالإيمان بل يستثنون، والدُّنْيا إرجاء، وقد ذكر ذلك في بعض الأخبار، لكن لا يشهد بصحته. وفي العقل بيان معنى الإرجاء، إذ هو الوقف في الأمر في أمر هو فعلهم. وما قالت المعتزلة في إرجاء صاحب الكبيرة بالتسمية أنه مؤمن أو كافر. مع ما قسم الخلق الذين امتحنوا قسمين في التحقيق مؤمن وكافر، وصيّر القسم الثالث المنافق؛ إذ هو مع هؤلاء في الظاهر، ومع هؤلاء في السر، فاستوجب أحكام أهل الإيمان في الظاهر مما عليه أهل الأديان في الدنيا، واستوجب في الباطن الأحكام مما عليه أمر الكفر في الظاهر، من أمر الآخرة. والله الموفق.
And the second interpretation: that this [condemnation] concerns the one who suspends judgment in his action, like what the Hashwiyya said concerning the name of the believer and the worldly life therein. And it is known that al-irja' is suspension in answering and granting respite for consideration. Then they do not definitively state the word of faith but rather make exceptions (yastathnun), and the worldly life is an irja'. That has been mentioned in some reports, but it is not attested as sound. And in reason is the clarification of the meaning of al-irja', for it is suspension in a matter that is their action. And what the Mu'tazila said concerning the irja' of the committer of a major sin by labeling him as believer or disbeliever. Along with the fact that He divided the creation who were tested into two categories in reality: believer and disbeliever, and made the third category the hypocrite; for he is with these outwardly and with those secretly, so he receives the rulings of the people of faith outwardly, according to what the people of religion [follow] in this world, and he receives inwardly the rulings of the matter of disbelief outwardly, concerning the matter of the Hereafter. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage presents the second interpretation of the hadith condemning the Murji'ah. Maturidi explains that the condemnation may apply to those who suspend judgment regarding their own action — for example, the Hashwiyya who refrain from definitively calling themselves believers, instead using exceptions like 'if Allah wills'. This suspension is irja'. He notes that such reports exist but are not sound. He then clarifies that rationally, irja' means suspending judgment on one's own actions. He compares this to the Mu'tazila who suspend judgment on the committer of a major sin by not labeling him believer or disbeliever. Finally, he discusses the three categories of people: believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites, who receive the outward rulings of believers but inward punishment of disbelievers. This shows that irja' in the sense of suspension is relevant to the hypocrite's status.

Key Terms
الإرجاء
الوقف
الاستثناء
الحشوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Irja' only means postponing political judgment.
Correction: Maturidi shows it also means suspending judgment on one's own faith, as the Hashwiyya do.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the meaning of al-irja'?
A) Postponing punishment for sins
B) Suspension in answering and granting respite
C) Excommunicating a believer
D) Predestination of actions

Key Takeaway
Irja' includes suspending judgment on one's own faith, not only on political matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a believer, if Allah wills,' do you mean it as humility or as a cover for uncertainty? What would it mean for you to declare your faith without that exception?
?
Maturidi says irja' is 'granting respite for consideration.' Are you still considering whether to fully commit to your faith, or have you already decided? What is holding you back from affirming it definitively?
?
How does your hesitation to judge your own faith mirror the Hashwiyya's suspension? What step will you take today to move from suspension to certainty?

The Mu'tazila and the Three Categories of Faith
Maturidi discusses the Mu'tazila and the three categories of people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's position on the committer of a major sin and the three categories of people: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite.

Core Idea
The hypocrite is a third category, outwardly faithful but inwardly disbelieving.

Maturidi continues discussing the second interpretation by addressing the Mu'tazila, who suspend judgment on the status of a grave sinner. He then presents the division of people into three categories, highlighting the unique position of the hypocrite who receives outward rulings of faith but inward punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

2
Identify the Mu'tazila's view

This is another example of irja'.
3
Analyze the three categories
Maturidi lists three categories: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite. Understand the hypocrite's dual status: outwardly with believers, inwardly with disbelievers.
The hypocrite receives worldly rulings of faith but Hereafter punishment.

The Creation of Faith: Known Therefore Created
Maturidi argues that faith must be created because it is known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that faith must be created because it is known, and how this refutes the Hashwiyya.

Core Idea
Faith is known, therefore it is created.

Maturidi engages with a group called al-Hashwiyya who deny the creation of faith. He constructs a logical argument: faith is either known or unknown. If unknown, it cannot be known; but since faith is known through revelation and proof, it must be created. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source text and its literal translation to grasp the flow of Maturidi's argument.
Pay attention to the conditional structure 'either known or unknown'.
2
Identify the conditional argument
Notice that Maturidi presents a dichotomy: faith is either known or unknown. He then examines the implications of each possibility.
This is a classic logical division (taqsim).
3
Understand the 'unknown' case
If faith were unknown, it would be like any other creation that cannot be known through proof. This would make the denial of creation meaningless.
Maturidi uses the example of 'what is witnessed' (shahid) to argue that everything besides Allah is created.
4
Understand the 'known' case
Since faith is known (through revelation and proofs), it must be created, because only Allah is uncreated and known without need of proof.
The command to have faith in all scriptures confirms its known status.
5
Reflect on the refutation of the Hashwiyya
Consider how this argument directly counters the Hashwiyya position that faith is not created.
The Hashwiyya claimed faith is uncreated, but Maturidi shows that knowledge of faith entails its creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[خلق الإيمان] ثم القول في خلق الإيمان فيما بيننا وبين فريق من الحشوية - مع ما قد بينا القول في خلق أفعال العباد ما يكفى ذلك من تأمل أمر الإيمان - أن الإيمان لا يخلو من أن يكون معروفًا أو مجهولاً. فإن كان مجهولاً لا يعلمه أحد، فنقول: من يقول بنفي الخلق لا معنى له، لأن الذي يجهله حتى لا يصل إلى العلم به من طريق الدليل هو الخلق الذي لم يجعل الله فيما يشهده دليلاً عليه يعرف مائيته وحقيقته، وذلك خلق في جملة القول؛ وبدلالة المحسوس على أن كل شيء سوى الله خلق، كائن بعد أن لم يكن. فأما الله تعالى وما يوصف به ففي الشاهد دليل على التحقيق والإثبات، فلا وجه للجهل به وفي ذلك تثبيت جعله خلقا. مع ما لا يجوز الجهل به؛ إذ الأمر بفعله عن الله في جميع كتبه المنزلة وعلى لسان رسله
[The creation of faith] Then the statement concerning the creation of faith between us and a group of the Hashwiyya — with what we have already stated concerning the creation of the actions of servants, which suffices for one who reflects on the matter of faith — is that faith cannot but be either known or unknown. If it is unknown, no one knows it, then we say: one who denies creation has no meaning, because that which is unknown to the extent that one cannot attain knowledge of it through proof is the creation that Allah did not place in what is witnessed a proof for it by which its essence and reality are known, and that is a created thing in summary; and by the indication of the sensible that everything other than Allah is a created thing, coming into existence after not having existed. As for Allah, exalted, and what is described by Him, in the witnessed there is a proof for verification and affirmation, so there is no occasion for ignorance of it, and in that is a confirmation of making it created. Along with what it is not permissible to be ignorant of; for the command to act upon it from Allah is in all His revealed books and on the tongues of His messengers.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the creation of faith (khalq al-iman). Maturidi begins by framing the discussion between his school and a group called al-Hashwiyya. He says that faith must be either known or unknown. If it were unknown, no one would know it, and then denying its creation would be meaningless because an unknown thing would be like any other creation that lacks a proof in the sensible world — and by the evidence of the senses, everything other than Allah is created. Therefore, if faith is known — as it is through revelation and proofs — it must be created, because only Allah is uncreated. Moreover, since Allah commands faith in all scriptures, it cannot be unknown. Thus, faith is a created entity known through divine command.

Key Terms
خلق الإيمان
الحشوية
مائية
حقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if faith is from Allah, it cannot be created.
Correction: Maturidi argues that everything known besides Allah is created, and faith is known; therefore faith is created.

Checkpoint
What is Maturidi's main argument for the creation of faith?
A) Faith is an action of humans, hence created
B) Faith is known through revelation, and everything known besides Allah is created
C) The Qur'an explicitly states that faith is created
D) The Hashwiyya deny creation, so it must be affirmed

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that faith is created because it is known through revelation, and everything known besides Allah is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is a created thing known through revelation, not through your fluctuating emotions, how will you hold yourself accountable to Allah's command to believe even when you feel doubt?
?
Maturidi says everything known besides Allah is created. What does this mean for your pride in knowledge? Will you humble yourself by acknowledging that even your certainty is a created gift from Allah?
?
Since faith is known through divine command in all scriptures and messengers, are you actually obeying that command, or have you replaced it with a comfortable feeling you call 'faith'?

Proof That Iman Is Created: Quranic Evidence
Maturidi argues that iman is created by citing verses on actions and inner states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses Quranic verses to prove that iman (faith) is created, and why inner actions of the heart are included in creation.

Core Idea
Quran proves iman is created because it is an action, and Allah creates all actions.

Imam Maturidi presents a concise proof for the creation of iman by linking it to actions (a'mal) and citing key verses. This lesson walks through his argument, showing how inner speech and conscience are also part of Allah's creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the author's use of Quranic verses as evidence.
2
Identify the main claim and verses cited
The claim is that iman is created. Find the two primary verses (37:96 and 67:13-14) and the supporting verse (25:59).
3
Understand how actions include inner states
The author argues that iman is 'speech and action of the conscience' not just physical. See how verse 67:13-14 is used to show Allah's knowledge of inner acts.
This counters the misconception that only outward acts are created.
4
See the extension to all creation
The author uses verse 25:59 to include iman in 'what is between the heavens and the earth', reinforcing that all things, including iman, are created.
This completes the proof by generalizing to all creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالله، فيجب به القول بخلقه ؛ أو القول بخلقه بما هو من الأعمال، وقد قال الله تعالى : والله خلقكم وما تعملون ﴾ [الصافات، ٩٦/٣٧]. إنه بحق القول وفعل الضمير دون غيرهما من الجوارح، وقد قال الله تعالى وأسروا قولكم أو اجهروا به إنه عليم بذات الصدور ألا يعلم من خلق وهو اللطيف الخبير ﴾ [الملك ، ١٣/٦٧-١٤] ، فهو داخل في جملة الشيئية بالأول، وفي جملة الأعمال في الثاني، وفي جملة ما نُسرّ ونَجهر . مع ما قد يكون في السموات والأرض مما لا إشارة إلى خلقه باسمه داخل ذلك فيما بينا، [كما] في قوله: الذي خلق السموات والأرض وما بينهما ﴾ [الفرقان ٥٩/٢٥] ، فمثله الإيمان من الذي بينهما . والله الموفق.
Then Allah, so it is necessary to say that it is created; or to say that it is created because it is of deeds, and Allah Most High said: 'And Allah created you and what you do' (Quran 37:96). It is truly speech and the action of the conscience without other limbs, and Allah Most High said: 'And conceal your speech or proclaim it, indeed He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, and He is the Subtle, the Aware' (Quran 67:13-14). So it is included in the category of thing-ness in the first, and in the category of deeds in the second, and in the category of what we conceal and proclaim. Along with what may be in the heavens and the earth of which there is no indication of its creation by name included in what we have explained, as in His saying: 'Who created the heavens and the earth and what is between them' (Quran 25:59). So like that is iman from what is between them. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that iman (faith) is created (makhluq) by drawing on Quranic verses. The author begins by stating that it is necessary to affirm the creation of iman, either directly or because it belongs to the category of actions (a'mal). He cites Surah al-Saffat (37:96): 'And Allah created you and what you do,' establishing that human actions are created by Allah. He then argues that iman includes inner speech (qawl) and the act of the conscience (fi'l al-damir), not just physical limbs, referencing Surah al-Mulk (67:13-14) where Allah knows both hidden and open speech, and asks rhetorically if He who creates does not know. This shows that inner acts are also known and thus included in creation. He further notes that iman falls under 'thing-ness' (shay'iyya) in the first verse, under 'deeds' (a'mal) in the second, and under what we conceal and proclaim. He extends the argument to include all things in the heavens and earth that are not explicitly named as created but are included in the general creation, as in Surah al-Furqan (25:59) where Allah created what is between them. Thus, iman, being among those things, is also created.

Key Terms

الخلق
الأعمال
فعل الضمير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Inner acts of the heart are not created by Allah.
Correction: The passage shows that inner speech and conscience are created, as Allah knows them and asks if He who creates does not know (Quran 67:13-14).

Checkpoint
Which verse does the author primarily use to argue that actions are created?
A) Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14
B) Surah al-Saffat 37:96
C) Surah al-Furqan 25:59
D) Surah al-Hujurat 49:7

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi proves that iman is created by establishing that it is an action and that all actions, including inner ones, are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your iman is created by Allah every moment, do you truly see it as a gift from Him that you should constantly be grateful for? How does this affect your prayer and reliance on Him to sustain your faith?
?
You now know that even your most private inner beliefs are created and known by Allah. Does that awareness make you more conscious of what you allow to dwell in your heart? What will you do this week to purify your inner state knowing it is being created and seen?
?
The proof shows that you cannot take credit for your own iman – it is Allah’s creation. Does this humble you or make you fearful? Are you willing to acknowledge that without His continuous creation of faith in your heart, you would have nothing? How will you respond to Him for every moment of belief?

Rational Proofs for the Createdness of Iman
Maturidi presents rational arguments and a dialectical question to prove iman's createdness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses rational inference and dialectical questioning to prove that iman is created.

Core Idea
Reason reveals that iman bears the same marks of creation as all other things.

In this passage, Maturidi extends his argument by appealing to reason's ability to recognize the traces of craftsmanship in iman. He argues that since iman is a temporal occurrence in the servant, it must be created. He then challenges the denier to identify the true nature of iman, forcing them to admit it falls into a created category.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify rational arguments
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Look for the two rational arguments: the analogy from craftsmanship and the argument from temporal occurrence.
Notice that the passage begins with 'أو أن يكون' indicating an alternative rational path.
2
Understand the temporal occurrence argument
Maturidi states that iman occurs to the servant (حدث للعبد) and that things known to be created are those that come into existence after non-existence (كان بعد أن لم يكن).
This is a direct application of the philosophical definition of creation.
3
Follow the dialectical question
Maturidi asks the denier about the true reality of iman, listing options like tasdiq, iqrar, etc. Whichever they choose, it is a created thing.
This forces the opponent to acknowledge iman's createdness through their own admission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أن يكون للعقل في تعرف ذلك نصيب، فوجد جميع ما في سائر المخلوقين من آثار الصنعة والخلقة في الإيمان، فيجب من طريق النظر الجمع بين ذلك. على أنه مما هو يحدث للعبد لحدثه، وعُرف خلق الأشياء بما كان بعد أن لم يكن. على أنّا نسأل من أنكر ذلك سؤالاً مقررًا عن حقيقة ذلك : من تصديق أو إقرار أو جميع الأعمال أو إقرار ومعرفة أو نحو ذلك؟ فيلزم الاعتراف بشيء من ذلك بما يُقابل به كل نوع ذلك . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقد روى في ذلك خبر عن رسول الله عليه السلام أنه قال: «إن الله خلق الإيمان فحقه بالسماحة والحياء» . وروى أن الله خلق مائة رحمة ، ومعلوم تسمية الإيمان رحمة؛ فيجب أن يكون فيما خلق ثمة له ضد يدفعه وشكل يعضده أو يوافقه، وكل ذي ضد وشبيه خلق.
Or that reason has a share in recognizing that, and it found all that is in other created things of traces of craftsmanship and creation in iman, so it is necessary by way of consideration to combine between them. And also that it is something that occurs to the servant due to its occurrence, and it is known that things are created by being after not being. And we ask the one who denies that a settled question about its reality: whether it is tasdiq or iqrar or all deeds or iqrar and ma'rifa or the like? So he is compelled to acknowledge something of that by which each type of that is confronted. And there is no power except with Allah. And a report has been narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Indeed Allah created iman and surrounded it with generosity and modesty.' And it is narrated that Allah created one hundred mercies, and it is known that iman is called mercy; so it must be that among what He created, it has an opposite that repels it and a form that supports or agrees with it, and everything with an opposite and a likeness is created.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage provides additional proofs for the createdness of iman, drawing on rational inference and prophetic traditions. The author states that reason can recognize the createdness of iman by observing that iman contains the same traces of craftsmanship (athar al-sun'a) and creation (al-khilqa) found in all other created things. Therefore, by rational consideration (nazar), one must conclude that iman is also created. He argues that iman occurs to the servant as a temporal event (hadith), and things are known to be created when they come into existence after non-existence. He then challenges the denier by asking for the reality of iman: is it tasdiq (assent), iqrar (acknowledgment), all deeds, or iqrar and ma'rifa (knowledge)? Whichever it is, the denier must admit that it belongs to one of these categories, each of which is created. He then cites two hadith: one stating that Allah created iman and surrounded it with generosity and modesty, and another that Allah created one hundred mercies. Since iman is called a mercy (rahma), it must be among those created mercies. Furthermore, anything that has an opposite and a form is created, and iman has opposites (like kufr) and supportive forms, thus it is created.

Key Terms
العقل
النظر
الصنعة
الخلقة
الحديث
التصديق
الإقرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rational proofs are not needed for matters of faith.
Correction: Imam Maturidi uses reason alongside revelation, showing that rational inference is a valid tool in theology.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is one reason to conclude that iman is created?
A) Because iman is an attribute of Allah
B) Because iman contains traces of craftsmanship like other created things
C) Because iman is eternal
D) Because iman is a gift that does not require reason

Key Takeaway
Reason and dialectical questioning both lead to the conclusion that iman is created, as it shares the marks of creation and is a temporal event.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your iman is a created thing that occurs to you after not having it, how does that reshape your daily dependence on Allah for every flicker of faith in your heart? What would it look like to live not as a 'self-made believer' but as one whose iman is constantly given and can be taken away?
?
The passage ends with 'There is no power except with Allah.' When you feel your faith weakening or when you sin, do you truly believe that only Allah can restore your iman? Or do you rely on your own efforts? What specific situation today can you entrust to Him in sincere helplessness?
?
Maturidi asks about the reality of iman: is it tasdiq, iqrar, deeds, or knowledge? Which of these do you find most lacking in your own heart right now? And knowing that each part is a created gift, what step can you take to ask Allah for that specific component of iman?
