Prophetic Traditions and the Argument from Opposites
Maturidi provides prophetic traditions and a logical argument based on opposites to prove iman's createdness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two hadiths and the argument from opposites prove that iman is created.

Core Idea
The Prophet's words and the nature of opposites confirm iman's createdness.

Maturidi now turns to transmitted evidence. He cites the hadith that Allah created iman and surrounded it with generosity and modesty, and another that Allah created mercy—iman being called mercy. He then uses the principle that anything with an opposite and a form is created, and iman has opposites like disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith about the creation of iman
Carefully read the hadith: 'Indeed Allah created iman and surrounded it with generosity and modesty.' Note that the verb 'khalaqa' directly indicates creation.
This hadith is explicit evidence for the createdness of iman.
2
Understand the connection between iman and mercy
The second hadith mentions Allah creating mercy. Since iman is called mercy in the Quran, iman must be among the created mercies.
This is an indirect but strong argument.
3
Apply the principle of opposites
Maturidi states that everything with an opposite and a form is created. Iman has an opposite (kufr) and forms (supporting characteristics), so it must be created.
This logical principle is derived from observation of the created world.

Analogies and Goodness Prove Iman is Created
Maturidi uses Quranic analogies and the nature of goodness to show iman is created

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses Quranic analogies and the intrinsic goodness of iman to argue that iman is a created act of Allah.

Core Idea
Iman is created because everything it is likened to is created.

Imam Maturidi presents a multi-layered argument that iman (faith) is a created entity. He first notes that iman is referred to as a path, religion, school, and creed – all of which are created. Then he draws on several Quranic analogies where Allah compares iman to created things like a tree, senses, and light. Finally, he argues that iman's own qualities – goodness, guidance, adornment – are attributes of created things. The Quranic verses he cites further confirm that iman is an act within the heart, and therefore must be created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Get a sense of the overall flow and the different types of evidence Maturidi presents.
Notice the repetition of 'then' (ثم) which marks each new argument.
2
Identify the analogies for iman
List the five analogies Allah makes for iman: tree, hearing and sight, life, good earth, and lamp. For each, ask yourself: is this thing created?
All are clearly created things, so the comparison implies iman is created.
3
Examine the argument from goodness
Maturidi says iman is good, excellent, guidance, and adornment. He then states that everything described thus is created. Reflect on why that is a logical step.
4
Analyze the Quranic verses
Read the three quoted verses (49:7, 49:14, 5:41). How do they show that iman is in the heart and is an act? Note that Allah 'adorns' iman, which implies making it; and He belies those who claim it without its reality.
The verse 49:7 is key: 'But Allah has made iman beloved to you and adorned it in your hearts.'
5
Reflect on the belying argument
Maturidi argues that if iman were not their act, Allah would not have belied them. What does this tell us about the nature of iman?
Actuality of iman can be absent even though its essence exists; it is a human act yet created by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم هو طريق يُسلك فيه، ودين يدان به و مذهب يختار ، ونحلة تُعتقد، وكل ذلك مخلوق . ثم الله تعالى ضرب مثله مرة بالشجر ، ومرة بالسمع والبصر ، ومرة بالحياة، ومرة بالأرض الطيبة ، ومرة بالسراج ، وكل ذلك مخلوق، فمثله الإيمان. ثم قد ضرب مثل الكفر بمضادات ما بينا، على الاجتماع في الحدثِية والخلقة، فمثله أمر الإيمان والكفر. والله الموفق. ثم الإيمان حسن وخير وهدى وزين لصاحبه، وكل ما ذلك وصفه فهو مخلوق. قال الله تعالى ولكن الله حبّب إليكم الإيمان وزينه في قلوبكم [الحجرات، ٧/٤٩] الآية ، ثم قال: ولما يدخل الإيمان في قلوبكم ﴾ [الحجرات، ١٤/٤٩]، وقال: ولم تؤمن قلوبهم [المائدة، ٤١/٥] الآية ، دلّ أنه في القلب، وهو فعله ، وبعيد كون ما ليس بمخلوق فيه. ثم كذَّبَ الله تعالى في ذلك قوما ادعوا لأنفسهم ؛ فلو لم يكن فعلهم لم يكن ليكذبهم، لأنه موجود وإنما يُعدم من حيث الفعل. والله الموفق.
Then it is a path that is traversed, a religion that is practiced, a school that is chosen, a creed that is believed, and all that is created. Then Allah Most High struck a likeness for it once by the tree, once by hearing and sight, once by life, once by the good earth, once by the lamp, and all that is created, so like that is iman. Then He struck a likeness for kufr by the opposites of what we have explained, upon the commonality in temporality and creation, so like that is the matter of iman and kufr. And Allah is the grantor of success. Then iman is good, excellent, guidance, and adornment for its possessor, and everything that is described thus is created. Allah Most High said: 'But Allah has made iman beloved to you and adorned it in your hearts' (49:7) the verse. Then He said: 'And iman has not entered your hearts' (49:14), and said: 'And their hearts have not believed' (5:41) the verse. This indicates that it is in the heart, and it is His act, and it is far that something not created should be in it. Then Allah belied some people who claimed it for themselves; for if it were not their act, He would not have belied them, because it exists and is only absent in terms of act. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage continues the argument that iman is created by using analogies and divine attributes. The author asserts that iman is a path (tariq), a religion (din), a school (madhhab), a creed (nihla) – all of which are created. He then notes that Allah Himself drew analogies for iman in the Quran: He compared it to a good tree (likely referring to 14:24), to hearing and sight (11:24), to life (35:22), to good earth (7:58), and to a lamp (35:19-21). All these analogies refer to created things, so the subject – iman – must also be created. Similarly, Allah compared kufr to the opposites of these, and both iman and kufr share the attribute of being temporal (hadithiyya) and created. The author then turns to the nature of iman: it is good (hasan), excellent (khayr), guidance (huda), and adornment (zayn) for its possessor. Everything described with such attributes is created. He quotes three Quranic verses: 'But Allah has made iman beloved to you and adorned it in your hearts' (49:7) – showing that Allah adorns it, implying it is His act; 'And iman has not entered your hearts' (49:14) – showing it enters the heart; and 'And their hearts have not believed' (5:41) – showing it is in the heart and an act of the heart. It is inconceivable that something not created should reside in the heart. Finally, he notes that Allah belied those who claimed iman for themselves (referring to some Bedouins in 49:14). If iman were not their own act, He would not have belied them, because the act (the actualization of iman) is what can be absent; the essence of iman exists but its realization as an act can be missing. Thus, iman is a created act.

المذهب
النحلة

البصر
الحياة
الأرض الطيبة
السراج
الكفر

الهدى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that analogies do not prove creation; the author emphasizes that all analogies are of created things, so the subject is created.
Correction: Maturidi is not simply saying 'analogy proves creation'—he is noting that every Quranic comparison of iman is to a created entity, and since the comparison is meaningful, iman must share the property of being created.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the author quote to show that Allah adorns iman in the heart?
A) 49:7
B) 49:14
C) 5:41
D) 37:96

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi argues that iman is created because it is likened to created things in the Quran, its attributes are created, and it is an act within the heart that Allah adorns.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If iman is something that enters the heart as a created act, what are you actively doing to ensure your heart remains open for it to enter and stay?
?
Allah belied those who claimed iman without it having truly entered their hearts. Where in your own life might you be claiming a faith that has not yet taken real root inside you?
?
The passage teaches that iman is adorned by Allah in the hearts. Are you treating your faith as a precious adornment from Him, or have you become complacent about its presence in your heart?

The Ruling on Making Exceptions in Iman
Maturidi states the principle of not making exceptions in affirming iman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that one must affirm iman absolutely without making exceptions, because the completeness of iman requires certainty in its components.

Core Idea
Iman must be affirmed with certainty, not conditional phrases like 'if Allah wills'.

This lesson explores a key principle of the Maturidi school: that one should not make exceptions (istithna) when affirming one's iman. The passage explains why saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is problematic when it implies doubt. We'll examine the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the original Arabic and the English translation side by side. Pay attention to the key terms like 'الاستثناء' and 'الإطلاق'.
2
Understand the principle of absolute affirmation
The passage states that the principle (الأصل) is to cut the statement of iman absolutely (قطع القول بالإيمان بالإطلاق) and to abandon exception (ترك الاستثناء). This means one should say 'I am a believer' without qualifiers.
Notice the word 'قطع' which implies decisiveness.
3
Analyze the rationale
The reason given is that iman is complete when all its meanings/components (كل معنى) exist together. Making an exception suggests that some component might be missing, thus undermining the completeness.
The phrase 'باجتماع وجوده تمام الإيمان' indicates that completeness comes from all parts being present.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some people think saying 'if Allah wills' is always fine. This teaching clarifies that it is problematic when it reflects doubt about the state of one's iman.
This aligns with the Maturidi emphasis on certainty in matters of faith.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you can identify the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة [ الاستثناء في الإيمان]  قال الفقيه رحمه الله : الأصل عندنا قطع القول بالإيمان وبالتسمّى به بالإطلاق وترك الاستثناء فيه، لأن كل معنى مما باجتماع وجوده تمام الإيمان عنده إذا استثنى فيه لم يصح.
Issue [Exception in iman]. The jurist (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The principle with us is to affirm the statement of iman and being named by it absolutely and to abandon exception in it, because every meaning which by its collective existence constitutes the complete iman in his view, if an exception is made in it, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling regarding making exceptions (istithna) in statements of iman. The author states that the established principle (al-asl) in the school is to affirm the name 'iman' absolutely (bi al-itlaq) and to avoid making exceptions. For example, one should not say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' (inshaAllah) in a way that implies doubt about one's own iman. The rationale is that iman consists of multiple components (e.g., tasdiq, iqrar, a'mal). When all these components are present together, iman is complete. If one makes an exception (e.g., 'I am a believer if Allah wills'), it undermines the completeness because it suggests that some component may be missing or uncertain. Therefore, such an exception invalidates the proper affirmation of iman. This position aligns with the Maturidi school's insistence on certainty in iman without qualifying it with conditions.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saying 'if Allah wills' about one's iman is always permissible.
Correction: The Maturidi school restricts this when it implies lack of certainty; iman must be affirmed absolutely.

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory
B) It is recommended
C) It is not valid
D) It is permissible but disliked

Key Takeaway
Iman must be affirmed with certainty, without making exceptions, because its completeness requires all components to be present without doubt.

The Ruling of Istithna' in Faith by Analogy to Worldly Oaths
Maturidi argues that attaching 'in sha' Allah' to testimony of faith is like using it in worldly oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses analogy between worldly oaths and faith to explain the effect of saying 'in sha' Allah' when testifying to faith.

Core Idea
Adding 'if Allah wills' to faith statements removes their binding force, just as in worldly contracts.

Imam Maturidi addresses a common practice: adding 'in sha' Allah' to declarations of faith. He argues that this has a legal effect similar to its use in worldly oaths and contracts. This lesson explores his reasoning and the Quranic evidence he cites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let Maturidi's argument unfold in his own words.
Pay attention to the examples he gives first.
2
Identify the examples
Notice that Maturidi lists several statements of faith: testimony of tawhid, prophethood, resurrection, etc. He attaches 'in sha' Allah' to each.
He is not singling out one testimony.
3
Grasp the general principle
Understand that for worldly matters (acknowledgments, contracts, promises), adding a condition like 'inshaAllah' prevents the statement from being binding as uttered. Maturidi claims the same applies to faith.
This is the core of the analogy.
4
Examine the Quranic support
Read the two Quran verses cited: 18:23-24 and 18:69. Note how they show that conditional statements are not considered broken if the condition is attached.
These verses provide authority for the analogy.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider the conclusion: if 'in sha' Allah' removes the binding nature of a faith declaration, does that weaken faith or change its ruling? Maturidi's point is legal, not about sincerity.
Think about how this affects the certainty of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك المعنى ؛ فعلى ذلك أمره في الجملة نحو أن يقول : أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله إن شاء الله ، أو «محمد رسول الله إن شاء الله، وكذلك الشهادة بالبعث والملائكة والرسل والكتب. وبالله العصمة. وأيضا إن حرف الدُّنْيا إذا أُلحق بالقول منع مُضيَّه على ما تفوه به كما هو من الإقرار والعقود والمواعيد وغير ذلك، فعلى ذلك أمر الإيمان وكذلك قال الله سبحانه: {ولا تقولن لشيء إني فاعل ذلك غدا إلا أن يشاء الله} [الكهف، ٢٣/١٨ - ٢٤]، وقال: {ستجدني إن شاء الله صابرا} [الكهف، ٦٩/١٨] الآية ، فلم يلحقه وصف الخلف إذا كان العهد مقرونا بالدُّنْيا . وبالله التوفيق.
That meaning; so accordingly his matter in general such as saying: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah if Allah wills, or 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah if Allah wills, and likewise bearing witness to the resurrection, angels, messengers, and books. And with Allah is protection. And also, the word of worldly [matters] when attached to speech prevents its execution as uttered, such as in acknowledgments, contracts, promises, and other than that. So accordingly is the matter of faith. And likewise God said: {And never say of anything, 'Indeed, I will do that tomorrow,' except [when adding], 'If Allah wills.'} [18:23-24], and He said: {You will find me, if Allah wills, patient} [18:69], the verse. So the description of breaking (promise) did not attach to him when the covenant was accompanied by [the phrase] 'if Allah wills' (dunya). And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage defines the analogy between istithna' (exception/conditioning) in worldly oaths and in faith. Maturidi begins by giving examples: saying 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, if Allah wills' and similar for the testimony to Muhammad, resurrection, etc. He then states that the word of dunya (worldly matters) when attached to speech prevents it from being binding as uttered, such as in acknowledgments, contracts, and promises. He argues that the same rule applies to faith. He supports this by citing Quranic verses: in Surah al-Kahf, Musa is told not to say 'I will do something tomorrow' without adding 'if Allah wills', and Khidr says 'you will find me, if Allah wills, patient'. In those worldly covenants, the person is not considered a promise-breaker because the condition was attached. Thus Maturidi concludes that istithna' in faith similarly affects the binding nature of the declaration.

Misconception: Using 'in sha' Allah' in faith is merely a sign of humility or a pious phrase without legal effect.
Correction: Maturidi shows that it has a legal effect analogous to worldly oaths: it prevents the statement from being binding as uttered. It is not just a pious addition but carries juridical weight.

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi argues that adding 'in sha' Allah' to declarations of faith has the same legal effect as in worldly oaths: it prevents the statement from being binding.

The Impermissibility of Istithna' in Faith: Certainty vs. Doubt
Maturidi explains the custom of istithna' for doubt and cites God's absolute testimonies to forbid it in faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Maturidi prohibits using istithna' (making exceptions) in declarations of faith, because it introduces doubt, and how God's absolute testimonies reinforce the need for certainty.

Core Idea
Istithna' in faith introduces doubt; but faith requires certainty.

This passage from Maturidi tackles the common practice of saying 'I am a believer, insha'Allah' (istithna'). He explains that such language stems from doubt, which contradicts the certainty of faith. By examining both human custom and divine testimony, Maturidi demonstrates that istithna' in matters of faith is not allowed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the custom of istithna'
Read how Maturidi describes the common usage of istithna' in everyday life—people only use it when they have doubt, not certainty.
He contrasts this with its use in faith.
2
See the Quranic warnings against doubt
Maturidi cites verses warning against doubt and describing hypocrites. Ask yourself: why does doubt in faith matter?
3
Examine God's absolute testimonies
Maturidi shows that Allah gives unqualified testimony of faith for believers and commands them to speak conclusively.
No one assumes they are excluded from these addresses.
4
Apply the reasoning to naming oneself a believer
Since God's addresses about faith are unconditional, we should not qualify our own faith with istithna'.
This is the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العرف الظاهر في الخلق أنهم لا يستعملونه في موضع الإحاطة والعلم؛ ومن سمع ذلك استعظم القول، نحو أن يُشار إلى محسوس ويستثنى؛ ويستعملونه في موضع الشكوك والظنون. وقد حذر الله تعالى بقوله: {ثم لم يرتابوا}، وبما وصف أهل النفاق بالشك والريب. لم يجز الثُّنْيا في كل ما لا يجوز [فيه] «أظنه» و «أحسبه» و«أشك فيه». وبالله التوفيق. ثم إن الله عز وجل شهد لمن آمن بالله ورسوله واليوم الآخر بالإيمان بقوله: {آمن الرسول} الآية، وقد مدح بقطع القول به بقوله: {قولوا آمنا بالله} الآية. ثم خاطب الله في كثير من العبادات باسم الإيمان، وفي كثير من الحل والحرمة في ذلك، ثم لم يوجد أحد يخرج [من خطاب الله] في شيء مما أحل باسم الإيمان وأمر به ظنًا منه بنفسه أنه ليس [فيه] تحقيق لذلك الاسم وأن المراد ينصرف إلى غيره، فكذلك في التسمّى.
Then the manifest custom among people is that they do not use it (istithna') in a place of encompassing knowledge; and whoever hears that considers the statement enormous, such as pointing to a perceived object and making an exception; and they use it in places of doubts and suspicions. And Allah the Exalted has warned by His saying: {Then they did not doubt}, and by His description of the hypocrites with doubt and suspicion. It is not permissible to make istithna' in everything in which it is not permissible [to use] 'I think' and 'I suppose' and 'I doubt'. And with Allah is success. Then Allah the Mighty and Majestic testified for those who believe in Allah, His Messenger, and the Last Day with faith by His saying: {The Messenger has believed} the verse, and He praised cutting off the statement with it by His saying: {Say, 'We believe in Allah'} the verse. Then Allah addressed in many acts of worship by the name of faith, and in many matters of permissibility and prohibition, then no one is found who excludes himself from the address of Allah in anything that He made permissible or commanded by the name of faith, out of an assumption that he himself does not have [in him] realization of that name and that the intended meaning refers to someone else. So likewise in being named.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage first discusses the common custom (urf) regarding istithna'. People do not use it when they have certainty and knowledge; if someone hears istithna' in such a context, they find it astonishing. Rather, people use istithna' in situations of doubt and suspicion. Maturidi then cites two Quranic warnings: Allah warns against doubt (thumma lam yartabu) and describes hypocrites as being in doubt. Therefore, istithna' is impermissible in all matters where using words like 'I think' or 'I doubt' is impermissible. Next, Maturidi argues that Allah Himself gave absolute testimonies of faith for believers, such as in the verse 'The Messenger has believed...' and praised those who make conclusive statements like 'Say, we believe in Allah...' Moreover, Allah addresses many acts of worship and rulings using the name of faith (iman), and no one assumes that they themselves are excluded from that address because they think they lack the true realization of that name. So the same applies to the matter of being named a believer: one should not qualify it with istithna'.

Correction: Maturidi clarifies that istithna' is only used for doubt, and doubt is impermissible in matters of faith. Therefore, using istithna' in faith is not permissible.

Iman as a Divine Gift: The Blameworthiness of Istithna'
Maturidi enumerates three cases of istithna' in faith and judges each negatively.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Maturidi considers using istithna' (saying 'if Allah wills') regarding one's faith to be blameworthy in all circumstances, and how it relates to ingratitude or ignorance.

Core Idea
Using istithna' in faith veils the divine gift and reveals ingratitude or self-ignorance.

Maturidi begins by establishing that faith is a pure gift from Allah, citing several Quranic verses that attribute faith to His favor, grace, and bounty. He then argues that anyone who says 'if Allah wills' about their own faith must be in one of three states: knowing they are truly faithful, not knowing their state, or knowing they are not faithful. In each case, the statement is blameworthy — either concealing God's blessings, reflecting ignorance of the greatest blessing, or vain hypocrisy. This passage challenges the notion that istithna' is a harmless expression of humility.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic passage once carefully. Notice the Quranic evidence (4 citations) and the logical argument (three cases). Let the rhythm of the original sink in before analysis.
The passage is dense but structured; try to spot the three cases.
2
Identify the three cases of istithna'
Maturidi presents three scenarios regarding the one who says 'if Allah wills' about their faith. List them and note the consequence for each.
The three cases are: (1) knowing one is genuinely faithful, (2) not knowing one's own state, (3) knowing one is not faithful.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi ends with a strong warning: istithna' in any form is blameworthy — it either conceals blessings or shows ignorance. Ask yourself: Why is this a theological principle, not just a moral advice?
This connects to the deeper idea that faith is a gift, not a possession we control.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأصل في ذلك / أن الإيمان مما يُنسب إلى الله بالإنعام كقوله تعالى: {صراط الذين أنعمت عليهم} [الفاتحة، ٧/١] وبالامتنان بقوله: {بل الله يمن عليكم} الآية، وبالتزيين في القلوب والتحبيب بقوله: {ولكن الله حبّب إليكم الإيمان وزينه في قلوبكم} [الحجرات، ٧/٤٩]، وبالإفضال بقوله: {ولولا فضل الله عليكم ورحمته} الآية. فلا يخلو من يستثنى من أن يكون عرف صدق نفسه وعظيم نعم الله وإفضاله أو لم يعلم ذلك، أو علم أنه على غير ذلك. فإن علم أنه على غير ذلك فبُعداً له، فإن الدُّنْيا لا تنفعه سوى الارتياب فيما زعم أنه لم يعلمه. وإن لم يعلم صدقه فيما قال ولا امتنان الله وإنعامه فويل له، إذ جهل أعظم نعم الله وكفر به. وإن علم ذلك فإن في حرف الشك عند السامعين ستر نعم الله وكفران مننه فذلك آية الزوال وسبب المحق. والله الموفق.
Then the principle in that is that faith is among those things attributed to God as blessing, as His saying: {The path of those upon whom You have bestowed favor} [1:7], and as favor by His saying: {Rather, Allah confers favor upon you} the verse, and by adornment in hearts and love by His saying: {But Allah has endeared to you the faith and has made it pleasing in your hearts} [49:7], and by bounty by His saying: {And if not for the favor of Allah upon you and His mercy} the verse. So he who makes istithna' is not free from either knowing the truth of himself and the greatness of God's favors and bounty, or not knowing that, or knowing that he is other than that. If he knows that he is other than that, then away with him, for dunya does not benefit him except doubt in what he claimed he did not know. And if he does not know the truth of what he said nor God's favor and bounty, then woe to him, for he is ignorant of the greatest of God's favors and has disbelieved in Him. And if he knows that, then in the word of doubt in the ears of the hearers is concealing God's favors and ingratitude for His bounties, and that is a sign of removal and a cause of extinction. And God is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle that iman (faith) is a blessing from Allah, attributed to His favor (in'am), grace (imtinan), adornment (tazyin) in hearts, and bounty (ifdal). Maturidi cites Quranic verses to support this. Then he argues that anyone who makes istithna' (says 'if Allah wills' regarding their faith) must be in one of three states: (1) They know the truth of their own faith and the greatness of Allah's favors. (2) They do not know whether they are truly faithful. (3) They know that they are not truly faithful (i.e., they are a hypocrite). If they know they are not faithful, then istithna' is useless and they are in disbelief. If they are ignorant of their own state and of Allah's favors, then they are guilty of ignorance of the greatest blessing. If they know their faith is genuine but still use istithna', then the word of doubt (shakk) in front of listeners conceals Allah's favors and shows ingratitude, which is a sign of the removal of blessings and cause of their extinction. Thus, istithna' in any case is blameworthy.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Maturidi argues that it actually reflects either ignorance of Allah's gift or ingratitude by concealing it, and it is never commendable.

D) It is a form of shirk.

Key Takeaway
Since iman is a pure gift from Allah, any doubt expressed through istithna' either reveals ignorance of this gift or constitutes ingratitude by concealing it.

Refuting Istithna' in Faith: Maturidi's Principle
Maturidi refutes those who require istithna' in faith, arguing it leads to perpetual ignorance of one's state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that using istithna' (scrupulosity) in declaring faith leads to either incurring Allah's wrath or ingratitude, and why it is rejected.

Core Idea
Istithna' in faith brings not safety but punishment or ingratitude.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi sets forth a key principle: that istithna' (saying 'if Allah wills') in one's declaration of faith is not a sign of piety but an error. He argues that if one's faith is genuine, such scrupulosity incurs divine wrath; if insincere, it shows ingratitude. Then he contrasts this with the views of the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hashwiyya, showing the absurd consequence of perpetual ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the English translation. Let the argument's flow sink in.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Maturidi presents two cases: if the person's faith is realized (true), scrupulosity does not benefit but brings wrath; if not realized, it incurs ingratitude. Find these in the text.
Notice the conditional 'law tahqaqu' and 'lam yutahaqqaq'.
3
Analyze the critique of the sects
Maturidi then attacks the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hashwiyya who require istithna'. Their view leads to perpetual ignorance of one's state. Understand why this is problematic.
Think about the consequence: if you can never be sure of your faith, you cannot claim belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأصل عندنا أن الثنيا حرف يُستعمل في موضع التحرج. وهذا موضع لو تحقق الذي له يتحرج لا ينفعه التحرج، بل يلزمه مقت الله ونقمته؛ ولو لم يتحقق يلحقه حكم كفران نعم الله حيث لم يره منه ولم يشكر له، إذ أوجب له ولايته وأضاف إلى نفسه الإخراج من الظلمات إلى النور. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم الحق على مذهب المعتزلة والخوارج والحشوية الاستثناء في الدين، وبخاصة في الإيمان. فأما عند المعتزلة والخوارج فإنه يخرج من حيث لا يشعر به، ويمتنع عن الإجابة من حيث لا يعلم به، وإذا كان كذلك فهو أبداً في جهل من حاله، فحقه أن لا يتسمى به. وعلى ذلك.
Then the principle with us is that istithna' is a word used in a place of scrupulosity (taharruj). And this is a situation: if the one who is scrupulous is actually realized (in his faith), scrupulosity does not benefit him; rather, he incurs Allah's wrath and punishment. And if it is not realized (i.e., his faith is not true), then the ruling of ingratitude for Allah's favors attaches to him, since he did not see (the favor) from Him and did not thank Him, because (Allah) obligated His allegiance to him and attributed to Himself the bringing out from darkness into light. And there is no power except with Allah. Then the truth according to the school of the Mu'tazila, the Khawarij, and the Hashwiyya is to make istithna' in religion, especially in faith. As for with the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, one exits (from faith) without being aware, and refrains from answering without knowing. And if this is so, then he is perpetually ignorant of his state, so it is proper that he not be named (a believer). And upon that.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
In this passage, Maturidi presents his own principle (al-asl 'indana): istithna' is used for taharruj (scrupulosity, seeking to avoid wrongdoing). But he argues that in matters of faith, this scrupulosity is misplaced. If the person's faith is truly realized (haqqaq), then using istithna' does not benefit him; instead, it incurs Allah's wrath because it implies doubt. If his faith is not realized (i.e., he is insincere), then he is guilty of ingratitude because he fails to acknowledge Allah's favor of guidance. Maturidi then criticizes the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Hashwiyya who require istithna' in religion, especially in faith. According to their views, a person can exit faith without realizing it (because they consider deeds as part of faith, so sinning can nullify faith), and they may refrain from answering (i.e., affirming faith) without knowing. Consequently, such a person remains perpetually ignorant of his state, and therefore it is proper that he not call himself a believer. Maturidi implies this is an absurd consequence.

Key Terms
التحرج
المعتزلة
الخوارج
الحشوية
الاستثناء
النقمة
الكفران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Istithna' in declaring faith is a humble and pious precaution.
Correction: Maturidi argues that istithna' in faith is not praiseworthy: for the true believer, it incurs Allah's wrath; for the insincere, it amounts to ingratitude.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what happens if a person with true faith uses istithna' (taharruj) in their declaration of faith?
A) They are rewarded for their caution.
B) They incur Allah's wrath and punishment.
C) Their faith becomes stronger.
D) It is considered an act of worship.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi rejects istithna' in faith because it either brings Allah's wrath upon the true believer or renders the insincere ungrateful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever said 'I am a believer if Allah wills' thinking it showed humility? According to Maturidi, if your faith is genuine, that very expression could incur Allah's wrath. How will you change your speech to reflect gratitude and certainty, not cautious doubt?
?
Maturidi argues that istithna' leads to perpetual ignorance of one's own state of faith. Do you truly know whether you are a believer in front of Allah? If you are uncertain, how can you escape that ignorance without falling into the very error he refutes?
?
The Mu'tazila and Khawarij end up unable to be named believers because of their perpetual ignorance. Could your own hesitation to affirm your faith be a sign of ingratitude for the guidance Allah has given you? What concrete step will you take today to affirm your faith without reservation?

True Iman is in the Heart, Not the Tongue
Maturidi explains that hypocrites' verbal claim to iman is false because iman is in the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true iman is a matter of the heart, not merely verbal declaration, and why hypocrites are considered liars despite their words.

Core Idea
Iman is in the heart; the tongue only expresses it.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses a critical distinction: faith is not simply what we say. Hypocrites may declare iman with their tongues, but if the heart is empty, the declaration is worthless. This lesson unpacks Maturidi's argument that the true reality of iman resides in the heart, not on the tongue.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
The passage begins mid-sentence, but the core argument is complete.
2
Identify the key claim about the heart
Notice that Maturidi says 'its due is the heart' and 'the tongue is an expression of it'. This establishes the heart as the seat of true iman.
3
Apply to hypocrites
Maturidi states that Allah testified against hypocrites as liars because they claimed iman but lacked it in their hearts. Ask yourself: Why does verbal confession not save them?
The passage concludes that only their statement remained, not true iman.
4
Reflect on the core idea
Internalize the lesson: iman must be heartfelt. Mere words do not make a believer.

لا يتوجه إلى هذا الوجه . فنفي عنهم ، وإن كانوا أظهروه من عند أنفسهم، لأن حقه القلب، واللسان مُعبّر عنه؛ لذلك شهد الله تعالى على المنافقين بالكذب بما أخبروا من إيمانهم ، إذ حقيقته بالقلب، ولم يكن لهم ذلك، ولهذا ما بقى إيمانهم، وأثبت لهم القول به لا غير. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
It is not directed towards this aspect. So denial is attributed to them, even if they have manifested it from themselves, because its due is the heart, and the tongue is an expression of it. Therefore, Allah testified against the hypocrites as liars regarding what they informed of their iman, since its reality is in the heart, and they did not have that. Hence, their iman did not remain, and He affirmed for them the statement only. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage defines the true reality (haqiqa) of iman as being in the heart, not merely on the tongue. The author begins by stating that hypocrites who outwardly declare iman are still disbelievers because the truth of iman belongs to the heart. The tongue only expresses what is in the heart. Allah testified against them as liars because they claimed iman but lacked it in their hearts. Therefore, their iman (in the sense of true iman) did not exist; Allah only affirmed that they made a verbal statement. The author emphasizes that verbal declaration without heart affirmation is not considered iman.

Correction: This passage shows that iman must be in the heart. Without inner conviction, a person is a hypocrite, not a believer.

Iman and Islam Are One in Reality
Maturidi argues using reason and Quran that iman and islam are identical in reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that iman (faith) and islam (submission) are identical in reality and cannot be separated.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are two names for the same reality.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi presents a rational and scriptural proof that iman and Islam are essentially one. He builds on the definitions established earlier and argues that it is impossible for a person to fulfill all conditions of one without the other. Through a careful analysis of Quranic verses and logical possibilities, he demonstrates their unity.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definitions
Maturidi starts by referencing the earlier definitions of iman (heart conviction) and islam (bodily submission). Understand that these are the foundations.
2
Follow the rational proof
Read the argument that it is inconceivable to have all conditions of iman without being a Muslim, or vice versa. This establishes their unity.
This is the core logical step.
3
Consider the three possibilities
Maturidi examines three cases for a believer: full Islam, partial Islam, or a different religion. See how he eliminates the second and third to conclude that true faith includes the whole of Islam.
4
Connect with Quranic evidence
Notice the verses from Surah Al-Imran that state only Islam is accepted. Maturidi uses them to reinforce that iman and Islam are the same religion.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The final conclusion is that iman and Islam are one in reality. Consider why this matters for understanding the nature of faith.
This lesson establishes a key Maturidi doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذ كان حقيقة الإسلام ما ذكرنا وحقيقة الإيمان ما ذكرنا، ففاسد أحدهما وجود بالحقيقة والآخر ليس. فلذلك قيل: هما واحد في التحصيل، وإن كانت العبارة من الاسم في الإطلاق ربما تختلف، كالإنسان وابن آدم ورجل وفلان. يختلف المعنى من ظاهر الإسلام وفي التحقيق هما واحد، من حيث كان بوجود واحد وجود الآخر إلا من الوجه الذي وصفت في حق الإسلام الذي هو باللسان. والله أعلم. ثم الأصل أنه من البعيد عن العقول أن يأتي المرء بجميع شرائط الإيمان ثم لا يكون مسلما، أو يأتي بجميع شرائط الإسلام ثم لا يكون مؤمنا، ثبت أنهما في الحقيقة واحد. ومعلوم أن الذي يسع له التسمّى بأحدهما يسع بالآخر، وأن الذي به تختلف الأديان إنما هو الاعتقاد لا بأفعال سواه. وبالوجود يستحق كل الاسم المعروف، لذلك وجب ما قلنا. وقد قال الله تعالى: إن الدين عند الله الإسلام (آل عمران 19)، وقال: ومن يبتغ غير الإسلام دينا فلن يقبل منه (آل عمران 85)، فالمؤمن بالصفة التي يصير بها مؤمنا، لا يخلو من أن يكون أتى بالإسلام الذي هو الدين عند الله، أو أتى ببعضه لا كله، أو ابتغى غير دين الله. فإن قال بالأول أذعن للحق، وإن قال بالثاني فهو إذا لم يبتغ به دينا إنما ابتغى بعضه، وذلك بعيد، بل شهد الله على مثله بأنه كافر حقا. وبعد، فإن كل كافر قد يأتي ببعضه ثم لم يجب به الاسم، وقد سُمّي به من ذكرت؛ ثبت أنه قد أتى بالكل. وإن قال بالثالث صير دار المؤمنين النار، وأبطل جميع ما جاء به الرسل من الأمر بالإيمان بهم، ثم لم يصر مسلما بذلك، وجاء بما لا يقبل منه من الأديان؛ ثبت أنه التام من الدين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then, since the reality of Islam is what we mentioned and the reality of iman is what we mentioned, one of them being corrupt is that one exists in reality and the other does not. Therefore, it is said: they are one in attainment, although the expression of the name in absolute usage may differ, like 'human', 'son of Adam', 'man', and 'so-and-so'. The meaning may differ from the apparent meaning of Islam, but in reality they are one, because the existence of one entails the existence of the other except from the aspect I described concerning Islam which is by the tongue. And Allah knows best. Then the principle is that it is far from reason for a person to come with all the conditions of iman and then not be a Muslim, or to come with all the conditions of Islam and then not be a believer. So it is established that they are one in reality. And it is known that whoever is permitted to be named by one of them is permitted to be named by the other, and that what distinguishes religions is only belief (i'tiqad), not actions other than it. And by existence each deserves the known name, therefore what we said is necessary. And Allah said: 'Indeed, the religion in the sight of Allah is Islam' (3:19), and 'Whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him' (3:85). So the believer, by the quality by which he becomes a believer, is either one who has come with Islam which is the religion of Allah, or he has come with part of it not all, or he has sought other than the religion of Allah. If he says the first, he has assented to the truth; if he says the second, then if he does not seek thereby a religion, he only seeks part of it, and that is far (from truth), rather Allah has testified that such a person is truly a disbeliever. Moreover, every disbeliever may come with part of it but the name (Muslim) does not apply, while it has been applied to those I mentioned; so it is established that he has come with the whole. And if he says the third, he makes the abode of the believers into fire, and nullifies all that the messengers brought of the command to believe in them, then he does not become a Muslim by that, and he brings what is not accepted from the religions; so it is established that he has the complete religion. And there is no power except through Allah.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a reasoned argument (istidlal) proving that iman and islam are materially identical in reality. The author begins by recalling the definitions: the reality of iman is heart conviction, and the reality of islam is bodily submission. He argues that it is corrupt to say one exists without the other. They are one in actuality (tahsil), although the words may differ in common usage, like different names for the same person. He then gives a rational proof: it is inconceivable by reason that a person fulfills all the conditions of iman yet is not a muslim, or vice versa. Therefore, they are one. He supports this with Quranic verses: the only religion accepted is Islam, implying true iman is identical with Islam. He then considers three possibilities for a believer: either he has full Islam (accepted), partial (rejected as disbelief), or a different religion (rejected). He argues that since disbelievers sometimes perform some Islamic acts but are not called Muslims, the true believer must have the whole of Islam. Therefore, iman and Islam are inseparable. The conclusion is that they are one in reality.

Key Terms
iman (إيمان)
islam (إسلام)
haqiqa (حقيقة)
i'tiqad (اعتقاد)
tahsil (تحصيل)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iman and islam are separate categories that can exist independently.
Correction: Maturidi argues they are identical in reality; one cannot have true faith without complete submission, and vice versa.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the relationship between iman and islam?
A) They are distinct and can exist separately
B) They are identical in reality
C) Islam is a subset of iman
D) Iman is only in the heart while islam is only in actions

Key Takeaway
Iman and Islam are two names for the same reality: a person who has true faith necessarily has complete submission, and vice versa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine your daily life: do you ever separate your inner beliefs (iman) from your outward actions (islam)? Where do you find yourself acting as if one can exist without the other? What would it take for you to make them truly one in your living?
?
If the only accepted religion is Islam, and iman and islam are identical, then you cannot claim to have faith while holding back full submission. What part of your life are you withholding from Allah? Will you surrender it today?
?
Maturidi says it is impossible to have all the conditions of iman and not be a Muslim. Consider your own iman—does it manifest in complete submission? If not, what are you missing? Ask Allah to grant you both iman and islam as one reality.

Maturidi's Reconciliation of the Hadith of Jibril
Maturidi explains two interpretations of the apparent distinction between iman and islam in the hadith of Jibril.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi reconciles the hadith of Jibril with the unity of iman and Islam through two interpretative approaches.

Core Idea
Distinct wording in hadith does not mean separate realities; Maturidi uses narrator variation and linguistic metaphor to affirm unity.

The famous hadith of Jibril appears to list iman, islam, and ihsan as separate categories, which might challenge the earlier conclusion that they are one. Imam Maturidi confronts this potential objection directly by examining variant narrations and proposing two ways to understand the apparent distinction. This lesson follows his careful reasoning to see how the hadith actually supports, rather than contradicts, the unity of iman and islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the variant narration
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice that Maturidi begins by citing a narration from Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet answered the question about iman with the laws of Islam—this suggests the original hadith may have been conflated.
This variant is key to Maturidi's first interpretation.
2
Identify the two main interpretations
Maturidi proposes two ways to understand the first hadith: either the narrator omitted part of the question/answer, or the community already knew the inseparability of iman and islam, so mentioning one sufficed—supported by linguistic metaphor.
Each interpretation preserves the reality of unity.
3
Understand how each interpretation upholds unity
The first interpretation relies on transmission error; the second uses two aspects: (a) prior knowledge that a believer must be Muslim, and (b) metaphorical naming where an action is called by its cause or associate. Conclude that Quranic rulings confirm they are one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نذكر الاختلاف الذي نشأ من خبر جبريل عليه السلام؛ قد روى في ذلك اختلاف في اللفظ. روى عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئل عن الإيمان، ثم عن شرائع الإسلام، فأجاب بالذي ذكر في السؤال عن الإسلام. فيكون هذا الخبر تفسيرًا للخبر الأول. ويُحمل الخبر الأول على جهتين. (أ) إما على أن الراوي لم يسمع الشرائع في السؤال أو في الرواية عن الذي رواه، فروى كذلك، يؤيده خبر ابن عمر أن ذلك قد كان. ومن البعيد أن يكون مقدار الأول. يؤيده ابن عمر، لما يُسقط الشهادة بما يخبر عن جبريل وعن الرسول بغير الذي قالا. وغير مدفوع حقا البعض على بعض، فيرويه على ما وقع عنده. وأيد هذا ما قد ذكر في بعض الأخبار أن النبي عليه السلام قال: «هذا جبريل أتاكم ليعلمكم دينكم»، وروى في غيره ليعلمكم أمر دينكم، فكان في الخبر «أمر دينكم» وإن خفى على الآخر، فمثله الخبر الأول. والجهة الثانية على أن الاكتفاء أحدهما به بوجهين: أنهم قد علموا أنه لا يجوز أن يكون مؤمنا غير مسلم في الحقيقة، أو مسلما غير مؤمن، فرأوا أن ذلك القدر كافٍ عن الإبلاغ في الذكر لظهور ذلك. والآخر أن يكون الثاني عنده البيان عن أفعال الإسلام يرويه باسمه، على مجاز اللغة في تسمية الشيء باسم سببه واسم المتصل به. ثم قد ثبت أنهما واحد في التحقيق على ما جرى به أحكام القرآن، قال الله تعالى:
Then we mention the disagreement that arose from the report of Jibril, peace be upon him; there is a difference reported in the wording. It is narrated from Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was asked about iman, then about the laws of Islam, and he answered with what was mentioned in the question about Islam. So this report is an interpretation of the first report. And the first report is understood in two ways: (1) Either the narrator did not hear the laws in the question or in the narration from the one who narrated it, so he narrated accordingly, supported by the report of Ibn 'Umar that this had occurred. And it is far from the extent of the first (report). Ibn 'Umar supports it, for he would not invalidate the testimony by reporting about Jibril and the Messenger other than what they said. And truly, one part is not rejected in favor of another; rather he narrates it as it occurred. This is supported by what has been mentioned in some reports that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'This is Jibril who came to teach you your religion,' and in another: 'to teach you the matter of your religion,' so in the report there was 'the matter of your religion,' even if it was hidden from the other. So the first report is similar. (2) The second way: that reliance on one of them suffices for two aspects: they knew that it is not permissible for a believer not to be a Muslim in reality, or a Muslim not a believer, so they saw that that much was sufficient for elaboration due to its obviousness. And the other (aspect) is that the second (narrator) had the explanation of the actions of Islam and narrated it by its name, as a metaphorical license in language of naming a thing by its cause and by its connected name. Then it has been established that they are one in reality according to what the rulings of the Qur'an proceed upon. Allah said:
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage addresses an apparent objection to the unity of iman and islam based on the well-known hadith of Jibril where the Prophet distinguishes between iman, islam, and ihsan. The author (Maturidi) notes that there is a variant narration from Ibn 'Umar in which the Prophet answered the question about iman with what is usually said about islam, indicating that the distinction may be due to narrator error or conflation. The author then proposes two main interpretations to harmonize the reports. The first interpretation: the narrator of the original hadith may have omitted part of the question or answer, as evidenced by Ibn 'Umar's version. The second interpretation has two sub-aspects: either the early community already knew the inseparability of iman and islam, so mentioning one sufficed; or the narrator used a linguistic metaphor where the name of a thing is applied to its cause or associated element. Ultimately, the author concludes that the Quranic rulings confirm that iman and islam are one in reality. Thus, the hadith does not contradict the earlier rational and Quranic proof.

Key Terms
hadith Jibril (حديث جبريل)
tawil (تأويل)
riwaya (رواية)
majaz (مجاز)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of Jibril proves that iman and islam are separate and distinct realities.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the apparent distinction can be explained by narrator variation or linguistic metaphor, and the Quran confirms they are one reality.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi reconcile the hadith of Jibril that lists iman and islam separately with the argument that they are one in reality?
A) He claims the hadith is weak
B) He gives two interpretations: either a narrator error or the use of linguistic metaphor/omission
C) He says iman and islam are different but both required
D) He reinterprets the hadith as referring to different historical contexts

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the apparent distinction in the hadith of Jibril can be resolved through textual analysis and linguistic principles, affirming that iman and islam are one reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a hadith that seems to contradict a clear principle from the Quran, do you immediately doubt your understanding, or do you, like Maturidi, seek a way to harmonize? What does your response reveal about your trust in the consistency of divine revelation?
?
Maturidi shows that even the Prophet's own words can be subject to narrator variation. Are you willing to humbly re-examine your most cherished interpretations of hadith when confronted with evidence, or do you cling to them out of habit? What is one hadith you might need to revisit?
?
If Iman and Islam are truly one in reality, then your inner faith and outward actions must align. Which area of your life exhibits a gap between what you claim to believe and how you act, and what concrete step will you take today to close that gap?

Islam and Iman Are Not Separate
Maturidi argues against separating Islam and Iman using Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational and scriptural argument that Islam and Iman are coextensive and cannot be separated.

Core Idea
Islam and Iman are two names for the same reality; you cannot have one without the other.

Maturidi opens this passage by challenging those who claim that 'Muslim' and 'believer' designate different categories. He presents both Quranic evidence and logical reasoning to show that no practical or theological distinction can be maintained. As we read, pay attention to how he uses the three categories of people in the Prophet's time to support his conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
The passage uses a dialectical style with rhetorical questions.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Notice the two verses Maturidi quotes: one linking righteous deeds with faith, the other linking submission to Allah. See how they imply integration of Islam and Iman.
Verse 20:112 and 31:22.
3
Follow the logical challenge
Trace the hypothetical questions Maturidi poses to anyone claiming a difference. He demands a practical distinction in this world or the next. No such distinction can be shown.
He then invokes the three categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. No separate 'Muslim' exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن يعمل من الصالحات وهو مؤمن ﴾ [طه، ۱۱۲/۲۰] الآية ، كما قال : ومن يُسلم وجهه إلى الله ﴾ [لقمان، ۲۲/۳۱] . ثم يقال لصاحب هذا القول: [هل ] يُحقق هذا الاسم بأحدهما ويمنع الآخر حكما في أمر الدنيا والآخرة أو لا ؟ فإن حقق فيقال : ما ذلك، [و] إلى أي الدارين يَرِد المسلم أو المؤمن؟ ثم في الشاهد أي الاسمين أحمد، وأي حق فيما بين العبد وربه أو بينه وبين الخلق يُحقق له عند وجود أحد الاسمين ولا يُحقق عند وجود الآخر؟ فلا يجد إلى تحقيق ذلك سبيلاً. فيقال عند ذلك : إذ لم تجعل الاسم بأحدهما علمًا لأمرٍ منعته المسمى بالآخر ـ وكذلك فيما يلحق الضرر - فإذا صرت أنت بالتفريق عابثًا ملبساً. ثم الناس في عهد رسول الله ثلاثة : مؤمن وكافر ومنافق، لم يُعرف للمسلم درجة خارجة من هؤلاء ولا للمؤمن، وفي التفريق ذلك، وذلك خلاف ما عليه الأمر الأول من الخلق. على أن أهل الأديان جميعا فروا عن اسم الإسلام؛ فلو لم يكن الإسلام معروفًا عندهم أنه ما معناه وما الذي نفرت عنه طباعهم لكان لا معنى لذلك. وبه وصف الرسل أنهم سموا . وإذا ثبت أنه معلوم عند الخلق فمن رام صرفه إلى معنى زائد في الدين أو إلى معنى زائد على الإيمان أو ناقص عنه، يجب إن ذهب إلى معنى ناقص عنه أن يجعل الإسلام دون الإيمان؛ فيجب عليه حقيقته والتدين بذلك الدين، ثم لا يكون مؤمنًا . وإن كان زائدا فيجب أن لا يقع النفار عن قدر ما يُدعون إلى الإيمان وإن لم يوصف لهم أنهم أسلموا . فإذ وجد ذلك ثبت ذلك غير زائد على الآخر ولا له وجود دونه. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And whoever does righteous deeds while he is a believer (Surah Taha, 20:112), as He said: And whoever submits his face to Allah (Surah Luqman, 31:22). Then it is said to the proponent of this view: Does he verify this name with one of the two and prevent the other regarding a ruling in the affairs of this world and the Hereafter, or not? If he verifies, it is said: What is that, and to which of the two abodes does the Muslim or the believer revert? Then in the witnessed realm, which of the two names is more praiseworthy, and what right between the servant and his Lord or between him and creation is verified for him when one of the two names exists and is not verified when the other exists? He finds no way to verify that. So it is said at that point: Since you did not make the name with one of the two a sign for a matter that you prevented for the one named by the other—as well as regarding what attaches of harm—then you have become, by making a distinction, a frivolous confuser. Then people at the time of the Messenger of Allah were three: a believer, a disbeliever, and a hypocrite. No degree was known for the Muslim outside these, nor for the believer, and in that distinction is that, and that is contrary to what the first affair of creation was. Moreover, all the people of religions fled from the name of Islam; if Islam were not known to them as to what its meaning is and what their natures recoiled from, that would have no meaning. And by it the messengers are described that they were named. And if it is established that it is known to creation, then whoever aims to divert it to an extra meaning in the religion, or to an extra meaning beyond faith, or less than it—if he goes to a meaning less than it, he must make Islam less than faith; then he must [follow] its reality and adherence to that religion, then he is not a believer. And if it is extra, then the aversion should not occur at the measure to which they are called to faith even if they are not described as having submitted. So when that is found, it is established that it is not extra to the other nor does it have existence without it. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage presents an argument against those who separate Islam and Iman as distinct categories. Maturidi begins by quoting two Quranic verses: one about righteous deeds while being a believer, and another about submitting one's face to Allah. He then poses a challenge to anyone who claims that the terms 'Muslim' and 'believer' designate different realities: If someone claims they differ, he must explain whether this difference has practical consequences in this world and the next. For example, to which abode does a Muslim go versus a believer? In the witnessed realm, which name is more praiseworthy? And what specific rights are established by one name but not the other? Since no such distinction can be demonstrated, the one making the distinction is merely playing with words. Next, Maturidi refers to the three categories of people in the Prophet's era: believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite. There was no separate category of 'Muslim' apart from these; thus, inventing a difference between Islam and Iman contradicts the early understanding. He also notes that all other religions fled from the name 'Islam', implying its meaning is known. If someone tries to reinterpret Islam as something more or less than Iman, inconsistencies arise: if Islam is less, then one could be Muslim without being a believer, which is false; if Islam is more, then people should have a greater aversion to it than to Iman, but that is not observed. The conclusion is that Islam and Iman are neither greater nor lesser than each other; they are coextensive.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الإسلام
المؤمن
المسلم
المنافق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Islam and Iman are distinct categories such that one can be a Muslim without being a believer.
Correction: Maturidi argues that Islam and Iman are coextensive; being a Muslim implies being a believer, and vice versa.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi use the three categories of people in the Prophet's time to argue against separating Islam and Iman?
A) He says there were Muslims, believers, and hypocrites, showing Islam is a separate category.
B) He says there were believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites, with no separate Muslim category, proving Islam and Iman are not distinct.
C) He says there were Muslims and believers only, indicating they are the same.
D) He says the Prophet's companions were all Muslims, so no distinction is needed.

Key Takeaway
Islam and Iman are not separate; they are two names for the same state of submission and belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever categorized yourself as a 'Muslim' while feeling distant from being a true 'believer'? What would change if you accepted that the two are inseparable in Allah's sight?
?
The hypocrites fled from the name Islam because they rejected its demands. Is there any area of your life where you flee from submission—where you claim to believe but avoid acting on it?
?
If Islam and Iman are truly the same, why do you sometimes act as if certain obligations are optional is while still calling yourself a believer? How might this self-deception harm your faith?

Maturidi's Argument: Islam Is Essentially Belief
Maturidi uses the hadith on apostasy to prove Islam is essentially belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the hadith on apostasy and a reductio argument to prove that Islam is fundamentally belief, not actions.

Core Idea
Changing religion means changing belief, not actions.

Maturidi presents a sharp textual and rational argument to settle a key theological question: What makes someone a Muslim? He cites the prophetic hadith on apostasy and a Quranic verse to show that the criterion is belief itself, and then he exposes the absurdity of including actions in the definition of religion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the hadith, the Quranic verse, and the logical question Maturidi poses.
Pay attention to the two possible answers to 'Is he a Muslim?'
2
Trace the Argument
Follow Maturidi's reasoning: the hadith and verse define religion. The question about being Muslim tests whether belief has changed. If one denies being Muslim, he has changed religion; if he affirms, he is Muslim by faith.
This shows that religion is identified with belief, not actions.
3
Understand the Reductio
Maturidi then argues: if actions were part of religion, then everyone would constantly be changing religion because everyone performs varying acts of devotion. This absurdity confirms that religion is solely belief.
Ask yourself: Why would including actions make the concept of changing religion meaningless?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من بدل دينه فاقتلوه ، ثم بيّن الله دينه فقال: فمن يكفر بالطاغوت ويؤمن بالله ، فيقال: أهو مسلم أو لا؟ فإن قال: لا، فقد بدل إذا دين الله . وإن قال: نعم، صار مسلما بفعل الإيمان لا غير. على أن هذا الخبر في تبديل الدين، وأنه معروف أنه الاعتقاد لا غير، وأن المراد في ذلك راجع إلى الدين الذي هو الإسلام؛ ثبت أنه معروف الحد والقدر، يُعرف مبدله . ولو كانت الأفعال سوى الاعتقاد دينا كان كل واحد في كل أحواله مبدل الدين لوجود في غير تلك الأفعال أفعال من القرب في كل وقت. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Whoever changes his religion, kill him. Then Allah explained His religion and said: Whoever disbelieves in the false deity and believes in Allah (Surah Al-Baqarah, 2:256). So it is said: Is he a Muslim or not? If he says: No, then he has changed the religion of Allah. And if he says: Yes, then he becomes a Muslim by the act of faith, not otherwise. Moreover, this report is about changing religion, and it is known that it is belief, not otherwise, and that what is intended in that refers to the religion which is Islam. It is established that it has a known limit and measure, and its changer is known. And if actions other than belief were religion, then every person in every state would be a changer of religion, because there exist in him, besides those actions, actions of devotion at all times. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage provides a proof from the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' and the Quranic verse defining religion as disbelief in false deities and belief in Allah. Maturidi argues that the hadith implies that religion is defined by belief, because the punishment for changing religion is execution, and that change is identified by a change in belief, not outer actions. If someone denies being a Muslim, he has changed the religion of Allah. If he affirms he is a Muslim, he is a Muslim by virtue of the act of faith (iman), not by anything else. The argument then shows that if actions other than belief were part of religion, then every person would be constantly changing religion, since everyone occasionally performs or omits actions; thus, the concept of changing religion would become meaningless. This solidifies that Islam is essentially belief, not a set of outward actions.

Key Terms
تبديل الدين
الاعتقاد
الإيمان
الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that changing religion refers to changing outward rituals or practices, not inner belief.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the hadith on apostasy defines changing religion as a change in belief, as indicated by the question 'Is he a Muslim?' which tests one's self-identification with Islam, not their actions.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him'?
A) Changing religion refers to changing outward actions only.
B) If actions other than belief were religion, everyone would constantly be changing religion.
C) The hadith only applies to hypocrites.
D) The hadith shows that Islam is a combination of belief and actions.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi proves that Islam is belief by showing that the hadith on apostasy treats belief as the criterion and that including actions would make the concept of changing religion meaningless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If someone asked you right now 'Are you a Muslim?', would your answer come from a conviction in your heart or just a habit of identification? What would change if you had to give that answer knowing it could cost you your life?
?
Maturidi argues that if actions were part of religion, everyone would be constantly changing their religion. Look at your own life: do you define your faith more by your daily deeds or by your settled belief? Which one actually determines your identity as a Muslim?
?
The passage says that changing religion means changing belief, not actions. Is there any area where you have changed your actions without addressing the belief underneath? What would it take for your inner belief to match your outward practice?

Refuting the Outward-Only Interpretation of Islam
Maturidi refutes the claim that Islam is merely outward actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that Islam is not merely outward actions but requires inner submission.

Core Idea
Outward submission without inner faith is not true Islam.

Maturidi tackles a common objection: if Islam is defined by actions, then hypocrites who perform the same actions would be Muslims. He uses Quranic verses to show that real Islam is inward submission (inqiyad) and surrender (istislam). This lesson unpacks his logical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure of the argument: it starts with an objection, then presents a reductio ad absurdum, and concludes with the true definition.
The text is cut off at the end due to page boundary; the argument remains clear.
2
Identify the objection being refuted
Maturidi addresses someone who interprets Islam based only on outward actions, citing a report. Find where this view is mentioned.
The objection is implicit; look for 'then it is said to him'.
3
Follow the reductio argument
Maturidi points out that hypocrites also perform outward actions and say 'we have submitted.' If that were true Islam, then the hypocrites would be Muslims, leading to absurd conclusions like sincere believers seeking a different religion.
Understand the logical consequence that makes the outward-only view untenable.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
Maturidi quotes verses: Surah Al-Hujurat 49:14 and 49:17, and alludes to others. See how these verses distinguish between mere outward submission and true faith.
Verse 49:17 rebukes those who think their submission is a favor, indicating it is not the essence of Islam.
5
Grasp the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the real meaning of Islam is 'inqiyad' (submission) and 'istislam' (surrender), which are inward states, not just outward actions.
This is the key doctrinal point: true Islam is faith in the heart, expressed through obedience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له : الخبر الذي رويتَ في هذا الباب في تفسير الإسلام فيه ذكر الأمور الظاهرة؛ وكذلك أهل النفاق يوافقون المؤمنين في الأمور الظاهرة، وقد قيل لهم قولوا أسلمنا [الحجرات ١٤/٤٩] . أهو الإسلام في الحقيقة أو لا؟ فإن قال: نعم، هو الإسلام في الحقيقة صير قوله : إن الدين عند الله الإسلام ﴾ [آل عمران، ۱۹/۳]، وقوله : ورضيت لكم الإسلام دينا [المائدة ٣/٥] هو الذي ذكر فيجب أن يكون قوله ومن يبتغ غير الإسلام دينا فلن يقبل منه وهو في الآخرة من الخاسرين ﴾ [آل عمران ۸۰/۳]، وقال: كيف يهدى الله قوما كفروا بعد إيمانهم ﴾ [آل عمران ٨٦/٣ ، هو ذلك الذي قال لهم: قولوا أسلمنا [الحجرات ١٤/٤٩] ، وما جاء به الخبر لوجود تلك الشهادة في أهل النفاق وتلك الأفعال. فيكون المخلصون والمؤمنون قد ابتغوا غير الإسلام دينا ، وتركوا ما رضي الله عنهم وأهل النفاق الذين جاءوا به ، وذلك بعيد. فثبت أن ذلك الإسلام الانقياد والاستسلام. وأما حقيقته فهو الدين في الحقيقة لا ما ذكر من الظواهر . دليل ذلك الأمر الذي ذكر أن الله قال في آخر السورة : يمنون عليك أن أسلموا قل لا تمنوا على إسلامكم ﴾ [الحجرات، ١٧/٤٩]، ولو كان
Then it is said to him: The report that you narrated in this chapter concerning the interpretation of Islam includes mention of outward matters. Likewise, the hypocrites conform with the believers in outward matters, and it was said to them: Say, we have submitted (Surah Al-Hujurat, 49:14). Is that Islam in reality or not? If he says: Yes, it is Islam in reality, then his statement makes His saying: Indeed, the religion with Allah is Islam (Surah Al-Imran, 3:19), and His saying: And I have chosen for you Islam as a religion (Surah Al-Ma'idah, 5:3), to be that which is mentioned, then it must be that the sincere ones and the believers have sought a religion other than Islam, and left what Allah was pleased with for them, while the hypocrites came with it, and that is far-fetched. So it is established that that Islam is submission and surrender. As for its reality, it is the religion in truth, not what is mentioned of outward appearances. Evidence of that is the matter which He mentioned that Allah said at the end of the surah: They consider it a favor to you that they have submitted. Say: Do not regard your submission as a favor to me (Surah Al-Hujurat, 49:17). And if it were...
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection based on a hadith that interprets Islam in terms of outward actions. Maturidi points out that the hypocrites also perform outward actions and even say 'we have submitted.' The question is whether that outward submission is the real Islam. If one affirms that it is, then the Quranic verses that declare Islam as the true religion would apply to the hypocrites' mere outward actions. This would lead to the absurd conclusion that sincere believers, who have inner faith, have sought a religion different from that of the hypocrites—meaning they rejected the Islam that Allah chose. Since that is impossible, it proves that the hypocrites' outward actions are not the true Islam. The true Islam is inward submission (inqiyad) and surrender (istislam). Its reality is the religion itself, not mere outward displays. Further evidence is from the verse in Al-Hujurat where Allah tells the Prophet not to accept their outward claim of submission as a favor, implying that real Islam is something deeper.

Misconception: Some people think that merely saying 'we have submitted' or performing outward rituals is sufficient to be a true Muslim, even if the heart is not submitted.
Correction: Maturidi shows that hypocrites do exactly that but are not true Muslims; real Islam requires inner submission (inqiyad) and surrender (istislam) of the heart.

Key Takeaway
True Islam is the inner submission of the heart, not merely outward actions or declarations.
