The Identity of Iman and Islam
Maturidi argues that iman and islam are identical using Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that iman (faith) and islam (submission) are identical in reality, based on Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Iman and Islam are one reality, not separate.

Imam Maturidi addresses a common distinction between inward faith and outward submission. Through a series of Quranic proof-texts, he argues that they are identical. This lesson follows his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the multiple Quranic citations.
2
Identify the key Quranic references
Locate the verses Maturidi uses: 49:17, 3:85-86, and 2:136. Note how he connects them to prove identity.
Each verse is used to refute a different angle of separation.
3
Understand Maturidi's principle about names
Maturidi states that names are instituted for identifying people regarding obligations and promises. Since the Quran uses 'iman' and 'islam' interchangeably, they must refer to the same reality.
This principle is key to his conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسلام ما أظهروا فقد كان ذلك ، كيف قال : إن كنتم صادقين ﴾ [الحجرات، ١٧/٤٩]. ثم فيه أنه جعلهم مسلمين كما قال ، أن هدوا للإيمان لا بما أظهروا . ثبت أن الإيمان هو الإسلام. وكذلك قال: ومن يبتغ غير الإسلام دينا فلن يقبل منه ﴾ [آل عمران، ٨٥/٣]، ثم بين ذلك الدين الذي هو الإسلام وقال : كيف يهدى الله قوما كفروا بعد إيمانهم ﴾ [آل عمران، ٨٦/٣] الآية، صيّر ذلك لم يُقبل دينا غير الإيمان الذي وصف، ثم جعلهم مبدلين دين الإسلام بالكفر بعد الإيمان ليعلموا أنهما واحد. مع ما كان فيما تقدم كفاية من قوله : قولوا آمنا بالله وما أنزل إلينا إلى قوله : مسلمون . والأصل عندنا أن الأسماء إنما جعلت لمعرفة أهلها فيما أُريدوا بأمور جُعِلت لهم وعليهم، وفيما وعدوا وأُوعدوا. ثم لم يكن أحد يخير فيما جرى آية الذكر باسم الإيمان أو الإسلام ممن ينتحل دين الإسلام - في اقتضاء الذكر إياه من حيث الاسم. ثبت أن حقيقتهما واحد وأن من يروم التفريق بينهما من بعيد يخترع. ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى. وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وآله الطيبين الطاهرين.
Islam is what they manifested, then that was so, as He said: 'If you are truthful' [Al-Hujurat 49:17]. Then in it He made them Muslims as He said, that they were guided to faith, not by what they manifested. So it is established that faith (iman) is Islam (islam). And likewise He said: 'And whoever seeks a religion other than Islam, it will never be accepted from him' [Al-Imran 3:85], then He explained that religion which is Islam and said: 'How shall Allah guide a people who disbelieved after their belief?' [Al-Imran 3:86] the verse. He made that no religion other than the faith which He described is accepted, then He made them exchange the religion of Islam for disbelief after faith, so that they know that they are one. And what was previously sufficient from His saying: 'Say, we believe in Allah and what has been revealed to us... to His saying: ...and we are Muslims' [Al-Baqara 2:136]. And the principle with us is that names are only made for knowing their people regarding what they are intended for by matters made for them and against them, and regarding what they are promised and threatened. Then no one who professes the religion of Islam can be given a choice regarding what the verse of remembrance mentions by the name of faith or Islam – in the requirement of the remembrance itself by the name. It is established that their reality is one, and that whoever seeks to differentiate between them from afar invents (falsehood). And there is no power except through Allah the Exalted. And may Allah bless our Master Muhammad and his pure and virtuous family.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text argument that iman (faith) and islam (submission) are identical in reality. Maturidi begins by addressing a potential objection: if islam were merely outward manifestation, then the verse 'If you are truthful' (Quran 49:17) would not have called them Muslims while asserting that they were guided to faith, not by their outward show. This establishes that faith is islam. He then cites Quran 3:85, which states that no religion other than islam is accepted, and immediately follows with Quran 3:86, which speaks of those who disbelieve after their faith. By linking these verses, Maturidi shows that the religion which is accepted (islam) is the same as the faith (iman) that was abandoned. He further references Quran 2:136, where the believers say 'we believe... and we are Muslims', again equating the two. Maturidi then articulates a principle: names are instituted to identify people in terms of obligations, promises, and threats. Since the Quran uses 'iman' and 'islam' interchangeably for the same people, they cannot be different. He concludes that their reality is one, and anyone who tries to separate them is inventing a false distinction.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الإسلام
حقيقة
الأسماء
الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think iman and islam are distinct, with iman being inward and islam outward.
Correction: Maturidi argues from Quranic proofs that they are identical; the Quran uses the terms interchangeably for the same people.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the relationship between iman and islam?
A) Iman is inward, islam is outward and they are different.
B) Iman and islam are identical in reality.
C) Islam is a subset of iman.
D) Iman is greater than islam.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi concludes that iman and islam are one reality, and any attempt to separate them is an innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself going through the motions of Islam—praying, fasting, giving—while your heart feels distant from genuine faith? How does Maturidi's argument that iman and islam are one reality challenge you to stop pretending they are separate and instead seek inner transformation that matches your outer practice?
?
If anyone who tries to separate iman from islam 'invents falsehood,' in what specific area of your life are you inventing a falsehood by acting Muslim but living as if your inner beliefs don't require outward change? What is one step you can take today to close that gap?
?
The Quran uses both 'iman' and 'islam' for the same people. Are you comfortable with the idea that your submission to Allah must be total and identical to your faith, leaving no room for a private 'spiritual but not religious' compartment? What would it cost you to fully embrace that unity?

Maturidi on the Possibility of Forgiveness for Major Sins
Maturidi establishes the priority of discussing major sins and argues for the possibility of forgiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's a fortiori argument that if major sins can be forgiven, minor sins are even more worthy of forgiveness, and why he prioritizes discussing major sins.

Core Idea
If major sins can be forgiven, minor sins are even more so.

Maturidi begins his discussion on grave sins by establishing a logical priority: if even major sins are subject to the possibility of forgiveness, then minor sins are even more likely to be forgiven. He also notes that this topic has caused significant disagreement in the Muslim community, making it essential to address. This passage sets the stage for his moderate position between Khawarij and Mu'tazila extremes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: Maturidi states his intention, gives a logical argument, and then a reason for focusing on this topic.
The argument uses the phrase 'إذا صارت بحيث احتمال العفو' meaning 'when they become such that forgiveness is possible'.
2
Identify the logical argument
Maturidi argues that if major sins can be forgiven, then minor sins are even more worthy of forgiveness. This is an a fortiori argument (qiyas al-awla). Think about why this reasoning makes sense.
3
Understand the context
Maturidi says that discussing this topic has caused clear disagreement in the community, so it is more appropriate to address it. Reflect on why this issue was controversial among early Islamic sects.
This connects to the historical debates about the fate of grave sinners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نذكر ما قيل في الكبائر ، فإنها إذ صارت بحيث احتمال العفو ، فما دونها الصغائر - أولى ، وبما للقول به فيها على الاختلاف أثر بين في الأمة ، فصرف الكلام إليه أحق
Then we mention what has been said concerning major sins. For when they become such that forgiveness is possible, then what is less than them – the minor sins – are more worthy [of forgiveness]. And because speaking about them has a clear effect of disagreement in the community, directing discussion to it is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage presents Maturidi's approach to the issue of major sins (kaba'ir). He states that if major sins are subject to the possibility of forgiveness (ihtimal al-'afw), then minor sins are even more worthy of forgiveness. The reasoning is that forgiveness for major sins is more controversial, so if it is possible, the lesser sins are a fortiori. He also notes that discussion of this topic has caused clear disagreement in the Muslim community, and therefore it is more appropriate to address it. This reflects Maturidi's method of engaging with disputed theological matters. The passage does not specify the punishment but implies that eventual forgiveness is possible for believers who commit major sins, contrary to the Khawarij and Mu'tazila who held that such sinners would be eternally punished.

Key Terms
الكبائر
الصغائر
العفو
الاختلاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi guarantees forgiveness for all major sins.
Correction: Maturidi only says forgiveness is possible (ihtimal al-'afw), not guaranteed. He leaves the matter to Allah's will.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude about minor sins in this passage?
A) They are never forgiven.
B) They are more worthy of forgiveness than major sins.
C) They are equal to major sins.
D) They are not worth discussing.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses an a fortiori argument to assert that if major sins can be forgiven, minor sins are even more worthy of forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Faith Remains: Maturidi's Refutation of Khawarij and Mu'tazila
Maturidi concludes that faith and the name of believer persist, refuting Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that faith does not cease with sin and why he labels those who deny this as obstinate.

Core Idea
Faith is never removed by sin; the believer's name remains.

Imam Maturidi concludes his discussion on faith and sin by affirming that the believer retains both faith and the name 'believer' even after committing major sins. This short but powerful passage explicitly refutes the positions of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, who taught that grave sins remove faith or render one an unbeliever. Maturidi warns that anyone who rejects this truth is simply being obstinate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the use of the conjunction 'ف' (so/thus).
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two foundational claims: first, that faith did not cease from the person; second, that the name of believer remains for him. Write these down.
These two claims are the pillars of Maturidi's conclusion.
3
Understand the refutation
Maturidi then uses these claims to invalidate the positions of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila. Ask yourself: how does the permanence of faith and the name contradict their teachings?
This step connects the claims to the broader sectarian debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فثبت أن الإيمان لم يزل عنه ، وأن الاسم قائم له . فيبطل بهذه الجملة التي من دفعها يعلم أنه مكابر معاند - ما قالت الخوارج والمعتزلة
So it is established that faith did not cease from him, and the name (of believer) remains for him. Thus, by this statement, whoever rejects it is known to be an obstinate contester, invalidates what the Khawarij and Mu'tazila said.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a concluding argument from Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid. He establishes two points: first, that faith does not leave a person who commits a sin; second, that the name 'believer' remains attributable to him. From these premises, he draws the conclusion that the claims of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila — who assert that grave sins remove faith entirely or render one an unbeliever — are invalidated. Anyone who rejects this conclusion is labelled an obstinate contester (mukābir). The argument follows a pattern common in kalam: estabishing a premise, then showing how it refutes a deviant position.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الاسم
المكابر
الخوارج
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sin completely removes faith and the name of believer.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that faith does not cease and the name remains, meaning sin does not nullify faith entirely, though it may affect its completeness.

Checkpoint

A) Faith ceases with sin
B) Faith does not cease and the name of believer remains
C) Faith is only for sinless people
D) Faith is removed by sin

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's conclusion that faith and the name of believer are permanent refutes those who claim sin removes faith entirely.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Maturidi's Definition of Iman as Inner Assent
Maturidi defines iman as inner assent, not verbal confession, citing Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Maturidi defines iman as inner assent (tasdiq) of the heart, not verbal confession, and how this is supported by Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Iman is what is in the heart, not just on the tongue.

Imam Maturidi presents a foundational definition of iman that distinguishes between inner faith and outward confession. Drawing on Quranic verses and a prophetic hadith, he argues that the essence of iman is the heart's assent, while verbal confession has worldly legal implications but does not reveal true belief. This lesson examines his evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let Maturidi's own words set the context.
Notice the two Quranic verses and the hadith about Usama.
2
Identify the two Quranic proofs
Find the two Quranic verses Maturidi cites (Q16:106 and Q49:14). Understand how each supports the distinction between inner assent and outer confession.
3
Understand the Usama incident
Read the story of Usama ibn Zayd. Reflect on why the Prophet rebuked him and what this teaches about judging others' faith.
This hadith illustrates the limits of judging inner faith based on outer actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإيمان هو التصديق بالقاب دون الإقرار باللسان لقوله تعالى: إلا من أكره وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان، وقوله: قالت الأعراب آمنا قل لم تؤمنوا ولكن قولوا أسلمنا ولما يدخل الإيمان في قلوبكم، وإن كان المقر بلسانه تجري عليه أحكام الإسلام لأن الإنسان لا سلطان له على قلوب الناس فهي من الغيوب. ففي الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله، فإذا قالوها عصموا مني دماءهم وأموالهم إلا بحقها وحسابهم على الله. وقد عاتب الرسول أسامة بن زيد حين قتل أحد الكفار في إحدى الغزوات بعد أن نطق بالشهادتين. قال رسول الله لأسامة: أقتلته بعد ما قال لا إله إلا الله، قال أسامة: إنما قالها تعوذا، قال رسول الله: هلا شققت عن قلبه؟ وقال: أومر أن أنقب عن قلوب الناس ولا أشق بطونهم.
And iman is tasdiq (assent) in the heart, not verbal confession, due to His saying: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is at peace with iman' (Q16:106), and His saying: 'The bedouins say: We believe. Say: You have not believed, but say: We have submitted, for faith has not yet entered your hearts' (Q49:14). And although the one who confesses with his tongue has the rulings of Islam applied to him, because man has no authority over people's hearts, for they are of the unseen. For in the report: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say: There is no god but Allah and I am the Messenger of Allah. When they say it, they protect from me their blood and their wealth except by its right, and their account is with Allah.' And the Messenger rebuked Usama ibn Zayd when he killed one of the disbelievers in one of the battles after he had uttered the two testimonies. The Messenger of Allah said to Usama: 'Did you kill him after he said: There is no god but Allah?' Usama said: 'He only said it as a shield.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Why did you not split open his heart?' And he said: 'Have I been commanded to dig into people's hearts and not split their bellies?'
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage defines iman according to Maturidi. He states that iman is essentially tasdiq (assent) in the heart, not verbal confession (iqrar bil-lisan). He supports this with two Quranic verses: Q16:106 which makes exception for one forced to utter disbelief while his heart is firm in iman, and Q49:14 which distinguishes between iman and islam, showing that the Bedouins are told they have only submitted outwardly, not believed inwardly. Then he clarifies that the outward confession does have legal consequences in this world (rulings of Islam apply), because we cannot judge hearts. He then cites a hadith describing the worldly criterion of protection from the Prophet's fighting (declaring shahada). Finally, he recounts the incident of Usama who killed a man after the man said shahada, and the Prophet rebuked him, saying 'Why did you not split open his heart?' meaning we cannot ascertain inner faith. This passage guards against over-reliance on outward confession for determining true iman, emphasizing inner assent.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الإقرار
اللسان
قلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi rejects any role of verbal confession in Islam.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that verbal confession has legal effects in this world (protection of life and property), but the essence of iman remains inner assent.

Checkpoint
What is the essence of iman according to Maturidi?
A) Verbal confession only.
B) Both verbal confession and inner assent.
C) Inner assent (tasdiq) only.
D) Actions only.

Key Takeaway
Iman is fundamentally the heart's assent; verbal confession serves as a worldly criterion but does not define true faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Prohibition of Exception in Declaring Faith
Maturidi prohibits saying 'I am a believer if God wills' because it implies doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi prohibits making an exception (istithna) when declaring one's faith, and the Quranic evidence he uses to support this ruling.

Core Idea
Declaring faith with 'if Allah wills' implies doubt, which contradicts the certainty of iman.

Maturidi addresses a common practice among some Muslims of saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' when asked about their faith. In this lesson, we will examine why he considers this practice prohibited, as it introduces doubt into a matter that should be certain. We will also see how he uses Quranic verses to support his position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source text and its literal translation carefully. Notice the concise style of Maturidi's argument.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the ruling and its basis
Find the core ruling: istithna is not allowed concerning iman. Understand the reason: because exception is used in cases of doubts and suspicions.
This links the prohibition to the nature of iman as certainty.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Maturidi cites three verses: Q49:15 (warning against doubt), Q2:285, and Q2:136 (decisive declarations). Consider how each supports the prohibition.
The verses show that iman is expressed with certainty, not conditionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز الاستثناء في الإيمان لأن الاستثناء يستعمل في موضع الشكوك والظنون وقد حذر الله تعالى من ذلك بقوله: ثم لم يرتابوا وقطع القول بالإيمان في قوله: آمن الرسول وقوله: قولوا آمنا بالله.
And exception (istithna) is not allowed concerning iman, because exception is used in cases of doubts and suspicions, and God Almighty warned against that with His saying: 'Then they did not doubt' (Q49:15), and He decisively declared iman in His saying: 'The Messenger believes' (Q2:285) and His saying: 'Say: We believe in Allah' (Q2:136).
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on making an exception (istithna) when professing one's iman. The practice some people had of saying 'I am a believer if God wills' is prohibited because istithna (saying 'in sha Allah') is used in contexts of doubt or uncertainty. Maturidi argues that iman is a matter of certainty, not doubt. He supports this with Quranic evidence: Q49:15 praises those who 'do not doubt,' and Q2:285 and Q2:136 show that the Quran expresses iman decisively without any conditional clause. Therefore, one should not qualify his declaration of iman with an exception, as that implies hesitation or uncertainty in one's faith. This passage guards against treating iman as something unsure.

Key Terms
الاستثناء
الشكوك
الظنون
الارتياب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Saying 'in sha Allah' when declaring faith is a sign of humility and recommended.
Correction: Maturidi prohibits it because it implies doubt in one's iman, which contradicts the certainty faith requires.

Checkpoint
Why is istithna (exception) in declaring iman prohibited according to Maturidi?
A) Because it is forbidden in all contexts.
B) Because iman is a matter of certainty, not doubt.
C) Because it implies associating partners with God.
D) Because it is a bid'ah.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that iman must be declared with certainty, without any conditional phrase that suggests doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Imagine you are tested with a severe trial—would your declaration of iman remain unconditionally firm, or would the conditional 'if Allah wills' slip out as a safety net? Why do you think you might hesitate?
?
The Quran praises those who 'do not doubt' (Q49:15). Where in your life do you find yourself doubting not Allah's existence, but your own standing as a believer? How can you train your heart to speak of your iman with the same decisiveness as the Prophet and the early believers?

Iman as Affirmation of the Heart
Maturidi defines iman as heart affirmation and discusses kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Imam al-Maturidi, iman (faith) is solely affirmation by the heart, not verbal declaration, and that committers of major sins remain believers.

Core Idea
Iman is in the heart, not on the tongue.

This lesson delves into the foundational Maturidi definition of iman. Imam al-Maturidi argues that true faith is internal conviction, distinguishing it from mere verbal submission. He supports this with Quranic verses and the Prophet's treatment of outward declarations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about kufr and major sins
Notice how Maturidi defines kufr as denial and states that a major sinner is still a believer.
2
Identify the definition of iman
Find the sentence where iman is defined as tasdiq bil-qalb. Contrast with iqrar bil-lisan.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
Look at the two verses cited and see how they separate faith from mere words.
4
Understand the practical ruling
Read the hadith about Usama. It shows that we accept outward Islam and cannot judge hearts.
This reinforces that iman is hidden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكفر عنها مع إبقاء اسم الايمان . وليس الكفر في العرف إلا بمعنى التكذيب ، ومرتكب الكبيرة وقت ارتكابها مصندق غير مكذب ، يرجو عفوه ويخاف عذابه . شأن علام والإيمان هو التصديق بالقاب دون الإقرار باللسان لقوله تعالى : " إِلَّا مَن أُكْرِة وَقَلْبُهُ مطمئن بِالإِيمَانِ " ، وقوله : " قَالَتِ الأَعْرَابُ آمَنَّا قُلْ لَمْ تُؤْمِنُوا وَلَكِن قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا وَلَمَّا يَدْخُلَ الإيمانُ في قُلُوبِكُم " ، وإن كان المقر بلسانه تجري عليه أحكام الإسلام لأن الإنسان لا سلطان له على قلوب الناس فهي من الغيوب. ففي الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله ، فإذا قالوها عصموا مني دماءهم وأسوالهم إلا بحقها وحسابهم على الله . وقد عاتب الرسول أسامة بن زيد حين قتل أحد الكفار في إحدى الغزوات بعد أن نطق بالشهادتين . قال رسول الله لأسامة : أقتلته بعد ما قال : لا إله إلا الله ، قال أسامة : إنما قالها تعوذا ، قال رسول الله : هلا شققت عن قلبه ؟ وقال : أومر أن أنقب عن قلوب الناس ولا أشق بطونهم . ولا يجوز الاستثناء في الإيمان لأن الاستثناء يستعمل في موضع الشكوك والظنون وقد حذر الله تعالى من ذلك بقوله : " ثُمَّ لَمْ يَرْتَابُوا " وقطع القول بالإيمان في قوله : " آمن الرسول " وقوله : " قُولُوا آمَنَّا بِاللهِ ".
And He pardons them while preserving the name of faith. And disbelief (kufr) in common usage is only by way of denial (takdhib). And the committer of a major sin at the time of committing it is a confirmer (musaddiq), not a denier (mukadhdhib); he hopes for His forgiveness and fears His punishment. Shan 'Allam. And faith (iman) is affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart, not declaration (iqrar) by the tongue, because of His saying: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is secure in faith' (16:106), and His saying: 'The bedouins said, "We have believed." Say, "You have not believed; but say, "We have submitted," and faith has not yet entered into your hearts"' (49:14). And even if one declares with his tongue, the rulings of Islam are applied to him, because man has no authority over the hearts of people, for they are among the unseen. For in the report: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say there is no god but Allah and that I am the messenger of Allah; when they say it, they protect from me their blood and their property except by their right, and their account is with Allah.' And the Messenger rebuked Usama ibn Zaid when he killed one of the disbelievers in one of the campaigns after he had uttered the two testimonies. The Messenger of Allah said to Usama: 'Did you kill him after he said "There is no god but Allah"?' Usama said: 'He only said it out of fear.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Why did you not split open his heart?' And he said: 'Have I been commanded to dig into people's hearts and not to split open their bellies?' And it is not permissible to make an exception (istithna) in faith, because an exception is used in cases of doubt and suspicion, and Allah Almighty has warned against that by His saying: 'Then they do not doubt' (49:15), and He made faith definitive in His saying: 'The Messenger believes' (2:285), and His saying: 'Say, "We believe in Allah"' (2:136).
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage defines the key concepts of iman (faith) and kufr (disbelief) and argues that iman is tasdiq bil-qalb (affirmation by the heart) rather than iqrar bil-lisan (declaration by the tongue). The author begins by stating that disbelief in common usage means denial (takdhib), and that a major sinner is not a denier. He then defines iman as heart affirmation, citing Quranic verses that separate true faith from mere verbal submission. He also discusses the practical ruling that verbal declaration suffices for the application of Islamic laws, as the Prophet was commanded to accept outward Islam. The incident of Usama ibn Zaid shows that interior cannot be judged. The passage concludes by forbidding making exceptions in one's statement of faith, as that implies doubt, whereas faith must be certain.

Key Terms
iman
kufr
tasdiq
iqrar
takdhib

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that iman includes verbal declaration (iqrar) as an essential component.
Correction: Maturidi argues that iman is solely affirmation by the heart; verbal declaration is only a condition for worldly rulings, not part of the essence of faith.

Checkpoint

A) Declaration by tongue
B) Affirmation by heart
C) Both heart and tongue
D) Actions

Key Takeaway
Iman is internal conviction of the heart, not outward speech; major sins do not remove one from faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada with your tongue, does your heart truly affirm it? If you were to die tonight, would you be confident that your heart's affirmation is genuine before Allah?
?

?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

Prohibition of Exceptions in Iman
Maturidi forbids making exceptions in iman and provides proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why making exceptions (istithna) in one's statement of faith is prohibited and how it relates to certainty.

Core Idea
Faith must be absolute; no room for doubt.

Having established that iman is heart affirmation, Maturidi now addresses a critical issue: can one say 'I am a believer if Allah wills'? He argues that such exceptions imply doubt, which contradicts the certainty required for faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the prohibition statement
Note the clear ruling: 'It is not permissible to make an exception in faith.'
2
Understand the reasoning
Maturidi explains that exceptions are used in cases of doubt, so they have no place in faith.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Look at the verses cited: they emphasize certainty and definitive statements of faith.
49:15 praises those who do not doubt; 2:285 and 2:136 use definitive language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكفر عنها مع إبقاء اسم الايمان . وليس الكفر في العرف إلا بمعنى التكذيب ، ومرتكب الكبيرة وقت ارتكابها مصندق غير مكذب ، يرجو عفوه ويخاف عذابه . شأن علام والإيمان هو التصديق بالقاب دون الإقرار باللسان لقوله تعالى : " إِلَّا مَن أُكْرِة وَقَلْبُهُ مطمئن بِالإِيمَانِ " ، وقوله : " قَالَتِ الأَعْرَابُ آمَنَّا قُلْ لَمْ تُؤْمِنُوا وَلَكِن قُولُوا أَسْلَمْنَا وَلَمَّا يَدْخُلَ الإيمانُ في قُلُوبِكُم " ، وإن كان المقر بلسانه تجري عليه أحكام الإسلام لأن الإنسان لا سلطان له على قلوب الناس فهي من الغيوب. ففي الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله ، فإذا قالوها عصموا مني دماءهم وأسوالهم إلا بحقها وحسابهم على الله . وقد عاتب الرسول أسامة بن زيد حين قتل أحد الكفار في إحدى الغزوات بعد أن نطق بالشهادتين . قال رسول الله لأسامة : أقتلته بعد ما قال : لا إله إلا الله ، قال أسامة : إنما قالها تعوذا ، قال رسول الله : هلا شققت عن قلبه ؟ وقال : أومر أن أنقب عن قلوب الناس ولا أشق بطونهم . ولا يجوز الاستثناء في الإيمان لأن الاستثناء يستعمل في موضع الشكوك والظنون وقد حذر الله تعالى من ذلك بقوله : " ثُمَّ لَمْ يَرْتَابُوا " وقطع القول بالإيمان في قوله : " آمن الرسول " وقوله : " قُولُوا آمَنَّا بِاللهِ ".
And He pardons them while preserving the name of faith. And disbelief (kufr) in common usage is only by way of denial (takdhib). And the committer of a major sin at the time of committing it is a confirmer (musaddiq), not a denier (mukadhdhib); he hopes for His forgiveness and fears His punishment. Shan 'Allam. And faith (iman) is affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart, not declaration (iqrar) by the tongue, because of His saying: 'Except one who is forced while his heart is secure in faith' (16:106), and His saying: 'The bedouins said, "We have believed." Say, "You have not believed; but say, "We have submitted," and faith has not yet entered into your hearts"' (49:14). And even if one declares with his tongue, the rulings of Islam are applied to him, because man has no authority over the hearts of people, for they are among the unseen. For in the report: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say there is no god but Allah and that I am the messenger of Allah; when they say it, they protect from me their blood and their property except by their right, and their account is with Allah.' And the Messenger rebuked Usama ibn Zaid when he killed one of the disbelievers in one of the campaigns after he had uttered the two testimonies. The Messenger of Allah said to Usama: 'Did you kill him after he said "There is no god but Allah"?' Usama said: 'He only said it out of fear.' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Why did you not split open his heart?' And he said: 'Have I been commanded to dig into people's hearts and not to split open their bellies?' And it is not permissible to make an exception (istithna) in faith, because an exception is used in cases of doubt and suspicion, and Allah Almighty has warned against that by His saying: 'Then they do not doubt' (49:15), and He made faith definitive in His saying: 'The Messenger believes' (2:285), and His saying: 'Say, "We believe in Allah"' (2:136).
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage defines the key concepts of iman (faith) and kufr (disbelief) and argues that iman is tasdiq bil-qalb (affirmation by the heart) rather than iqrar bil-lisan (declaration by the tongue). The author begins by stating that disbelief in common usage means denial (takdhib), and that a major sinner is not a denier. He then defines iman as heart affirmation, citing Quranic verses that separate true faith from mere verbal submission. He also discusses the practical ruling that verbal declaration suffices for the application of Islamic laws, as the Prophet was commanded to accept outward Islam. The incident of Usama ibn Zaid shows that interior cannot be judged. The passage concludes by forbidding making exceptions in one's statement of faith, as that implies doubt, whereas faith must be certain.

Correction: Maturidi argues this implies doubt, which is prohibited. Faith must be stated with certainty.

Faith must be expressed with certainty; exceptions imply doubt and are therefore prohibited.

Nullification of Command and Prohibition
Reductio argument against denying command to the disbeliever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's reductio argument that denying the command to the disbeliever at the moment of disbelief leads to the nullification of all command and prohibition.

Core Idea
If the disbeliever isn't commanded now, he's never commanded — and command becomes meaningless.

This passage presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum against a claim that the disbeliever is not commanded at the moment of disbelief. Imam Maturidi shows that such a position logically destroys the very institution of divine command and prohibition. The argument is central to the Maturidi insistence on universal moral accountability and the ongoing obligation to believe.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's claim
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the opponent's claim that the disbeliever is commanded to faith based on a power that existed before his disbelief.
The opponent seems to separate power from command temporally.
2
Identify Maturidi's first response
Maturidi points out that all Muslims agree the disbeliever is capable (qawī) of his disbelief at the moment. So the same logic applied to command should apply to power — they are one in meaning.
This exposes inconsistency in the opponent's reasoning.
3
Follow the reductio
Maturidi then shows that if the disbeliever is not commanded or prohibited at his current moment, then he is also not commanded in any future moment, ad infinitum.
This leads to the complete nullification of command and prohibition.
4
Understand the conclusion
The argument concludes that the opponent's view renders command and prohibition void, because the command would forever apply to a time when the person is not compliant — an impossibility.
Thus the disbeliever must be commanded at every moment of his disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم أن الكافر مأمور به فى حال كفره بالإيمان ، تأويله أن النهى تقدمه ، فيلزمه أن يقول : هو قادر عليه بقدرة تقدمت ، وزعم أنه ترك في الأول لقول المسلمين ، ووجه إلى ما أمكن ، وفى الآخر لم يقل نقول نحن وبالله التوفيق : لا أحد من المسلمين إلا وعنده أن الكافر في حال كفره قوى على ما هو عليه ، فقل فى القدرة مثل الذى قلت في الأمر ، إذ المعنى واحد في القول والتحصيل جميعاً . ثم تأويله قول المسلمين على وجه يعلم كل مسلم أن ذلك لم يخطر بباله ، بل لا يحتمله عقل كل أحد لو ألزم يجهد / أن يكون كافر ليس بمنهى عن كفره ، وليس بمأمور فى حاله ، فإذا لم يكن في وقته مأمورا منهيا لما هو فيه ولا لضده ، وهو كذلك فى الوقت الثاني والثالث إلى ما لا نهاية له ، وفى ذلك بطلان الأمر والنهي على التحقيق : لأنه يكون الأمر بالشيء للوقت الثانى والنهى عن ضده ، وهو في ذلك ليس بمؤتمر بالأمر ولا مرتكب النهى ؛ لأنه ليس ذلك ، وكذا فى كل وقت ، فيبطل حق الأمر والنهي عن الفعل أبدا ، ويرجع إلى غير حال الائتمار والارتكاب ، وذلك بعيد
And he claimed that the disbeliever is commanded during his disbelief to have faith, its interpretation that the prohibition preceded him, so he must say: he is able to it by a power that preceded. And he claimed that he left in the first [part] the saying of the Muslims, and directed as much as possible, and in the latter he did not say. We say and by Allah is success: There is none among the Muslims except that he holds that the disbeliever during his disbelief is capable of that which he is upon, so say concerning power the like of what you said concerning the command, for the meaning is one in statement and realization together. Then his interpretation of the saying of the Muslims in a way that every Muslim knows that that never occurred to his mind, rather the intellect of everyone cannot bear it if he is compelled/exerted to be that a disbeliever is not prohibited from his disbelief, and not commanded during his state. So if he is not at his time commanded or prohibited regarding what he is in nor its opposite, and he is likewise in the second time and third ad infinitum, then in that is the nullification of command and prohibition in reality: because the command would be for something for the second time and the prohibition for its opposite, and he in that is not compliant with the command nor committing the prohibition, because that is not [the case], and likewise in every time, so the right of command and prohibition regarding the action is nullified forever, and it returns to a state not of compliance and commission, and that is far.
Source pages p. 872

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent's claim regarding the command to the disbeliever. It argues that if the disbeliever were not commanded at the very moment of his disbelief, then command and prohibition would be rendered invalid. The argument follows: The opponent interprets the command to the disbeliever as based on a power that existed before his disbelief (a power that has since passed). The author responds that all Muslims agree that the disbeliever during his disbelief is capable (qawī) of what he is doing, so the same reasoning applied to command should be applied to power—both are one in meaning. Then the author shows the absurd consequence: if the disbeliever is not commanded at his time, then he is also not commanded at any future time, leading to the nullification of command and prohibition entirely, because the command would be for a time when he is not compliant. This is impossible (ba‘īd). The structure is a reductio ad absurdum: starting from the opponent's premise, it leads to the dissolution of shar‘ī obligations.

الأمر (command)
النهي (prohibition)
الكافر (disbeliever)
الإيمان (faith)
القدرة (power)
الائتمار (compliance)
الارتكاب (commission)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The disbeliever is only commanded when he has the power to obey, not at the moment of disbelief.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the disbeliever is commanded at every moment, otherwise all commands become void.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude if the disbeliever were not commanded at the moment of his disbelief?
A) He is still commanded later
B) Command and prohibition become null
C) He is commanded but not prohibited
D) The command applies to his past state

Key Takeaway
The disbeliever is commanded to believe at every moment, otherwise command and prohibition lose their meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever excused your own sin by telling yourself that you were not really commanded at that moment because you felt unable to obey? How does this lesson's infinite regress argument strip away that excuse?
?
When you see someone persisting in disbelief or sin, do you assume they are not accountable because they seem powerless to change? What does Maturidi's claim that the disbeliever is capable of his disbelief demand of your attitude toward them?
?
If you truly believe that God's command applies to every moment of your life, even when you feel weak or resistant, what one area of obedience have you been postponing until you feel 'ready'? Will you act on it today?

The Claim That All Sins Remove One from Faith
Maturidi introduces the issue and presents the claim that all sins cause exit from faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the view that all sins are equal in causing exit from faith and the scriptural basis used by its proponents.

Core Idea
All sins are disobedience, so all sins remove you from faith — Maturidi will refute this.

Maturidi opens a new topic on the status of grave sinners. He presents a position held by some scholars that all sins, regardless of size, cause a person to exit faith. This view relies on Quranic verses that speak generally about disobedience, treating all sins as equally deserving of eternal punishment. This lesson sets up the claim that Maturidi will later refute.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice that the passage ends mid-sentence with 'And His saying, Exalted is He:' indicating that more scriptural evidence is being introduced.
This passage is the opening of a new discussion.
2
Identify the key verses cited
Maturidi mentions two partial verses: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger...' (4:14) and 'It is not for a believing man or a believing woman...' (33:36). Identify these verses in your memory or look them up.
These verses are used by proponents of the view.
3
Understand the reasoning
The reasoning is that all sins share the name 'disobedience' ('isyan). Therefore, they argue, all sins equally necessitate the name 'misguidance' (dalal) and eternal punishment in Hell. This is a straight line from sin → disobedience → misguidance → eternal damnation.
This is not Maturidi's own view; he is presenting an argument to refute.
4
Recognize the role of this passage in the larger discussion
This passage introduces a position that Maturidi will systematically refute in subsequent lessons. Note that it is a claim, not a conclusion.
The commentary clarifies that Maturidi opposes this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في مقترفي الذنوب وهل يخرجون بذنوبهم من الإيمان. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : تكلم الناس فى محل الذنوب وتسمية مقترفيها، فجمع بينها قوم في الإخراج من الإيمان بقوله : وَمَنْ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ ، وقوله : وَمَا كَانَ لِمُؤْمِن وَلَا مُؤْمِنَةٍ ، والذنوب كلها في تحقيق اسم العصيان واحد، فعلى ذلك في تحقيق اسم الضلال وايجاب الخلود [في النار] . وقوله تعالى :
A question concerning those who commit sins: do they exit faith by their sins? Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: People have spoken about the status of sins and the naming of their committers. Some people lumped them together in causing exit from faith by His saying: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger...' and His saying: 'It is not for a believing man or a believing woman...' All sins are one in the realization of the name of disobedience. Likewise they are one in the realization of the name of misguidance and the necessitation of eternal [stay in the Fire]. And His saying, Exalted is He:
Source pages p. 922

Commentary
This passage opens a new topic: the ruling on grave sinners and whether they leave the fold of faith by committing sins. Maturidi (Abu Mansur) states that people have discussed the status of sins and the labels for those who commit them. Some scholars (likely the Khawarij and possibly earlier Mu'tazila) treat all sins as equal in causing exit from faith. They cite Quranic verses that speak generally about disobedience, such as 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His messenger' (4:14) and 'It is not for a believing man or a believing woman' (33:36). These verses, they argue, apply to any sin, since all sins are disobedience ('isyan). Therefore, they claim, every sin makes one a disobedient person, and thus a misguidant (dall) deserving eternal punishment in Hell. Maturidi notes that according to this reasoning, all sins are unified in the realization of the name of disobedience, and therefore also unified in the realization of the name of misguidance and the necessitation of eternal damnation. The passage ends with 'And His saying, Exalted is He:' which indicates that Maturidi is about to quote more verses or respond to this argument, but the text in this window cuts off. This lesson thus presents the initial claim that all sins remove one from faith, which Maturidi will refute in subsequent lessons.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think this passage represents Maturidi's own view.
Correction: This passage actually presents the view that Maturidi will refute. He is setting up the argument of his opponents.

Checkpoint

B) All sins are equal in causing exit from faith because they all share the name of disobedience.
C) Sins do not affect one's faith at all.
D) Only sins against the prophets remove one from faith.

Key Takeaway
This passage presents the opposing view that all sins are equal in causing exit from faith, a position Maturidi will refute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a sin you tend to treat as 'small' or insignificant. Does the argument that all sins are equally disobedience convict you of trivializing any of them? What would it mean for your daily life to take every sin as seriously as a major one?

The Real Disagreement: What Removes Faith, Not the Threat
Maturidi clarifies that the disagreement is about what removes faith, not the threat itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Mu'tazila and early Murji'a actually agreed on the reality of eternal punishment for those who lose faith, and that their real dispute concerns what causes one to lose faith.

Core Idea
The threat is agreed; the dispute is over the exit from faith.

Maturidi addresses a common misconception about the early theological debate on divine threat (al-wa'id). Many assume that the Mu'tazila and Murji'a disagreed about whether eternal punishment exists. In this brief passage, Maturidi shows that both groups actually affirmed eternal punishment for those who truly lose faith. The real point of contention, he explains, is about the criterion: what precisely removes a person from the state of faith? Understanding this reframes the entire discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the basic meaning.
Notice that both groups mention eternal punishment.
2
Identify the two groups and their shared position
Locate the positions of the Mu'tazila and the Murji'a (Husayn and others). Notice that both affirm eternal fire for those who lose faith.
The shared position is that the threat is real for those who deserve it.
3
Find Maturidi's core clarification
Look for the sentence where Maturidi states that the disagreement is not about the threat itself but about what removes from faith.
The key phrase is 'والاختلاف بين هؤلاء فيا به يخرج من الإيمان لا فى حق الوعيد'.
4
Reflect on the argumentative error
Consider why Maturidi says that using the threat as an argument in this question is an error. What is the correct focus?
This highlights the need to identify the correct point of debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت المعتزلة الوعيد يأخذ من أخرجه فعله عن الإيمان ، وكذلك قال حسين وجميع أهل الإرجاء إن كان من استحق بفعله زوال اسم الإيمان فهو كله في النار أبدا ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . والاختلاف بين هؤلاء فيا به يخرج من الإيمان لا فى حق الوعيد ، فالاحتجاج بأى الوعيد في المسألة خطأ
And the Mu'tazila said: The threat (al-wa'id) takes hold of the one whose action removes him from faith (al-iman). And likewise Husayn and all the people of irja' (al-irja') said: If someone deserves by his action the removal of the name of faith, then he is entirely in the Fire forever, and there is no power except by God. And the disagreement between these [groups] is concerning what removes from faith, not concerning the reality of the threat. So using the threat as an argument in this question is an error.
Source pages p. 922

Commentary
This passage states the position of the Mu'tazila and the Murji'a (ahl al-irja') regarding the divine threat (al-wa'id) of eternal punishment. The Mu'tazila hold that the threat applies to anyone whose action causes him to exit faith. Husayn and the Murji'a similarly affirm that if a person, due to his action, deserves that the name 'faith' be removed from him, then he remains in the Fire forever. Maturidi then clarifies that the real disagreement between these groups is not about whether the threat is real (both agree on eternal punishment for those who meet the condition), but rather about what specific action or state causes a person to exit faith. Therefore, arguing by simply citing the existence of the threat is a mistake; the debate must focus on the criterion (what removes faith).

Key Terms
الوعيد
الإيمان
الإرجاء
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Mu'tazila and Murji'a disagree on whether eternal punishment exists.
Correction: Both groups affirm eternal punishment for those who lose faith. The actual disagreement is about what action or state removes a person from faith.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the actual point of disagreement between the Mu'tazila and the Murji'a?
A) Whether eternal punishment exists
B) What removes a person from faith
C) Whether actions affect faith
D) The number of major sins

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila and Murji'a agreed on eternal punishment for those who lose faith; their dispute is about what causes loss of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to argue with a brother about a religious issue, would you first ensure you know what the real point of disagreement is, or do you often argue past each other? Will you commit today to listening more carefully to understand the actual difference?
?
This lesson shows that two major groups agreed on the eternal Fire for those who lose faith. What if you are more concerned about whether punishment is real than about what actually endangers your own faith? Will you ask Allah to show you the actions that truly remove faith, so you can guard against them?
?
Both sides used the 'threat' argument, but it was a mistake. Are there arguments you use in your own spiritual life that miss the deeper issue? Will you pray for clarity to see what truly matters for your salvation?

Do Sinners Exit Faith? The Group's Argument and Forgiveness
Maturidi presents the group argument for expulsion from faith and two ways to forgive sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that all sins expel from faith and two explanations for forgiveness of major and minor sins.

Core Idea
Sins are serious, but repentance and forgetfulness can bring forgiveness.

Maturidi opens a critical question: do sins force a person out of faith? Some scholars argue that any disobedience, great or small, removes one from faith. They cite verses equating sin with misguidance and eternal punishment. However, Maturidi then presents two ways to understand delicate verses about avoiding major sins, showing that repentance wipes away major sins and forgetfulness excuses minor ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very compact style here.
2
Identify the group's argument
Find the verses the group uses to argue that any disobedience expels from faith. Notice how they claim all sins are equal in being 'disobedience' and 'misguidance'.
3
Understand the two ways for forgiveness
The passage presents two ways (wajhan) to explain the verse about avoiding major sins. One is repentance, the other is minor sins committed inadvertently. Identify each and note the supporting verses.
The first way cites 'except those who repent'; the second cites verses on unintentional actions.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: does the existence of these two ways mean the group's argument is weakened? Or does it provide a nuanced view?
This connects to the broader question of whether sin can negate faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في مقترفي الذنوب وهل يخرجون بذنوبهم من الايمان
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : تكلم الناس فى محل الذنوب وتسمية مقترفيها ، فجمع بينها قوم في الإخراج من الإيمان بقوله : وَمَنْ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ . وقوله : وَمَا كَانَ لِمُؤْمِن وَلَا مُؤْمِنَةٍ ، والذنوب كلها في تحقيق اسم العصيان واحد ، فعلى ذلك في تحقيق اسم الضلال وايجاب الخلود [في النار] . وقوله تعالى : إِنْ تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ نخرج على وجهين أحدهما أن يكفر بالتوبة لقوله : ويخلد فيه مهاناً إلا من تاب . وقوله تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا توبُوا إِلَى اللهِ توبةً نصوحا عسى ربُّكُمْ أَنْ يُكَفِّر عَنْكُم سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ ... وغير من الآيات . والثانى أن تكون الصغائر منها التي تقع على السهو والغفلة فهى المغفورة بما قال تعالى : لَا يُؤَاخِذْ كُم اللهُ باللغْوِ فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ ، وقال : وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ فِيمَا أَخْطَأْتُمْ به . وما جاء من الخبر بالعفو عنه منهم له اسم الكفر بوجهين : أحدهما بقوله : لَا يَصْلَاهَا إِلَّا الأَشْقَى الَّذِي كذب وتولى ، وقال : وَهَلْ نُجَازِي إِلَّا الكَفُور ، وقال : مَنْ يَعْمَلْ سوءا يجز به ، وقال : وَمَنْ جاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَلَا يُجْزَى إِلَّا مِثْلَهَا ، وقال : وَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا يَرَهُ . فأثبت الجزاء فيا صغر منه ، وأخبر أنه لا يجازي إلا الكفور ولا يصليها إلا من ذكر ، مع ما قال الله تعالى : إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يُؤْذُونَ اللهَ وَرَسُولَهُ . وكل عاص فهو يؤدى رسول الله ولا قوة إلا بالله . والثانى أن عقد إيمان كل مؤمن أن لا يعصى الله فيما أمره ونهاه ، فمن عصاه ما كان اعتقاده كان موقوفا على ما يظهر بالابتلاء بقوله : لم يف به
Question concerning those who commit sins and whether they exit faith by their sins. Abu Mansur (may God have mercy on him) said: People have spoken about the status of sins and the naming of those who commit them. A group gathered them together in expulsion from faith by His saying: 'And whoever disobeys God and His Messenger...' and His saying: 'And it is not for a believing man or a believing woman...' and all sins are one in the verification of the name of disobedience, and likewise in the verification of the name of misguidance and the affirmation of eternity [in the Fire]. And His saying the Exalted: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden...' proceeds on two ways: One of them is that [sin] is expiated by repentance, by His saying: 'And he will remain therein disgraced, except those who repent.' And His saying the Exalted: 'O you who have believed, repent to God with sincere repentance; perhaps your Lord will remove from you your misdeeds...' and other verses. And the second is that the minor sins that occur out of forgetfulness and inattention are forgiven by what He said the Exalted: 'God does not punish you for what is unintentional in your oaths...' and He said: 'And there is no blame upon you concerning what you have mistaken...' And what came of the report about forgiveness for them... Among them (the group) there is a name of disbelief in two ways: One of them: by His saying: 'None will enter it except the most wretched who denies and turns away,' and He said: 'And do We recompense except the ingrate?' and He said: 'Whoever does evil will be recompensed for it,' and He said: 'And whoever comes with a bad deed will not be recompensed except its like,' and He said: 'And whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.' So He affirmed recompense for the small of it, and He informed that He does not recompense except the ingrate and none enters it except whom He mentioned, along with what God said the Exalted: 'Indeed, those who harm God and His Messenger...' And every disobedient person harms God's Messenger, and there is no power except by God. And the second is that the covenant of faith of every believer is that he not disobey God in what He commanded and forbade him, so whoever disobeys Him, his conviction was suspended on what appears by trial, by His saying: 'he did not fulfill it'.
Source pages p. 922

Commentary
This passage opens a new question (mas'ala) about the status of those who commit sins and whether they thereby exit faith. Maturidi reports that some scholars group all sins together and use verses like 'Whoever disobeys God and His Messenger' (Q 4:14) and 'It is not for a believing man or a believing woman' (Q 33:36) to argue that any sin expels from faith, since all sins equally constitute disobedience and misguidance, and thus lead to eternal punishment. However, Maturidi then introduces two ways (wajhan) to understand the verse 'If you avoid the major sins...' (Q 4:31). The first way is that repentance (tawba) expiates sin, citing verses like 'he will remain disgraced except those who repent' (Q 25:69) and 'Repent to God with sincere repentance' (Q 66:8). The second way is that minor sins (al-sagha'ir) committed inadvertently or forgetfully are forgiven, citing verses about unintentional oaths (Q 2:225) and mistakes (Q 33:5). The passage then shifts to a different argument: some give the label of 'disbelief' (kufr) to sin in two ways. One way is using verses that restrict punishment to the ungrateful (kafur) and the most wretched, implying that only disbelievers are punished eternally (e.g., Q 92:15-16, Q 34:17, Q 4:123, Q 6:160, Q 99:8). These verses show that recompense is for small things, but only the ungrateful are recompensed. Also, those who harm God and His Messenger (Q 33:57) are cursed, and every disobedient person harms the Messenger. The second way is that the very covenant (عقد) of faith obligates a believer not to disobey, so if someone disobeys, his faith was conditional upon fulfilling the covenant, and failure means he did not uphold it. The passage ends abruptly with 'he said: he did not fulfill it.'

Key Terms
الذنوب
المقترفون
الإيمان
الكبائر
الصغائر
التوبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Maturidi outright rejects the idea that sins can lead to exit from faith.
Correction: Maturidi presents the group's argument as a serious view, then balances it with two ways of forgiveness. He does not dismiss the possibility of expulsion, but offers nuance.

Checkpoint
According to the first way (أحدهما) that explains the verse about avoiding major sins, how are sins expiated?
A) By repentance (tawba)
B) By good deeds
C) By divine forgiveness without condition
D) By avoiding all sins

Key Takeaway
The group's argument uses verses on disobedience to show sin expels from faith, but Maturidi balances it with two ways of forgiveness through repentance and minor sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The group's argument uses verses on disobedience to claim that any sin leads to eternal punishment. Do you ever treat your own sins as if they are all equally damning, ignoring the doors of repentance and forgiveness that Allah has opened? What sin have you been most reluctant to bring to Allah in sincere repentance?
?
Maturidi mentions that minor sins from forgetfulness are forgiven. Have you ever despaired over a sin you committed unintentionally, forgetting that Allah's mercy covers even that? Will you now accept that forgiveness and move forward in trust, or will you continue to dwell in guilt?
?
The passage shows that repentance can expiate major sins. What major sin are you holding onto that you have not sincerely repented from? What is one concrete step you will take today to turn back to Allah and seek His forgiveness?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
4 min
When Is Sin Called Disbelief? Two Approaches
Maturidi presents two ways sin is called disbelief: through punishment verses and covenant violations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two ways in which sin is labeled as disbelief: through punishment verses and through the covenant of faith.

Core Idea
Sin can be called disbelief when it incurs divine punishment or breaks faith's covenant.

Maturidi continues with another perspective: some scholars give the name 'disbelief' to sin in two ways. First, by using verses that reserve eternal punishment for the ungrateful, implying that sinners share that destiny. Second, by arguing that the very act of sinning proves a failure to uphold the covenant of faith, effectively nullifying it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the shift in argument: from forgiveness to labeling sin as disbelief.
2
Identify the two ways
The passage explicitly says 'two ways' (wajhain). Find them and note how each is justified with Quranic verses.
3
Understand the first way: punishment verses
The first way uses verses that restrict eternal punishment to the 'most wretched' and 'ungrateful', implying that whoever is punished for sin is counted among them.
Verses cited: Q 92:15-16, Q 34:17, Q 4:123, Q 6:160, Q 99:8, and Q 33:57.
4
Understand the second way: covenant violation
The second way argues that the very covenant of faith obligates obedience, so disobedience proves the covenant was not fulfilled, thus the person is not a true believer.
The passage ends abruptly with 'he did not fulfill it', indicating the conclusion.

According to the second way, why is sin labeled as disbelief?

?
Your faith is a covenant with God that you will not disobey Him. Have you ever broken that covenant without repentance? What does that mean for your conviction—is it suspended until you obey again?

The Lying Claimant of Faith is a Kafir
Maturidi proves that a lying claimant of faith is a kafir via Quran and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that a person who falsely claims faith while being inwardly a disbeliever or hypocrite is a kafir, based on obedience to Satan.

Core Idea
A false claim of faith is kufr because it follows Satan.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi confronts the question of hypocrisy: can someone who says 'I believe' while lying be considered a believer? He argues decisively that such a person is a kafir, grounding his reasoning in Quranic verses and rational examination. The key is that a liar in faith is effectively obeying and worshipping Satan, which constitutes kufr.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the Quranic citations Maturidi uses.
2
Identify the Quranic proof texts
Maturidi cites two verses: 29:2 and 29:11. Understand how they establish that outward falsehood in belief warrants the name of kufr.
The verses test the sincerity of faith.
3
Follow the rational argument
See how Maturidi uses rational examination (النظر) to link falsehood in faith to obeying Satan, and thus to worshipping Satan, which is kufr.
Obedience to Satan is considered worship.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is clear: whoever worships Satan is a kafir. The liar in faith falls into this category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَحَسِبَ النَّاسُ أَنْ يُتْرَكُوا أَنْ يَقُولُوا آمَنَّا ، وَقَالَ : وَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ المُنَافِقِينَ ، في موضع آخر فثبت بذلك استحقاق اسم الكفر بما ظهر كذبه فيما أظهر من الاعتقاد ، والنظر يوجب ذلك بما هو بالذى مخالفا فيه من الله مجيب الشيطان إلى ما دعاه ومطيع له فيما أمره ، ومن ذلك وصفه فقد عبده ، ومن عبد الشيطان فهو كافر ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Do people think they will be left to say, 'We believe,' while they will not be tested? And He said, 'And He will surely know the hypocrites,' in another place. So it is established by that that the name of kufr is deserved because of the appearance of his falsehood in what he shows of belief. And rational examination necessitates that because he is, in what he opposes Allah in, responding to Satan's call and obeying him in what he commands. And because of that, he has described him, so he has worshipped him. And whoever worships Satan is a kafir. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage is a proof that a person who falsely claims faith while being inwardly a hypocrite or disbeliever is a kafir. Maturidi begins by citing Quranic verses: 'Do people think they will be left to say, "We believe," while they will not be tested?' (29:2) and 'And He will surely know the hypocrites' (29:11). He argues that the appearance of falsehood in one's professed belief warrants the name of kufr. Rational consideration (النظر) also supports this: the person who opposes Allah is responding to Satan and obeying him. Since he follows Satan, he has effectively worshipped Satan (from the perspective of obedience, as described in the Quran: 'Did I not command you, O children of Adam, that you not worship Satan?' (36:60)). And whoever worships Satan is a kafir. Thus the conclusion: the lying claimant is a kafir.

Key Terms
كفر
إيمان
شيطان
عبادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only inner disbelief matters for kufr, and outward falsehood in claiming faith does not make one a kafir.
Correction: Maturidi shows that outward falsehood in a claim of faith, as in hypocrisy, alone makes one a kafir because it involves following Satan.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the basis for judging a person a kafir in this passage?
A) Inner belief alone
B) Falsehood in outward claim of faith
C) Committing a major sin
D) Associating partners with Allah

Key Takeaway
A person who falsely claims faith is a kafir because their outward falsehood shows they are responding to Satan, which is a form of worship of Satan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever claimed to believe something with your tongue while your heart was indifferent or resistant? According to this lesson, that very act of falsehood makes you a kafir. Will you now search your heart for any such contradiction and repent before you are counted among those who worshipped Satan?
?
This lesson says that merely opposing Allah by a false claim is responding to Satan. In what areas of your life are you giving lip service to faith but your actions or inner thoughts actually obey Satan? What will you do today to align your inner and outer submission to Allah?
?
Maturidi argues that the lying claimant worships Satan because he obeys him. Is there any sin or habit in your life where you know you are obeying Satan? Reflect on how that makes you a worshipper of Satan, and pray for sincerity. Write down one practical step to break that obedience.

The Distinction Between Calling a Hypocrite a Mushrik or a Kafir
Maturidi reports the view that such a person is a mushrik due to his action, not his innate nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why some scholars label a hypocrite as a mushrik (associator) rather than a kafir (disbeliever), based on Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Hypocrisy's shirk is in action, not in innate nature.

Maturidi presents a nuanced position on the classification of hypocrites. While many call them kafirs, some scholars reserve the term 'mushrik' for them, arguing that their sin is one of action rather than original disposition. This lesson examines the Quranic basis for that view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp Maturidi's argument at a surface level.
Pay attention to the distinction between 'fi'l' (action) and 'quwwa' (innate power).
2
Identify the core argument
Understand why some scholars say the hypocrite is a mushrik: because his state is achieved by his action, not his original nature.
This is the key doctrinal point that sets this view apart.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
Look at the three verses Maturidi cites (18:110, 12:106, 4:48) and see how each supports the idea that shirk can be in action.
Notice how verse 12:106 shows that belief in Allah can coexist with shirk, implying shirk in deeds.

ومنهم من يسميه مشركا ، لا كافرا ، إنما صار إلى ما صار بالفعل لا بالقوة ، وقد قال الله تعالى : فَمَنْ كَانَ يَرْجُو لِقَاءَ رَبِّهِ فَلْيَعْمَلْ عَمَلًا صَالِحًا وَلَا يُشْرِكْ بِعِبَادَةِ رَبِّه أَحَدًا ، فجعل في العمل شركا ، وكذا تسمية أهل الشرك بما أشركوا في العبادة غير الله ، وذلك معنى قوله : وَمَا يُؤْمِنُ أَكْثَرُهُم بِاللَّهِ إِلَّا وَهُمْ مُشْرِكُونَ ، وقال : إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ ، وقد بينا إنما يُغفر من الذنوب هى التى كانت على الخطأ أو الإكراه كما جاء به الكتاب ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
And among them are those who call him a mushrik, not a kafir, saying that he only came to what he came to by action, not by [innate] power. And Allah said: 'So whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord, let him do righteous work and not associate anyone in the worship of his Lord.' So He made shirk in action. Likewise, the people of shirk are named by what they associated in worship besides Allah. And that is the meaning of His statement: 'And most of them do not believe in Allah except that they are mushrikoon.' And He said: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him.' And we have explained that only those sins are forgiven that are due to error or compulsion, as the Book has brought. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage presents an alternative view: some scholars call the hypocrite a mushrik (one who associates partners with Allah) rather than a kafir. Their reasoning is that the person's state is achieved by his action (الفعل) and not by his original nature (القوة). Maturidi then supports this with Quranic evidence: (18:110) commands doing righteous work and not associating any partner in worship, thus shirk can be in action. Also (12:106) states that most people are mushrikoon despite believing in Allah, meaning they commit shirk in their actions. And (4:48) emphasizes that Allah does not forgive shirk. Maturidi adds that they have previously explained that only sins committed by mistake or under compulsion are forgiven. The passage ends with the formula 'ولا قوة إلا بالله'. This shows that labeling such a person as mushrik highlights the aspect of associating others in worship through action.

Key Terms
كفر
شرك
فعل
قوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kafir and mushrik are synonymous terms.
Correction: Maturidi explains that mushrik can be a specific category: one who commits shirk in action while still believing in Allah, unlike a kafir who rejects faith entirely.

Checkpoint
Why do some scholars call the hypocrite a mushrik rather than a kafir?
A) Because he denies Allah
B) Because his state is due to his action, not his original nature
C) Because he does not believe in the Prophet
D) Because he commits major sins

Key Takeaway
Some scholars call the hypocrite a mushrik because his sin lies in his actions, not his original nature, as supported by Quranic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever performed an outwardly good act—like charity or prayer—while inwardly seeking praise or validation from others? How does Maturidi's point that shirk can occur in action force you to re-examine the sincerity of your own deeds today?
?
The verse 'most of them believe in Allah except that they are mushrikoon' (12:106) describes a state where correct belief coexists with associating partners in action. In what area of your life—work, relationships, or worship—do you find that your actions contradict your stated belief? What specific step will you take this week to align your deeds with your faith?
?
If you were to die tonight, would any of your actions be considered shirk—seeking someone's approval over Allah's, or relying on created means as if they were independent? What would you need to repent from to face your Lord with pure worship?
