Sins Do Not Remove Iman: Proof from Seeking Forgiveness
Maturidi defends the permanence of iman despite major sins using Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Quranic command for the Prophet to seek forgiveness for believers as proof that major sins do not remove a person from iman.

Core Idea
The command to seek forgiveness for believers proves they remain believers despite sin.

Maturidi addresses a critical debate in early Islamic theology: do major sins expel a person from iman? The Khawarij said yes, the Mu'tazila said the sinner is in an intermediate state. Maturidi presents a decisive proof from the Qur'an: Allah commanded the Prophet to seek forgiveness for the believers, which would be meaningless if they had lost their faith. In this passage, you will follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main proof
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that Maturidi first states his position, then presents a key proof: the command to seek forgiveness for believers.
The proof rests on three premises: (1) forgiveness is only for sinners, (2) believers are commanded to seek forgiveness, (3) therefore believers have sins yet remain believers.
2
Examine the logic of the proof
Maturidi argues that if the Prophet is commanded to seek forgiveness for believers, then those believers must have sins, and their iman is still intact. Otherwise, the command would imply they are mushrikeen or hypocrites, which is impossible.
He uses the prohibition of seeking forgiveness for mushrikeen and hypocrites as a contrast.
3
Understand the refutation of Khawarij and Mu'tazila
Maturidi explicitly states that this argument refutes both the Khawarij (who declare sinners kafir) and the Mu'tazila (who remove the name iman from sinners).
This connects the proof to the broader theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من قسم الذنوب قسمين : فجعل منها صغائر تغفر باجتناب الكبائر وبالعفو بالجزاء ، ونحو ذلك على اختلاف أقاويلهم، وهو قولنا في ألا يجوز إخراج صاحبها من الإيمان ، وفاسد مع الإيمان الخلود في النار ؛ لما فى الوعد بقوله : فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ ، وما جاءت به الآيات . فمن يعمل من الصالحات وهو مؤمن ، والوعد فى ذلك ، ثم الذى يمنع اسم الكفر في الحقيقة والشرك أوجه : أحدها أمر الله نبيه أن يستغفر له وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات ، ثم لا يحتمل الأمر به على اثبات كفر أو شرك بقوله : مَا كَانَ لِلنَّبِيِّ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ يَسْتَغْفِرُوا لِلمُشْرِكِينَ ، وبما أمره أن يستغفر للمؤمنين ، ومحال يأمره بالاستغفار باسم الإيمان وهو عنهم زائل ؛ لأنه قد حذره عن الاستغفار لأهل الشرك بما ذكرت ، ولأهل النفاق بقوله : سَيَقُولُ لَكَ المُخَلَّفُونَ مِنَ الأَعْرَابِ ... وقوله : سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِم اسْتَغْفَرَتْ لَهُمْ ، وتهيه إياه عن الصلاة ، فثبت أن أولئك الذين أمرهم بالاستغفار هم أهل الأيمان في الحقيقة . ثم لا يحتمل أن يؤمر بالاستغفار ولا ذنوب لهم ، أو كانت مغفورة لهم ؛ لأن الاستغفار هو طلب المغفرة ، وطلبها لمن قد غفر له كتمان نعمة الغفران ، وذلك كفران النعمة ، بل حق ذلك الشكر والحمد ، وما لا ذنب له ثمة فيخرج طلب المغفرة مخرج كفران العصمة ، والسؤال أن لا يجوز ؛ إذ تعذيب مثله في حكمه جود ، ثم لا يحتمل أن يكون رسول الله والملائكة يستغفرون لمن أمروا به ، ثم لا يجابون ، فيثبت بهذا أن لا يزول اسم الإيمان لكل ذنب ، وأن من الذنوب ما ليس بمغفور ، يغفر بالتوبة عنه ؛ إذ ليس في استغفار غير المذنب توبة . وفى ذلك نقض على المعتزلة في إزالتهم اسم الايمان بكل ذنب ليس بمغفور لصاحبه حتى يستغفر ، ونقض على الخوارج بما ذكرنا ، والله أعلم . وأيضا إن الله تعالى قال فى الذنوب التي لا يغفرها : سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِم اسْتَغْفَرَتْ لهم ، وعلى ذلك قال : وَتُوبُوا إلى اللهِ جَمِيعًا أَيُّهَا المُؤْمِنُونَ لَعَلَّكُم تُفْلِحُونَ ، وقال : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً نَصُوحًا ، فألزمهم إثبات الإيمان وأخبر أنه بالتوبة يغفر لهم ، وفى ذلك وجهان : أحدهما على التوبة مع
And among them are those who divided sins into two categories: they made among them minor sins that are forgiven by avoiding the major sins and by pardon through recompense, and so on according to the difference of their opinions. And this is our statement: that it is not permissible to remove its possessor from iman, and eternal abiding in the Fire is corrupt with iman, due to the promise in His statement: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' and what the verses have brought. So whoever does righteous deeds while he is a believer, and the promise is concerning that. Then what prevents the name of kufr in reality and shirk are aspects: one of them is the command of Allah to His Prophet to seek forgiveness for himself and for the believing men and believing women. Then it is not possible that this command implies establishing kufr or shirk, due to His statement: 'It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to seek forgiveness for the mushrikeen' and because He commanded him to seek forgiveness for the believers. And it is impossible that He commands him to seek forgiveness in the name of iman while it has departed from them, because He has warned him against seeking forgiveness for the people of shirk as mentioned, and for the people of hypocrisy by His statement: 'The ones who remained behind among the Bedouins will say...' and His statement: 'It is the same for them whether you ask forgiveness for them or not' and His prohibition of prayer for them. So it is established that those whom he was commanded to seek forgiveness for are indeed the people of iman in reality. Then it is not possible that he is commanded to seek forgiveness while they have no sins, or that they have already been forgiven, because seeking forgiveness is requesting forgiveness, and requesting it for one who has already been forgiven is concealing the blessing of forgiveness, and that is ingratitude for the blessing. Rather, the proper thing is gratitude and praise. And one who has no sin at all, seeking forgiveness for him takes the form of ingratitude for divine protection, and it is not permissible because punishing someone like that would be considered bounty in His judgment. Then it is not possible that the Messenger of Allah and the angels seek forgiveness for those they are commanded to, and then they are not answered. So by this it is established that the name of iman is not removed for every sin, and that there are sins that are not forgiven except by repentance from them, because there is no repentance in seeking forgiveness for one who is not a sinner. And in this is a refutation of the Mu'tazila regarding their removal of the name of iman for every sin that is not forgiven for its doer until he seeks forgiveness, and a refutation of the Khawarij by what we have mentioned. And Allah knows best. And also, Allah said concerning the sins that He does not forgive: 'It is the same for them whether you ask forgiveness for them or not' and likewise He said: 'And turn to Allah in repentance, all of you, O believers, that you might succeed' and He said: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance.' So He required them to affirm iman and informed that through repentance He forgives them. And in that are two aspects: one of them concerning repentance with...
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument defending the position that major sins do not remove a person from the fold of faith (iman), refuting both the Khawarij and the Mu'tazila. Maturidi begins by noting that some classify sins into minor and major, with minor sins forgiven by avoiding major sins or by pardon. He affirms that the doer of a major sin remains a believer and will not abide eternally in Hell, citing the promise of reward for good deeds. Then he presents a key proof: Allah commanded the Prophet to seek forgiveness for himself and for the believers, but forbade seeking forgiveness for mushrikeen and hypocrites. This implies that those for whom forgiveness is sought are believers in reality. Moreover, it would be absurd to seek forgiveness for those without sin, since forgiveness is for sinners. Seeking forgiveness for someone already forgiven is ingratitude. Also, if the Prophet and angels seek forgiveness for believers, they must be answered; otherwise it would be futile. Thus, believers can have sins that are not yet forgiven, and these sins are forgiven through repentance. Therefore, the name of iman does not depart due to sin. This refutes the Mu'tazila who say that a major sinner ceases to be a believer (though they are not kafirs, but in an intermediate state) and the Khawarij who declare sinners as kafirs. Maturidi also cites verses commanding believers to repent, showing they are still called believers while commanded to repent, proving their iman remains despite sin.

صغائر
كبائر
توبة
إيمان
مغفرة
معتزلة
خوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any unrepented major sin removes a person from iman completely.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the command to seek forgiveness for believers proves they remain believers despite having unrepented sins, because forgiveness is requested for them.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the main evidence that major sins do not remove the name of iman?
A) The Prophet's hadith about intercession
B) The command for the Prophet to seek forgiveness for believers
C) The classification of sins into major and minor
D) The consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's command to seek forgiveness for believers proves that major sins do not remove the name of iman, contradicting both Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Are you truly humble enough to admit that you are always in need of Allah's forgiveness, or do you sometimes feel too ashamed to ask?
?
This passage refutes those who say a major sinner is no longer a believer. Is there any sin in your life that you have allowed to make you doubt your identity as a believer? How will you actively combat that doubt using the proof from this lesson?

Seeking Forgiveness Proves Faith Remains with Sins
Maturidi argues from the command to seek forgiveness for believers to prove faith remains with sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the Qur'anic command to seek forgiveness only for believers to prove that the name of faith does not disappear with sin, refuting the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Faith remains even with sins; the command to seek forgiveness proves it.

The Mu'tazila and Khawarij argued that major sins remove a person from faith. Maturidi counters with a simple yet powerful argument from the Qur'an: if sins removed faith, the Prophet would not be commanded to seek forgiveness for believers. In this passage, he unpacks the implications with precise reasoning, showing that the very command to seek forgiveness for believers presupposes their continued faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the density of reasoning in Maturidi's style.
2
Identify the key verses cited
Find where Maturidi cites the prohibition of seeking forgiveness for polytheists and the command to seek it for believers. Understand how these verses frame the argument.
The verses are from Surah al-Tawbah and Surah al-Munafiqun.
3
Follow the logical chain
Trace how Maturidi deduces that faith must remain: if the command is given in the name of faith (seeking forgiveness for believers), then faith cannot be absent.
He also argues that seeking forgiveness presupposes sins, so believers have sins but keep faith.
4
Understand the refutation
See how this argument directly refutes the Mu'tazila (who remove faith for any unforgiven sin) and the Khawarij (who deem sinners disbelievers).
The conclusion is that the name of faith does not disappear for any sin.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this means for the relationship between faith, sin, and forgiveness in Islamic theology.
This is a key point in the debate on grave sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يحتمل الأمر به على اثبات كفر أو شرك بقوله : " مَا كَانَ لِلنَّبِيِّ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ يَسْتَغْفِرُوا لِلمُشْرِكِينَ " ، وبما أمره أن يستغفر للمؤمنين ، ومحال يأمره بالاستغفار باسم الإيمان ، وهو عنهم زائل ؛ لأن الكذب يوجب قد حذره عن الاستغفار لأهل الشرك بما ذكرت ، ولأهل النفاق بقوله : سَيَقُولُ لَكَ المُخَلَّفُونَ مِنَ الأَعْرَابِ ، وقوله : سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِم اسْتَغْفَرْتُ لَهُمْ ، وتهيه إياه عن الصلاة ، فثبت أن أولئك الذين أمرهم بالاستغفار هم أهل الأيمان في الحقيقة . ثم لا يحتمل أن يؤمر بالاستغفار ولا ذنوب لهم ، أو كانت مغفورة لهم ؛ لأن الاستغفار هو طلب المغفرة ، وطلبها لمن قد غفر له كتمان نعمة الغفران ، وذلك كفران النعمة ، بل حق ذلك الشكر والحمد ، وما لا ذنب له ثمة فيخرج طلب المغفرة مخرج كفران العصمة ، والسؤال أن لا يجوز ؛ إذ تعذيب مثله في حكمه جود ، ثم لا يحتمل أن يكون رسول الله والملائكة يستغفرون لمن أمروا به ، ثم لا يجابون ، فيثبت بهذا أن لا يزول اسم الإيمان لكل ذنب ، وأن من الذنوب ما ليس بمغفور ، يغفر بالتوبة عنه ؛ إذ ليس في استغفار غير المذنب توبة . وفى ذلك نقض على المعتزلة في إزالتهم اسم الايمان بكل ذنب ليس بمغفور لصاحبه حتى يستغفر ، ونقض على الخوارج بما ذكرنا ، والله أعلم.
Then it is not possible that the command [to seek forgiveness] implies affirming unbelief or shirk by His saying: 'It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to seek forgiveness for the polytheists,' and by His commanding him to seek forgiveness for the believers. It is impossible that He command him to seek forgiveness in the name of faith while it is removed from them, because lying would necessitate... He has already warned him about seeking forgiveness for the people of shirk as I mentioned, and for the people of hypocrisy by His saying: 'Those who stayed behind among the Bedouins will say to you...' and His saying: 'It is the same for them whether you ask forgiveness for them or not,' and His preventing him from the prayer. Thus it is established that those whom He commanded to seek forgiveness for are in reality the people of faith. Then it is not possible that they be commanded to seek forgiveness while they have no sins, or that their sins are already forgiven, because seeking forgiveness is requesting forgiveness, and requesting it for one who has already been forgiven is concealing the blessing of forgiveness, and that is ingratitude for the blessing. Rather, the appropriate thing is thanks and praise. And one who has no sin—asking forgiveness for him comes out as ingratitude for [God's] protection, and the request is not permissible, because punishing someone like that is generosity in His judgment. Then it is not possible that the Messenger of God and the angels seek forgiveness for those they are commanded to, and then not be answered. So it is established by this that the name of faith does not disappear for every sin, and that among sins are those that are not forgiven, but are forgiven by repentance, because there is no repentance in the seeking of forgiveness for one who is not a sinner. And in that is a refutation of the Mu'tazila regarding their removal of the name of faith for every sin that is not forgiven for its doer until he seeks forgiveness, and a refutation of the Khawarij by what we have mentioned. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 925

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Qur'anic command to seek forgiveness only for believers. Maturidi argues that if sins removed faith, the Prophet would not be commanded to seek forgiveness for those with sins. He first cites the verse prohibiting seeking forgiveness for polytheists and the command to seek it for believers. He reasons that if faith were removed from sinners, commanding the Prophet to seek forgiveness for them in the name of faith would be impossible because it would involve lying or implying faith remains. He then argues that seeking forgiveness presupposes sins; if the believers had no sins or were already forgiven, asking forgiveness would be ingratitude. He also notes that the Prophet's intercession must be answered, otherwise the command would be futile. Therefore, the name of faith does not disappear with every sin, and some sins require repentance. This refutes the Mu'tazila who remove the name of faith for any unforgiven sin, and the Khawarij who deem sinners disbelievers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that seeking forgiveness for a believer implies the believer is not a true believer because they have sinned.
Correction: Maturidi shows the opposite: the command to seek forgiveness in the name of faith proves that the believer still has faith despite sins.

Checkpoint

A) Believers never sin.
B) The name of faith does not disappear for every sin.
C) Sins always remove faith.
D) Only polytheists need forgiveness.

Key Takeaway
The command to seek forgiveness only for believers proves that faith remains even when sins are committed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What would change if you truly internalized that your faith remains intact right now, despite your failures? This week, when the guilt of a particular sin weighs on you, will you respond by seeking forgiveness with hope, or by despairing?
?
The Prophet himself is commanded to seek forgiveness for believers like you. Does this truth make you feel secure enough to confess the sin you have been hiding? How will you acknowledge it today and seek forgiveness, trusting that your faith is not lost?
?
If the name of faith remains even with sins, does that make you complacent or more grateful? Starting tonight, will you repent with a heart that is thankful for the faith you still have, or will you take it for granted?

God's Command to Repent Proves Faith Remains with Sins
Maturidi cites verses commanding repentance to prove faith remains with sins, refuting Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses verses commanding repentance to argue that faith remains with sins, refuting Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Addressing sinners as believers while commanding repentance proves their faith remains.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents a powerful Qur'anic argument against those who claim that major sins remove faith entirely. By citing verses where Allah commands believers to repent, he demonstrates that the very act of commanding repentance presupposes the continued existence of faith in the sinner. This refutes both the Mu'tazila position (that sin removes the name of faith) and the Khawarij position (that sin makes one a disbeliever). Let's walk through the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the verses cited and the logical conclusion drawn.
Pay attention to the phrase 'فألزمهم إثبات الإيمان' which highlights the obligation to affirm faith.
2
Identify the two refutations
The passage explicitly mentions two 'aspects' (وجهان): one against the Mu'tazila and one against the Khawarij. Locate these in the text.
The Mu'tazila remove the name of faith; the Khawarij call sinners disbelievers.
3
Understand the logical inference
Why does commanding repentance necessitate that the sinners are still believers? Think about how Allah addresses them as 'O believers'.
If they were not believers, the command would be meaningless or contradictory.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this argument protects the integrity of faith as separate from sin, and why this matters for everyday Muslim life.
This is a cornerstone of the Maturidi position on faith and sin.

وأيضا إن الله تعالى قال فى الذنوب التي لا يغفرها : سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِم اسْتَغْفَرْتَ لَهُمْ أَمْ لَمْ تَسْتَغْفِرْ لَهُمْ ، وعلى ذلك قال : " وَتُوبُوا إلى اللهِ جَمِيعًا أَيُّهَا المُؤْمِنُونَ لَعَلَّكُم تُفْلِحُونَ " ، وقال : يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا تُوبُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ تَوْبَةً نَصُوحًا ، فألزمهم إثبات الإيمان وأخبر أنه بالتوبة يغفر لهم ، وفى ذلك وجهان : أحدهما على المعتزلة في إزالتهم اسم الإيمان في كل ذنب لا يُغفر عندهم إلا بالتوبة ، وفى ذلك إثباته ، وعلى الخوارج بتسميتهم كفرة وأهل الشرك ، ومحال مع ذلك اسم الإيمان والأمر بغيره : والله الموفق
And also God Almighty said concerning the sins that He does not forgive: 'It is the same for them whether you ask forgiveness for them or not,' and upon that He said: 'And turn to God all together, O believers, so that you may succeed,' and He said: 'O you who have believed, turn to God with sincere repentance.' So He obligated them to affirm faith and informed that through repentance He will forgive them. And in that are two aspects: one against the Mu'tazila regarding their removal of the name of faith for every sin that is not forgiven according to them except through repentance, and in that is an affirmation of it; and against the Khawarij regarding their naming them disbelievers and people of shirk, and it is impossible with that the name of faith and the command to something else. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 925

Commentary
This passage is a double refutation using Qur'anic verses that command repentance. Maturidi first cites the verse that it is the same whether forgiveness is sought for some sinners, implying unforgiven sins do not remove faith. Then he cites verses commanding believers to repent. He argues that God addresses them as 'believers' while commanding repentance, which means they still have faith despite sin. This refutes the Mu'tazila who say the name of faith is removed for any sin that requires repentance, because the verse affirms faith. It also refutes the Khawarij who label such sinners as disbelievers, because it is impossible to call them believers and command them to repent if they are actually disbelievers.

Key Terms
التوبة
المؤمنون
المعتزلة
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that commanding repentance implies the person is no longer a believer.
Correction: Maturidi shows the opposite: the command to repent is addressed to believers, so they must still have faith despite their sins.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi use the verse 'O you who have believed, repent' against the Khawarij?
A) It shows repentance is only for polytheists.
B) It proves that sinners are still called believers.
C) It proves that sins remove faith.
D) It shows repentance is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses the Qur'anic command to repent, addressed to believers, to prove that major sins do not remove faith, thereby refuting both the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Figurative naming: Kafir as metaphor
Maturidi explains figurative naming using analogy and Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that terms like kafir can be used figuratively in cases of coercion, without implying real unbelief.

Core Idea
Faith is in the heart; words can be figuratively called kufr without it being real.

Maturidi confronts a linguistic dilemma: the Qur'an calls someone a kafir even when forced, yet his heart remains faithful. How is this consistent? This lesson unpacks his solution: figurative language allows names based on actions without altering reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get its flow. Notice the analogy of 'deaf' and 'blind' used for someone who does not grasp reality.
The first word has an OCR issue — it should be 'ولو كان'.
2
Identify the linguistic analogy
Maturidi compares calling a coerced person a kafir to calling someone 'deaf' or 'blind' figuratively. Understand that this naming is based on external action, not inner reality.
3
Analyze the Qur'anic example
Look at the verse (Q16:106) cited: 'Whoever disbelieves in God after his faith...'. Maturidi highlights that the name 'kufr' is applied only verbally under coercion, because the heart is at peace with faith.
This shows that the Qur'an itself uses figurative language in this context.
4
Grasp the principle
From this, Maturidi concludes that it is permissible to call sinners disbelievers figuratively due to their actions, but not literally. The real faith remains intact.
This principle preserves the integrity of faith while accounting for outward actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كا[ن] في شيء تسمية بالكفر فهو مجاز اللغة من حيث ذلك صنيعهم ، ونحو ذلك ، على ما يقال للمرء : أصم وأعمى بما لا يقف على حقيقة ما بذلك يوصل إليه ، وذلك نحو قوله : مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ ، فأثبت اسم الكفر فما كان منه على الإكراه لفظا لا تحقيقا لما اطمأن قلبه بالإيمان ، فثبت أن قد يجوز تسميته لنوازل مجازا ، فمثله الأعمال ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And if there is any naming of [someone] as kufr, it is a linguistic metaphor due to their action, and the like of that, just as it is said of a person: 'Deaf' and 'Blind' for one who does not grasp the reality of what that leads to. And that is like His saying: 'Whoever disbelieves in God after his faith' — so He affirmed the name of kufr for what was from him under coercion, in word not in reality, because his heart is at rest with faith. So it is established that it is permissible to name him figuratively for occurrences. And likewise deeds. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 926

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic argument about figurative speech. Maturidi notes that sometimes people are called by names figuratively based on their actions, not reality. For example, a person who does not understand something may be called 'deaf' or 'blind' metaphorically. He cites the Qur'anic verse about one who disbelieves under coercion: such a person is called a 'disbeliever' only linguistically because his heart remains faithful. Therefore, it is permissible to call sinners disbelievers figuratively due to their actions, but not literally. This reinforces that actual faith remains, and such naming does not entail real unbelief.

Key Terms
مجاز
الإكراه
الكفر
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any Qur'anic term of kufr implies real unbelief, regardless of context.
Correction: Maturidi shows that in cases of coercion, the term is used figuratively; the person's inner faith remains intact.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why can a person coerced into uttering disbelief be called a kafir?
A) Because his faith is removed.
B) As a linguistic metaphor, not reality.
C) Because he is truly a disbeliever.
D) Because coercion invalidates faith.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that naming someone a kafir can be a linguistic metaphor when external constraints like coercion occur, without negating their inner faith.

What would change in how you interact with Muslims who appear to be in sin?

Good deeds are seen after faith, refuting Mu'tazila and Khawarij
Maturidi argues from Quranic verses about recompense to show good deeds are rewarded after faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that good deeds performed before faith are rewarded after faith, based on Quranic verses, and how this refutes the positions of Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Good deeds done before faith are rewarded after repentance, not nullified by sins.

Imam Maturidi presents a concise yet powerful argument from the Quran that good deeds done in a state of disbelief are not lost but are seen and rewarded after faith. He cites several verses to establish that recompense for both good and bad deeds occurs after one embraces faith and repents. This directly challenges the views of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, who held that major or minor sins can nullify all good deeds, even for a believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of Maturidi's argument and the Quranic verses he quotes.
Pay attention to the sequence of verses he uses.
2
Identify the key Quranic verses
List the three Quranic verses cited: 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it,' 'Whoever does evil or wrongs himself,' and 'If they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them,' and the verse about changing evil deeds to good.
These verses are the foundation of his argument.
3
Understand Maturidi's interpretation
See how Maturidi connects these verses to show that good deeds done before faith are not wasted but are rewarded after faith, and that sins do not nullify them.
He argues that the seeing of good occurs after faith, not during shirk.
4
See how it refutes Mu'tazila and Khawarij
Notice that Maturidi explicitly says this understanding does not hold according to Mu'tazila (who think major or minor sins nullify good deeds) and Khawarij (who think any sin nullifies faith and deeds).
This shows the practical implication of his tafsir.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider what this means for the relationship between faith, deeds, and forgiveness. It emphasizes God's mercy and the importance of repentance.

وأيضا إن الله تعالى قال : فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ ، ثم معلوم أنه لا يرى الخير ، وجزاه مع الشرك ، ولا جزا[ه] شر في حال الكفر يرى ذلك بعد الإيمان لقوله تعالى : وَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا أَوْ يَظْلِمْ نَفْسَهُ ، وقوله : " وَإِنْ يَنْتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُمْ مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ ، وقال : " فَأُولَئِكَ يُبَدِّلُ اللهُ سَيِّئَاتِهِم حَسَنَاتٍ ، دل ما ذكرت من تحقيق حال فيها جزاء الأمرين، وذلك لا يكون على قول المعتزلة فى وقت الكبائر ولا فى وقت الصغائر ، وكذا فى قول الخوارج ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also God Almighty said: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it.' Then it is known that he does not see the good and its reward with shirk, and he does not see evil in the state of disbelief; he sees that after faith, due to His saying: 'And whoever does evil or wrongs himself,' and His saying: 'And if they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them,' and He said: 'They are the ones whose evil deeds God will change into good deeds.' What I have mentioned indicates the reality of the situation in which the recompense of both things occurs. And that does not happen according to the Mu'tazila's view regarding major sins nor minor sins, and similarly according to the Khawarij's view. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 926

Commentary
This passage is an argument from Qur'anic verses about recompense. Maturidi cites the verse that whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, but clarifies that this seeing occurs after faith, not while in a state of shirk or disbelief. He supports this with verses stating that if they desist from shirk, past sins are forgiven, and that God changes evil deeds into good deeds after repentance. This shows that good deeds done before faith are rewarded after faith, and that major or minor sins do not nullify all good deeds. This refutes the Mu'tazila who say that major sins (and according to some minor sins) nullify all good deeds, and the Khawarij who say that any sin nullifies faith and good deeds.

Correction: Maturidi shows from Quranic verses that good deeds are rewarded after faith, and sins are forgiven upon repentance, refuting the idea that they are nullified.

God's forgiveness of shirk through repentance refutes unconditional denial
Maturidi clarifies the verse on shirk and refutes two erroneous interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the known fact that shirk can be forgiven through repentance to refute two erroneous views about forgiveness.

Core Idea
Shirk can be forgiven if repented, so the verse threatens only unrepentant shirk.

Imam Maturidi presents a key clarification about the famous verse 'God does not forgive shirk.' He shows that this verse does not mean shirk is absolutely unforgivable; rather, it refers to dying in that state without repentance. This argument refutes both those who take the verse unconditionally and those who deny forgiveness for major sins without repentance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi starts with the Qur'anic statement and then draws a logical conclusion.
2
Identify the two groups
Find the two groups that Maturidi refutes: those who make the verse unconditional and those who deny forgiveness for major sins without repentance.
3
Understand the reasoning
Reflect on why the known fact that shirk can be forgiven through repentance invalidates both positions. How does it expose their error?
4
Connect to God's will
Notice the final phrase: God has assigned to Himself the will to forgive. This underscores that forgiveness is ultimately God's prerogative, not a mechanical rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الله تعالى قال : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ ومعلوم أن الشرك قد يغفر بالتوبة ، فبطل به قول من يجعله لما قسم الكتاب ، وبطل قول من يبطل المغفرة فى الكبائر بلا توبة ؛ لأن الله جل ثناؤه جعل لنفسه مشيئة المغفرة ، وذلك
Then God Almighty said: 'Indeed God does not forgive that partners be associated with Him.' And it is known that shirk can be forgiven through repentance. So by this the statement of those who make it [the verse] for what the Book divides [i.e., unconditionally] is invalidated, and the statement of those who nullify forgiveness for major sins without repentance is invalidated; because God, exalted be His praise, has assigned to Himself the will to forgive.
Source pages p. 926

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of the Qur'anic verse that God does not forgive shirk. Maturidi notes that it is known by consensus that shirk can be forgiven through repentance, so the verse does not mean that shirk is never forgiven; it means that if one dies upon shirk without repentance, it is not forgiven. This refutes two groups: those who interpret the verse unconditionally (some Khawarij or literalists) to mean shirk is never forgiven, and those who deny the possibility of forgiveness for major sins without repentance (probably the Mu'tazila who require repentance for forgiveness). Maturidi asserts that God has reserved for Himself the will to forgive, implying that He may forgive major sins without repentance if He wills.

Key Terms
الشرك
المغفرة
التوبة
الكبائر
المشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'God does not forgive shirk' means shirk is never forgiven under any circumstances.
Correction: Maturidi shows that shirk can be forgiven if the person repents before death. The verse refers to those who die without repentance.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi argue that the verse 'God does not forgive shirk' does not mean shirk is never forgiven?
A) Because shirk is not a sin.
B) Because it is known that shirk can be forgiven through repentance.
C) Because the verse applies only to minor shirk.
D) Because forgiveness is impossible for any sin.

Key Takeaway
Even the gravest sin, shirk, can be forgiven through repentance, so God's forgiveness is vast and not restricted by any sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The verse threatens unrepentant shirk. Is there any form of shirk (like showing off, relying on created beings, or hidden pride) that you have not sincerely repented from? Will you examine your heart now and repent for anything that competes with God's sole worthiness of worship?

Metaphorical Naming of Disbelief and Faith
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila and Khawarij on naming of kufr/iman and introduces metaphorical usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses linguistic metaphor (majaz) to distinguish between literal disbelief and figurative naming of actions, refuting both the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Not every action called 'kufr' makes a person a literal disbeliever.

Maturidi addresses two extreme sectarian positions: the Mu'tazila who strip the name of faith from sinners, and the Khawarij who label them disbelievers. He then presents a linguistic principle: the term 'kufr' can be used metaphorically, just as a stubborn person is called 'deaf' or 'blind' without being literally so. The Quran itself supports this in the verse about forced disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Find the mentions of Mu'tazila and Khawarij in the Arabic and translation. Note what each group does with the names of iman and kufr.
Mu'tazila remove iman for sin; Khawarij affirm kufr for sin.
2
Understand the metaphor argument
Maturidi compares calling a sin 'kufr' to calling a stubborn person 'deaf' or 'blind'. This is a figurative use, not a literal judgment of disbelief.
Focus on the phrase مجاز اللغة.
3
Apply the Quranic example
Read the verse about one who utters disbelief under compulsion while the heart is settled in faith. How does this support Maturidi's claim?
The verse affirms the name 'kufr' for the utterance but not the person's state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعتزلة في إزالتهم اسم الإيمان في كل ذنب لا يُغفر عندهم إلا بالتوبة ، وفى ذلك إثباته ، وعلى الخوارج بتسميتهم كفرة وأهل الشرك ، ومحال مع ذلك اسم الإيمان والأمر بغيره : والله الموفق • ۱، ولو كان في شيء تسمية بالكفر فهو مجاز اللغة من حيث ذلك صنيعهم ، ونحو ذلك ، على ما يقال للمرء : أصم وأعمى بما لا يقف على حقيقة ما بذلك يوصل إليه ، وذلك نحو قوله : مَنْ كَفَرَ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ إِيمَانِهِ ، فأثبت اسم الكفر فما كان منه على الإكراه لفظا لا تحقيقا لما اطمأن قلبه بالإيمان ، فثبت أن قد يجوز تسميته لنوازل مجازا ، فمثله الأعمال ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
The Mu'tazila, in their removal of the name of faith for every sin that is not forgiven except through repentance, and in that is its affirmation, and upon the Khawarij, by their naming them disbelievers and people of shirk, and impossible with that is the name of faith and command of other than it: and God is the granter of success. And if there was in something a naming with disbelief, it is a metaphor of language from that aspect of their doing, and similar to that, as it is said of a man: deaf and blind concerning what he does not grasp the reality of what is thereby conveyed to him. And that is like His saying: 'Whoever disbelieves in God after his faith' - so He affirmed the name of disbelief, and what was from him under compulsion is a word, not a realization, because his heart is settled with faith. So it is established that it may be permissible to name him for occurrences metaphorically. So likewise are deeds. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 926

Commentary
This passage defines the positions of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij regarding the naming of sins as disbelief or removal of faith. Maturidi then presents a linguistic argument that the term 'kufr' can be used metaphorically (majaz) in certain situations, as in the Quranic verse about one who utters disbelief under compulsion while the heart is firm in faith. Thus, naming a deed as kufr does not necessarily imply literal kufr, but can be figurative.

Key Terms
إيمان
كفر
مجاز
إكراه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Maturidi denies the reality of kufr or that calling an action kufr makes one a literal disbeliever.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that the name kufr can be used metaphorically (majaz) for actions or utterances while the person remains a believer at heart, as in the case of compulsion. Literal kufr requires inner conviction.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi use to support the metaphorical use of 'kufr'?
A) The consensus of scholars
B) The verse about forced disbelief
C) The practice of the Khawarij
D) Logical necessity

Key Takeaway
Maturidi argues that naming an action 'kufr' is often a metaphorical (majaz) usage, not a literal declaration of disbelief, especially when the person's heart remains firm in faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe a fellow Muslim committing a sin, do you ever find yourself mentally labeling them as a 'disbeliever' or 'hypocrite' without considering the state of their heart? How does Maturidi's teaching on metaphorical naming challenge you to examine your own judgment and the gravity of takfir?

How does Maturidi's affirmation that the heart can remain faithful despite outward failure reshape your understanding of God's mercy and your own need for humility?

Maturidi's Refutation of Equating Minor Sins with Disbelief
Maturidi condemns equating minor sins with disbelief or eternal punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi considers the view that minor sins constitute kufr or shirk as an abandoned opinion that contradicts God's attributes of forgiveness and justice.

Core Idea
Calling minor sins kufr contradicts God's nature as the Pardoner.

Imam Maturidi here addresses an extreme theological position: the claim that minor sins are equivalent to disbelief (kufr) or that they warrant eternal punishment. He argues that such a view is not only scripturally unsupported but also theologically incoherent, as it strips God of His attributes of forgiveness and mercy. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong opening phrase 'قول مهجور' (abandoned saying).
2
Identify the core argument
The view nullifies God's attributes of pardon and mercy because it implies no sin is forgiven without repentance.
This is the central theological problem.
3
Consider the consequences
Maturidi lists further problems: it leads to enmity, implicates prophets, and misrepresents God's justice and generosity.
Each consequence reinforces the rejection.
4
Reflect on the final note
The last sentence indicates the argument extends beyond what is mentioned, showing the thoroughness of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القول فى جعل الصغائر كفرا أو شركا أو التخليد في النار جزاء لها قول مهجور ؛ بما يسقط معنى تسميته عفوا غفورا رحيما ؛ إذ لا يسعه مأثم ولا زلة بلا توبة ، ويوجب به المعاداة بعد أن عرفه عفوا غفورا كريما ، وعادي لأجله من أزال عنه هذا الاسم إلى كل ما يوصف كل قاس وكل لئيم ، وبه يستحق الذي قال ؛ إذ هذا أعظم الذنوب ، حيث صفات الرب ، ثم بما بلى به الأنبياء ، في تلك الأحوال ، ومن كفر ينبى في وقت فهو كافر لا ريب فيه. ثم بهذا وصف الرب بالجود لما فيه إبطال الحسنات بزلة ، والعدل هو الذي يجزى بالإحسان والإساءة فيما أظهر عز وجل من كرمه ، ثم التجهيل بما لم يعرف من يصلح للرسالة ويقوم بأداء الأمانة ، ثم بما لا أجد عنه ، فيكون في الذي ذكر
Then the saying about making minor sins as disbelief or shirk or eternal punishment in the Fire as a recompense for them is an abandoned saying, because it nullifies the meaning of His being called Pardoner, Forgiver, Merciful; since no sin or slip would be allowed to Him without repentance, and it necessitates enmity after He has been known as Pardoner, Forgiving, Generous, and hostile for His sake whoever removes this name from everything described as harsh and base, and by it the one who said deserves; since this is the greatest of sins, where the attributes of the Lord, then what He afflicted the prophets with in those states, and whoever disbelieves in a prophet at the time is a disbeliever without doubt. Then by this He described the Lord with generosity because it nullifies good deeds by a slip, and justice is that which rewards for good and evil in what He has shown of His generosity, then ignorance of who is suitable for messengership and carries out the trust, then what I do not find, so it is in what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 927

Commentary
This passage declares that the position equating minor sins with kufr or shirk or eternal punishment is abandoned (mahjur). Maturidi argues that such a view contradicts God's attributes of pardon, forgiveness, and mercy, because it would mean that no sin can be forgiven without repentance, thereby stripping God of these attributes. It also leads to enmity against those who do not hold this view. He further argues that this view implicates the prophets whose minor slips were forgiven, and it impugns God's justice and generosity. The passage ends with a note that the argument extends to what is not mentioned, indicating the strength of the refutation.

Key Terms
صغائر
كفر
تخليد
مغفرة
عدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that any minor sin is an act of disbelief and leads to eternal punishment in Hell.
Correction: Maturidi explains that this view is abandoned because it contradicts God's attributes of forgiveness and mercy, and it would imply that even prophets' minor slips would lead to punishment, which is not the case.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi call the position of making minor sins kufr 'abandoned'?
A) It is a minority view
B) It contradicts the attributes of God
C) It is not found in the Quran
D) It was invented by heretics

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that equating minor sins with kufr undermines God's attributes of forgiveness and justice, and is therefore an abandoned position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever categorized someone's minor mistake as a sign of weak faith or hypocrisy? How does Maturidi's warning about equating minor sins with kufr challenge your tendency to judge others harshly? What concrete change will you make today to practice seeing others through God's attribute of al-`Afuww?
?
You know that God is al-Ghafur, but do you truly believe that your own repeated minor sins are covered by His mercy, or do you live in a quiet fear that they have accumulated beyond forgiveness? What would it mean for your daily life to fully accept that God's forgiveness is not conditional on never slipping?
?
Maturidi says that calling minor sins 'kufr' makes God appear hostile and unforgiving. Look at your own speech: do you ever describe God in ways that diminish His mercy? When you speak about sin and punishment, do your words reflect the balance of His justice and generosity, or do they lean toward fear without hope? Write down one sentence you will correct today.

Faith and Disbelief

6 min
The Scriptural Case for Major Sinners as Disbelievers
Maturidi presents Quranic evidence equating major sins with disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses to argue that major sinners share the name of disbelief.

Core Idea
Major sinners are called disbelievers because they share the same divine threat.

This lesson presents Maturidi's scriptural arguments that equate major sins with disbelief. He begins by noting that minor sins can be forgiven, which shifts the threat to major sins. Then he cites verses that describe disbelievers' characteristics and applies them to major sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on minor sins
Notice how Maturidi uses the possibility of forgiveness for minor sins to shift the focus to major sins.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
List each verse Maturidi cites and see how he connects them to major sinners.
Consider the verse about judging by other than God's law.
3
Understand the naming argument
Maturidi points out that major sinners are called by the same names as disbelievers: fisq, fujur, zulm.
4
Grasp the initial conclusion
If the threat of hellfire is established for major sinners, they are effectively called disbelievers.
This conclusion is based on the scriptural evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فما يثبت فى الصغائر من إمكان العفو أو إبقاء الإيمان أوجب صرف الوعيد إلى الكبائر، وما يثبت من ذكر جزاء الكفر والشرك ونحوه يوجب تحقيق اسم الشرك . وقول قوم : والكفر على قول، وأيد ذلك قوله : "إِنَّهُ لَا يَيْأَسُ مِنْ رُوحِ اللَّهِ إِلَّا القَوْمُ الكَافِرُونَ" وقال : "وَمَنْ يَقْنَطُ مِنْ رَحْمَةِ رَبِّهِ إِلَّا الضَّالُّونَ" مع ما كان صاحب الكبيرة حاكما بغير الذى أنزل الله، وتاركا الحكم به، وقد قال الله تعالى : وَمَنْ لَمْ يَحْكُمْ بِمَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ فَأُولَئِكَ هُم الكَافِرُونَ . وبعد، فإنه قد سمى بالأسماء التي سمى الله بها الكفرة من الفسق والفجور والظلم لزمه أيضا اسم الكفر مع ما قسم الله البشر الذين جرى عليهم القلم فيما عليه أمرهم في الدنيا والآخرة فقال : "هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ فَمِنْكُم كَافِرٌ وَمِنْكُمْ مُؤْمِنٌ" وقال : "فَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيُؤْمِنْ وَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيَكْفُرْ" وقال : "فَمَنْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَنْ يُهْدِيَهُ" : "يُضِلُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ" وقال : "أَفَمَنْ كَانَ مُؤْمِنًا كَمَنْ كَانَ فَاسِقًا لَا يَسْتَوُونَ" ثم بين كفر المسمى فاسقا، وقال في أمر الآخرة : "يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وَجُوهٌ" وقال : "فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ" فجعلهم جميعا متسمين، فلا ثالث في التحقيق . مع ما بين أن النار أعدت للكافرين. فإذا ثبت الوعيد لصاحب الكبيرة جعله كافرا، وبعد، فإن الله تعالى وصف أنه لا ييأس من روح الله إلا القوم الكافرون وقد لزم ألا يأس على قول هو لا لزمه اسم الكفر، على أن الأسماء لا منافع لها ولا مضار بها على أهلها، إنما المضار والمنافع في حقائق ما لها الأسماء، فإذا لزم الخلود في النار بطلت فائدة الاسم إن كان مؤمنا أو كافرا لا يمنع عنه اسم الكفر إذ عوقب بعقوبته، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
What is established regarding minor sins (al-saghā'ir) of the possibility of forgiveness or preservation of faith necessitates directing the threat to major sins. And what is established of the mention of the recompense of disbelief and polytheism and the like necessitates the realization of the name polytheism. And some people say: disbelief is based on a saying. And that is supported by His saying: 'Indeed, no one despairs of the mercy of God except the disbelieving people' and He said: 'And who despairs of the mercy of his Lord except the astray?' along with the fact that the perpetrator of a major sin was judging by other than what God revealed, abandoning judgment by it, and God Almighty said: 'And whoever does not judge by what God has revealed – those are the disbelievers.' And moreover, he (the sinner) has been named with the names with which God named the disbelievers, such as sin (fisq), depravity (fujūr), and injustice (zulm), so the name of disbelief also applies to him, along with what God divided mankind – those upon whom the pen has written concerning their affair in this world and the Hereafter – and He said: 'He is the One who created you, and among you is a disbeliever and among you a believer' and said: 'So whoever wills – let him believe; and whoever wills – let him disbelieve' and said: 'Whomever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam' and said: 'Then is one who was a believer like one who was defiantly disobedient? They are not equal.' Then He made clear the disbelief of the one called a sinner. And He said concerning the matter of the Hereafter: 'On the Day when faces will be whitened' and said: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand,' and He made all of them described by names, so there is no third in reality. Along with what He made clear that the Fire is prepared for the disbelievers. So if the threat is established for the perpetrator of a major sin, it makes him a disbeliever. And moreover, God Almighty described that no one despairs of the Spirit of God except the disbelieving people, and it necessarily follows that there is no despair according to a saying that makes the name of disbelief necessary. However, names have no benefits nor harms for their possessors; the harms and benefits are only in the realities to which the names refer. So if eternal abiding in the Fire is necessary, the benefit of the name is nullified, whether he is a believer or a disbeliever – it does not prevent the name of disbelief from being applied to him since he is punished with its punishment. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 928

Commentary
This passage is a proof or argument. Maturidi builds a scriptural case for the view that major sinners are called disbelievers in the Quran, but then offers a nuanced conclusion. He starts by noting that minor sins may be forgiven, which shifts the threat to major sins. He then cites several Quranic verses that seem to equate certain sins with disbelief or polytheism, such as despairing of mercy, judging by other than God's law, and being named with the same terms as disbelievers. He also cites divisions of mankind into believers and disbelievers, and verses where a sinner is contrasted with a believer. He concludes that if the threat of hellfire is established for the major sinner, then he is effectively called a disbeliever. However, he then qualifies: the names themselves have no intrinsic harm; what matters is the reality of punishment. So even if the name 'disbeliever' is applied, it does not change the fact that the punishment is the key. This is a nuanced position that avoids outright takfir while acknowledging the severity of major sins.

Key Terms
صغائر (saghā'ir)
وعيد (wa'īd)
كفر (kufr)
شرك (shirk)
فسق (fisq)
فجور (fujūr)
ظلم (zulm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does the verse 'And whoever does not judge by what God has revealed' imply about such a person?
A) He is a sinner
B) He is a disbeliever
C) He is a hypocrite
D) He is unjust

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses multiple Quranic verses to argue that major sinners are called disbelievers because they share the same threatening characteristics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you truly feel the weight of being grouped with the disbelievers? How does this lesson force you to reconsider your casual attitude toward sin, knowing that the same threat of hellfire applies to you if you persist?
?
The Quran divides mankind into only believers and disbelievers. If you were to die tonight, which side would you be on based on your actions and faith? Are you relying on the forgiveness of minor sins while neglecting the danger of major sins?
?
Maturidi argues that calling a major sinner a disbeliever is not just a name but a consequence of shared characteristics like despair, injustice, and breaking God's law. Does your life reflect the characteristics of a believer or those of a disbeliever? What is one change you must make today to align yourself with the believers?

Names vs Reality: The Nuanced Conclusion
Maturidi clarifies that names are secondary to the actual punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's distinction between the name 'disbeliever' and the actual reality of punishment.

Core Idea
Names do not harm; what matters is the actual punishment.

After establishing that major sinners are called disbelievers, Maturidi qualifies this conclusion. He explains that names are merely labels; the real significance lies in the punishment that follows. This prevents the conclusion from being used for outright takfir.

Guided Path
1
Read the final part of the passage
Focus on the statement about names having no benefit or harm.
2
Understand the distinction between name and reality
Maturidi says the harm is in the reality (punishment), not the name itself.
3
Consider the implication for major sinners
Even if called a disbeliever, the key is the punishment in the Hereafter.
4
Reflect on the overall message
Maturidi avoids takfir while upholding the severity of major sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Faith and Disbelief

The First Proof: Shared Names and Divine Division
First proof: shared names and divine division leave no third category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's first scriptural argument that a major sinner must be called a disbeliever because God applies the same names to him and divides humanity into only two categories.

Core Idea
If the name fits and the threat is the same, the judgment follows.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents the first of two proofs from the Quran that major sinners should be termed disbelievers. He begins by noting that such sinners already bear the same names (sinner, unjust) that God uses for disbelievers. Then he shows that God divides people into only believers and disbelievers, and declares the Fire is for disbelievers—so there is no third category for the major sinner.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the use of multiple Quranic verses in quick succession.
2
Identify the key names
Maturidi lists names like fasiq, fajir, and zalim that God uses for disbelievers. See how these are applied to the major sinner.
3
Notice the division of people
Maturidi quotes verses that divide people into only two categories: believer and disbeliever. There is no third label for major sinners.
Pay attention to verses like 'Is one who is a believer like one who is a sinner? They are not equal.'
4
Connect threat to name
The Fire is prepared for disbelievers, and the major sinner faces the same threat. This seals the argument: he must be called a disbeliever.
Maturidi concludes: 'So when the threat is established for the committer of a major sin, it makes him a disbeliever.'

Source Text

وبعد، فإنه قد سمى بالأسماء التي سمى الله بها الكفرة من الفسق والفجور والظلم لزمه أيضا اسم الكفر مع ما قسم الله البشر الذين جرى عليهم القلم فيما عليه أمرهم في الدنيا والآخرة فقال: "هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ فَمِنْكُمْ كَافِرٌ وَمِنْكُمْ مُؤْمِنٌ" وقال: "فَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيُؤْمِنْ وَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيَكْفُرْ" وقال: "فَمَنْ يُرِدِ اللهُ أَنْ يَهْدِيَهُ يُضْلِلْ مَنْ يَشَاءُ" وقال: "أَفَمَنْ كَانَ مُؤْمِنًا كَمَنْ كَانَ فَاسِقًا لا يَسْتَوُونَ" ثم بين كفر المسمى فاسقا، وقال في أمر الآخرة: "يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ" وقال: "فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ" فجعلهم جميعا متسمين، فلا ثالث في التحقيق. مع ما بين أن النار أعدت للكافرين. فإذا ثبت الوعيد لصاحب الكبيرة جعله كافرا. وبعد، فإن الله تعالى وصف أنه لا ييأس من روح الله إلا القوم الكافرون وقد لزم ألا يأس على قول هو لا لزمه اسم الكفر، على أن الأسماء لا منافع لها ولا مضار بها على أهلها، إنما المضار والمنافع في حقائق ما لها الأسماء، فإذا لزم الخلود في النار بطلت فائدة الاسم إن كان مؤمنا أو كافرا لا يمنع عنه اسم الكفر إذ عوقب بعقوبته، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And then, he has been named with the names that Allah named the disbelievers: of sin, immorality, and injustice, so the name of disbelief also necessarily applies to him, along with what Allah divided the people—upon whom the pen has run concerning their affair in this world and the Hereafter—and He said: 'It is He who created you, and among you is a disbeliever and among you is a believer,' and He said: 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve,' and He said: 'For whomever Allah wills to guide, He leads astray whomever He wills,' and He said: 'Is one who is a believer like one who is a sinner? They are not equal.' Then He made clear the disbelief of the one named a sinner, and He said concerning the matter of the Hereafter: 'On the Day when faces become white' and He said: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand,' so He made all of them [distinctly] named, so there is no third [category] in reality. Along with [the fact] that He made clear that the Fire is prepared for the disbelievers. So when the threat is established for the committer of a major sin, it makes him a disbeliever. And then, Allah the Exalted described that none despairs of the mercy of Allah except the disbelieving people, and it necessarily follows that there is no despair according to a saying that he does not necessitate the name of disbelief for him; but indeed the names have no benefits or harms upon their people; only the harms and benefits are in the realities of what the names indicate. So when eternity in the Fire becomes necessary, the benefit of the name is nullified whether he is a believer or a disbeliever, and the name of disbelief does not prevent him from being punished with its punishment. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 929

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs. First proof: God has named disbelievers with terms like fasiq, fajir, zalim, and He divides people into only two categories—believer and disbeliever—with the Fire prepared for disbelievers. Since the major sinner is called by these same names and faces the same threat (wa'id), he must be called a disbeliever; there is no third category. Second proof: Despair of God's mercy is characteristic of disbelievers. If a major sinner does not despair, he might avoid the name of disbelief, but names have no inherent benefit or harm; only the realities (haqa'iq) matter. If he is punished with eternal Fire, the name—whether believer or disbeliever—does him no good, so refusing the name kafir does not protect him from punishment. Thus the Mu'tazila's caution over the name is futile.

Key Terms
كفر
صاحب الكبيرة
الوعيد
تسمية
فاسق
ظالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A major sinner cannot be called a disbeliever because he still has faith.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the names and the threat of fire indicate he falls under the category of kafir, regardless of his internal faith.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's first proof, what makes a major sinner deserving of the name 'disbeliever'?
A) He commits an act of shirk.
B) He bears the same names as disbelievers and is threatened with the Fire, which is prepared for disbelievers.
C) He despairs of God's mercy.
D) He rejects a clear command.

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that since God applies the same names and the same threat to major sinners, they must be called disbelievers; there is no middle category.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you bear the names of sin, immorality, or injustice, have you considered that you might be on the path of disbelief? What will you do today to remove yourself from that category?
?
This passage says there is no third category—you are either a believer or a disbeliever. Are you certain that your major sins do not place you among the disbelievers? What evidence from your own life confirms your faith?
?
The Fire is prepared for disbelievers, and the threat applies to those who share the same names and punishment. How does this truth change the way you view even a single sin you are committing right now? Will you repent immediately?

The Second Proof: Despair of Mercy and the Futility of Names
Second proof: despair of mercy and the irrelevance of names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's second argument that major sinners are kuffar because despair of mercy is exclusive to disbelievers, and that names themselves do not affect punishment.

Core Idea
Despair reveals disbelief, but names do not ward off the Fire.

Imam Maturidi now presents a second proof from the Quran: that only disbelievers despair of God's mercy. Since major sinners do not despair (assuming they hope for mercy), the objector might say they should not be called disbelievers. Maturidi responds that names have no intrinsic benefit; what matters is the reality—if the major sinner is punished with eternal Fire, the name does not protect him.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the verse about despair and the subsequent reasoning.
2
Understand the verse about despair
Quran says: 'none despairs of the mercy of Allah except the disbelieving people.' This links despair to disbelief.
The major sinner does not necessarily despair, so an objector might argue he is not a disbeliever.
3
See the objection and response
Maturidi anticipates the objection: if no despair, then no name of kufr. He responds by noting that names are irrelevant to punishment; only realities matter.
He uses the example: if he is punished with eternal Fire, the name whether believer or disbeliever does not benefit him.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Therefore, refusing to call the major sinner a disbeliever does not protect him from the punishment of disbelief.
The focus is on the reality of punishment, not the label.

Hypocrisy and the Mu'tazila's Naming Argument
Maturidi discusses hypocrisy and presents the Mu'tazila's objection and its rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's view on how major sins are linked to hypocrisy and the Mu'tazila's argument that a major sinner cannot be called a believer.

Core Idea
Major sins can align one with the name of hypocrisy, challenging the Mu'tazila's strict naming logic.

This passage delves into the concept of hypocrisy (nifaq) and how it relates to major sins. Maturidi uses Quranic verses and a well-known hadith to show that major sinners often exhibit the traits of hypocrisy. He then presents the Mu'tazila's objection: since the major sinner is called by evil names and faith is a good name, he cannot be called a believer, a claim Maturidi critiques. This sets the stage for a deeper understanding of naming and judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the flow from discussing hypocrisy to the Mu'tazila's argument.
The passage gets cut off at the end, so the Mu'tazila's complete argument is not fully captured.
2
Identify Maturidi's evidence for hypocrisy
Notice how Maturidi cites Quranic verses and the hadith about three traits to argue that major sinners can be called hypocrites.
The hadith lists lying, breaking promises, and betrayal as signs.
3
Examine the Mu'tazila's naming argument
Look at how the Mu'tazila argue that a major sinner cannot be called a believer because he is associated with evil names and the promise (wa'd) is specific to believers.
The argument seems to rely on the exclusivity of the name 'faith'.
4
Reflect on the incomplete ending
The passage ends mid-sentence. Consider what Maturidi's full rebuttal might be based on the context.
This highlights the challenge of working with incomplete texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدخل تسمية الشرك والكفر فيما مر بيانه، ومن حقق له اسم النفاق فمخالفة ما أعطى بلسانه من الايمان وتعاهد حدوده وحفظ حدود الله ما ظهر بأفعالهم، و بذلك قال الله تعالى: وَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ المُنَافِقِينَ، وقال: الم، أَحَسِبَ النَّاسُ أَنْ يُتْرَكُوا، أخبر ببيان ما أعطته الألسن من الصدق والكذب بالمحنة. وكذا روى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: ثلاث من كن فيه فهو منافق: من إذا حدث كذب، وإذا وعد خلف، وإذا اوتمن خان. فقد ظهر له ذلك كله من مرتكبى الكبيرة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. واحتجت المعتزلة فى الاسم بما سمى صاحب الكبيرة باسماء خبيثة، والإيمان من الأسماء الطيبة لا يسمى به، مع ما جاء من الوعد باسم الإيمان، والوعد لا يحتمل الخصوص، ثم صاحب الكبيرة قد جاء فيه الوعيد، فبطل أن يكون
So the naming of polytheism and disbelief entered into what has been explained earlier. And whoever is warranted the name of hypocrisy—due to contradicting what he gave with his tongue of faith and the observance of its limits and the preservation of the limits of Allah in what appears from their actions—and with that Allah the Exalted said: 'And Allah will surely know those who believe and will surely know the hypocrites,' and He said: 'Alif Lam Meem. Do the people think that they will be left [unaccounted]?', informing of the clarification of what the tongues give of truth and falsehood through trial. Likewise it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Three qualities, whoever has them is a hypocrite: one who lies when he speaks, breaks his promise when he vows, and betrays when he is entrusted.' So all of that has become evident from the committers of major sins. And there is no power except with Allah. And the Mu'tazila argued concerning naming that the committer of a major sin is called with evil names, and faith is among the good names and is not called with it, along with what has come of the promise in the name of faith, and the promise does not admit specification; then the committer of a major sin has the threat in him, so it is invalid that he be...
Source pages p. 930

Commentary
This passage first ties the naming of shirk and kufr to the earlier discussion, then introduces the concept of hypocrisy (nifaq). A person incurs the name of hypocrite when his outward faith contradicts his inner state, as shown in Quranic verses about testing and the hadith listing three traits of hypocrisy. Maturidi notes these traits are found in major sinners, implying they share the name of hypocrite. Then he presents the Mu'tazila's objection: they argue that since the major sinner is described by evil names (like fasiq), and faith is a good name, he cannot be called a believer; moreover, the promise (wa'd) of reward is given to believers specifically and is not general, and the threat (wa'id) applies to the major sinner, so it is invalid that he be called a believer. This argument, though cut off, is the Mu'tazila's justification for denying the name kufr and maintaining the major sinner in a middle category.

منافق
وعد
وعيد
احتجاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila's naming argument is logically sound because it follows strict naming rules.
Correction: Maturidi implies that the Mu'tazila's argument is flawed because it misunderstands the relationship between names and realities; names are not exclusive but can overlap, and the hadith shows major sinners exhibit hypocrisy.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi mention the hadith about the three traits of hypocrisy?
A) To prove that major sinners are not hypocrites.
B) To show that major sinners exhibit hypocritical traits, thus the name of hypocrisy may apply to them.
C) To refute the Mu'tazila's argument about naming.
D) To define the conditions of true faith.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses Quran and hadith to link major sins to hypocrisy, then presents the Mu'tazila's incomplete argument that a major sinner cannot be called a believer due to naming exclusivity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you commit a major sin, do you assume your faith remains intact? The Mu'tazila denied you the name of believer. Does your conscience bear witness to your faith or to your hypocrisy?
?
If Allah were to test you today as He tested the hypocrites in the Quran, would your actions confirm your words or contradict them? What is one habit you can change to align your deeds with your confession of faith?

The Definition and Scope of al-Wa'id
Maturidi defines wa'id and its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of wa'id and how the majority of scholars define its scope.

Core Idea
The divine threat applies only to sins that remove one from faith, not to all sins.

Imam Maturidi begins by clarifying a key theological term: al-wa'id (the divine threat). He explains that it is not used to call a believer a disbeliever, but is reserved for sins that negate faith. This sets the stage for a debate about who the threat applies to.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the technical terms used.
The passage contains a definition and two matters related to wa'id.
2
Identify the definition of wa'id
Find where Maturidi states what wa'id applies to. It is not for naming a believer a disbeliever, but for specific sins (fisq, fujur, zulm).
3
Understand the two aspects of threat
Maturidi mentions two matters: the generality of reports and the verse (4:31). Reflect on how these relate to the scope of wa'id.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما كان الوعيد مؤمنا ولم يسم به كافرا بما لم يرد به التسمية، فسمى به الذي أجمع أنه له اسم وهو الفسق والفجور والظلم. ثم لهم في الوعيد أمران: عموم أخباره، والثاني قوله: إِن تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ، بين ما لا يغفر ويغفر، مع بالتخليد أعظم في المنع وأبلغ في الزجر فهو أحق، على أن الوعيد إذا وجب لزم دخول النار، ولم يذكر فيهم الخروج، ولا قوة إلا بالله.

قال الفقيه أبو منصور رحمه الله: نقول وبالله نستعين: أجمع [شو لا؟] على أن الوعيد بما لم يشرك فيه المؤمنين، بل هو في كل ذنب أخرج صاحبه عن الإيمان وأسقط عنه اسمه. والمرجئة توافقهم أن كل ذنب يخرج صاحبه عن [الإيمان؟] فالوعيد [له؟] لازم. ثم إن المرجئة تخاف على المؤمنين فيما ارتكبوا من المآثم مع قيام الإيمان بالعقوبة، وأولئك لا يخافون عليهم، وكان احتجاجهم بعموم الآثار، فثبت بالذي ذكرت من قول الجملة أن المرجئة، وهي التي أرجأت، أشد استعمالا لها على العموم من الذين ادعوا عمومها؛ إذ الذنوب جعلوا الوعيد في أحد فريقى البشر، وهم الذين ليسوا بمؤمنين، ولا قوة إلا بالله.

ثم قد ثبت بأدلة القرآن وما عليه أهل الإيمان والذي جرى به أن الإيمان هو التصديق، به نؤمن، وبذلك جرت أحكام القرآن في الحلال والحرام، وما به قيام العبارات والاشتراك في الجماعات، والاجتماع في مجالس الذكر والخيرات، على غير تناكر منهم، وفيهم القبول بحق المؤمنين، وكذا جميع ما جرى به الخطاب. لم يوجد معتزلي ولا خارجي ولا حشوي مع ما فيهم أنواع المعاصي والسيئات التي بان لهم أنها كبائر أو لم يبن لهم حقيقتها بخبر في أمر الخطاب أن أحد [له؟] لما فيه، فثبت أن الإيمان لم يزل عنه، وأن الاسم قائم له، التي من دفعها يعلم أنه مكابر معاند – ما قالت الخوارج والمعتزلة فيبطل بهذه الجملة يكون غير [؟] ولا قوة إلا بالله.
What was the threat (al-wa'id) [for] a believer, and he was not named by it a disbeliever by that which the naming was not intended, so he named it with that which it is agreed that it has a name, and it is wrongdoing (al-fisq) and immorality (al-fujur) and injustice (al-zulm). Then they have concerning the threat two matters: the generality of its reports, and the second is His saying: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden' (4:31), distinguishing between what is not forgiven and what is forgiven, with [mention of] eternity (al-takhled) being greater in prevention and more effective in deterrence, so it is more deserving, [proceeding] on that the threat, if it is necessitated, necessitates entering the Fire, and exiting is not mentioned concerning them, and there is no power except with Allah.

The jurist Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We say, and with Allah we seek help: The [scholars?] have agreed that the threat, by that in which believers are not included, rather it is in every sin that removes its doer from faith (al-iman) and cancels his name. And the Murji'ah agree with them that every sin removes its doer from [faith?], so the threat is necessary for him. Then indeed the Murji'ah fear for the believers regarding what they have committed of sins (al-ma'athim) with the abiding of faith, regarding the punishment, and those [others] do not fear for them, and their argument was by the generality of the reports. So it is established by what I mentioned of the statement of the majority (al-jumla) that the Murji'ah, who postponed [judgment], are stronger in applying it generally than those who claimed its generality; for [regarding] sins, they made the threat [apply to] one of the two groups of mankind, and they are those who are not believers, and there is no power except with Allah.

Then it has been established by the proofs of the Qur'an and what the people of faith are upon, and what has proceeded, that faith is affirmation (al-tasdiq), by it we believe, and by that the rulings of the Qur'an proceed in the lawful and the unlawful, and what establishes expressions and participation in congregations, and gathering in assemblies of remembrance and good deeds, without denial among them, and among them is acceptance of the right of the believers, and likewise all that the address (al-khitab) has proceeded upon. There is no Mu'tazili nor Khariji nor Hashwi, despite what is in them of types of disobedience and evil deeds which are clear to them that they are major sins or whose reality has not become clear to them by a report, in the matter of the address that anyone [has?] for what is in it, so it is established that faith has not ceased from him, and that the name is established for him, which whoever rejects knows that he is a stubborn opponent – what the Khawarij and Mu'tazila said, so it is invalidated by this statement, it becomes other [?], and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 931

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument by Imam Maturidi. It begins by defining the concept of al-wa'id (divine threat) and clarifying that it applies to sins which remove one from faith, not to every sin. The author then mentions that the scholars (jama'a) agree that the threat is for every sin that removes its doer from iman and cancels the name of believer. The Murji'ah agree in principle but differ in that they still fear punishment for believers who commit sins, while the Khawarij and Mu'tazila do not fear because they consider such sinners to have left iman. Maturidi then establishes that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) based on Qur'anic proofs and the practice of the community. He argues that no sect (Mu'tazili, Khariji, Hashwi) denies that the name 'believer' remains for one who commits sins, implying that their own positions contradict this. The conclusion is that iman does not cease and the name remains, refuting the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Key Terms
الوعيد
الفسق
الفجور
الظلم
التخليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think wa'id applies to all sins equally.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that wa'id applies only to sins that remove one from faith, i.e., major sins that cancel iman.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, to what does the term 'wa'id' apply?
A) All sins without exception.
B) Only sins that remove one from faith and cancel the name of believer.
C) Only sins of disbelievers.
D) Only major sins, but the name of believer remains.

Key Takeaway
Wa'id is specifically for sins that negate faith, not for every sin of a believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you take the threat of eternal punishment for certain sins seriously enough to avoid them, or do you downplay them? What is one specific sin you commit that you consider 'major' – and what will you do today to turn away from it?
?
The passage warns against labeling a believer a disbeliever. Think of someone you disagree with religiously: do you ever mentally 'excommunicate' them? How can you uphold the truth without falling into the error of false takfir?
?
If you truly believed that some sins lead to eternal punishment with no exit, how would your daily choices change? What is one habit you need to break to avoid such a fate, starting now?
