Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
The Position of the Murji'ah and the Proof of Iman as Tasdiq
Maturidi discusses Murji'ah view and proves iman is tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Murji'ah position on wa'id and how Maturidi proves that iman is tasdiq, refuting the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The Murji'ah agree on wa'id for sins removing faith but still fear punishment for believers, while Maturidi affirms that iman remains despite sins.

Having defined wa'id, Maturidi now turns to the positions of different groups. He notes that the jama'a agrees wa'id is for sins that remove faith, and the Murji'ah concur. However, the Murji'ah differ in that they still fear punishment for believers who sin, whereas the Khawarij and Mu'tazila do not. Maturidi then establishes that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) and that the name 'believer' remains even when sins are committed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the different groups mentioned: jama'a, Murji'ah, Khawarij, Mu'tazila, and Hashwi.
Some phrases are unclear in the original, but the overall argument is discernible.
2
Compare the Murji'ah and Khawarij/Mu'tazila views
Notice that the Murji'ah agree on the principle of wa'id for sins removing faith, but they still fear punishment for believers. The Khawarij and Mu'tazila do not fear because they consider such sinners to have lost iman.
Maturidi argues that the Murji'ah are actually stronger in applying wa'id generally.
3
Understand Maturidi's proof that iman is tasdiq
Maturidi asserts that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) based on Qur'anic proofs and communal practice. This definition allows that iman remains with a believer even when sins are committed.
4
See how this refutes the Khawarij and Mu'tazila
Maturidi argues that no sect denies the name 'believer' remains for one who sins, contradicting their own positions. Therefore, iman does not cease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما كان الوعيد مؤمنا ولم يسم به كافرا بما لم يرد به التسمية، فسمى به الذي أجمع أنه له اسم وهو الفسق والفجور والظلم. ثم لهم في الوعيد أمران: عموم أخباره، والثاني قوله: إِن تَجْتَنِبُوا كَبَائِرَ مَا تُنْهَوْنَ عَنْهُ، بين ما لا يغفر ويغفر، مع بالتخليد أعظم في المنع وأبلغ في الزجر فهو أحق، على أن الوعيد إذا وجب لزم دخول النار، ولم يذكر فيهم الخروج، ولا قوة إلا بالله.

قال الفقيه أبو منصور رحمه الله: نقول وبالله نستعين: أجمع [شو لا؟] على أن الوعيد بما لم يشرك فيه المؤمنين، بل هو في كل ذنب أخرج صاحبه عن الإيمان وأسقط عنه اسمه. والمرجئة توافقهم أن كل ذنب يخرج صاحبه عن [الإيمان؟] فالوعيد [له؟] لازم. ثم إن المرجئة تخاف على المؤمنين فيما ارتكبوا من المآثم مع قيام الإيمان بالعقوبة، وأولئك لا يخافون عليهم، وكان احتجاجهم بعموم الآثار، فثبت بالذي ذكرت من قول الجملة أن المرجئة، وهي التي أرجأت، أشد استعمالا لها على العموم من الذين ادعوا عمومها؛ إذ الذنوب جعلوا الوعيد في أحد فريقى البشر، وهم الذين ليسوا بمؤمنين، ولا قوة إلا بالله.

ثم قد ثبت بأدلة القرآن وما عليه أهل الإيمان والذي جرى به أن الإيمان هو التصديق، به نؤمن، وبذلك جرت أحكام القرآن في الحلال والحرام، وما به قيام العبارات والاشتراك في الجماعات، والاجتماع في مجالس الذكر والخيرات، على غير تناكر منهم، وفيهم القبول بحق المؤمنين، وكذا جميع ما جرى به الخطاب. لم يوجد معتزلي ولا خارجي ولا حشوي مع ما فيهم أنواع المعاصي والسيئات التي بان لهم أنها كبائر أو لم يبن لهم حقيقتها بخبر في أمر الخطاب أن أحد [له؟] لما فيه، فثبت أن الإيمان لم يزل عنه، وأن الاسم قائم له، التي من دفعها يعلم أنه مكابر معاند – ما قالت الخوارج والمعتزلة فيبطل بهذه الجملة يكون غير [؟] ولا قوة إلا بالله.

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument by Imam Maturidi. It begins by defining the concept of al-wa'id (divine threat) and clarifying that it applies to sins which remove one from faith, not to every sin. The author then mentions that the scholars (jama'a) agree that the threat is for every sin that removes its doer from iman and cancels the name of believer. The Murji'ah agree in principle but differ in that they still fear punishment for believers who commit sins, while the Khawarij and Mu'tazila do not fear because they consider such sinners to have left iman. Maturidi then establishes that iman is tasdiq (affirmation) based on Qur'anic proofs and the practice of the community. He argues that no sect (Mu'tazili, Khariji, Hashwi) denies that the name 'believer' remains for one who commits sins, implying that their own positions contradict this. The conclusion is that iman does not cease and the name remains, refuting the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Murji'ah and the jama'a hold identical views on wa'id.
Correction: Maturidi shows they agree on principle but differ: Murji'ah still fear punishment for believers, while jama'a (Sunnis) do not necessarily fear eternal punishment.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi prove that iman is tasdiq?
A) By citing a single verse from the Qur'an.
B) By relying on the consensus of the Murji'ah.
C) By appealing to proofs from the Qur'an and the practice of the community.
D) By arguing from the position of the Khawarij.

Key Takeaway
Iman is affirmation, and it remains with a believer even when sins are committed, contrary to the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into sin, do you ever doubt whether you are still a true believer? How does Maturidi's insistence that iman is tasdiq and remains despite sins challenge you to hold onto the name 'believer' even in your weakest moments? What will you do the next time you sin to remind yourself that your faith is not lost?
?
The Murji'ah feared punishment for believers who sin, even while affirming their faith. Do you truly fear the consequences of your sins, or have you become complacent, thinking that deeds don't matter? Examine your heart: are you more afraid of Allah's punishment or of losing your reputation? What change in your daily life would show that you take both iman and sin seriously?
?
Maturidi points out that even the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, who claim sinners lose faith, still call sinning Muslims 'believers' in practice. Are you consistent? Do you treat fellow Muslims who commit major sins as brothers and sisters in faith, or do you mentally exclude them? Which Muslim do you need to reconcile with or show mercy to, starting today?
